قذف [۱۷۳۰ (۵) فان تزوج مسلم ذمية بشهادة ذميَّين جاز عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وابي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى وقال محمد رحمه الله لايجوز الا ان يشهد شاهدين گواہوں کی موجودگی میں بھی نکاح ہو جائے گا۔
آیت میں ہے کہ محدود فی القذف والوں کی گواہی قبول نہ کرو۔ آیت یہ ہے و الذين يـرمـون الـمـحـصـنـت ثم لم يأتو باربعة شهداء فاجلدوهم ثمانين جلدة ولا تقبلوا لهم شهادة ابدا واولئك هم الفاسقون (الف) (آیت ۴ سورۃ النور ۲۴) لیکن ہم کہتے ہیں کہ محدود فی القذف والوں کی گواہی قاضی قبول نہ کرے لیکن وہ گواہ بن سکتا ہے۔ اور تقریبا ہمیشہ ایسا ہوتا ہے کہ نکاح کے گواہ کو قاضی کے سامنے گواہی دینے کی ضرورت نہیں پڑتی کہ اس کی گواہی قبول کرنے کی ضرورت پڑے (۲) نکاح کے گواہ بننے میں تھوڑی آسانی ہے کیونکہ وہ روز مرہ کا کام ہے۔ نا اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک نکاح میں بھی فاسق اور محدود فی القذف کی گواہی قابل قبول نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ ان کی دلیل اوپر کی حدیث ہے اور آیت ہے جن میں ان لوگوں کی گواہی قبول کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ (۱۷۳۰ (۵) پس اگر مسلمان نے زمیہ عورت سے شادی کی دو ذمیوں کی گواہی سے تو امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ نہیں جائز ہے مگر دو مسلمانوں کی گواہی سے۔
ر اس عبارت میں زمیہ سے مراد نصرانیہ اور یہودیہ عورت ہے۔ تو مطلب یہ ہوا کہ مسلمان نے یہودیہ یا نصرانیہ سے شادی کی دو یہودی یا دو نصرانی کی گواہی سے تو شیخین کے نزدیک نکاح ہو جائے گا۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ذمی مسلمان کے نقصان کے لئے گواہی دینا چاہے تو قابل قبول نہیں ہے۔ آیت میں ہے ولـن يـجـعـل الـلـــه للكافرين على المؤمنين سبيلا (ب) ( آیت ۱۴۱ سورۃ النساء ۴) اس آیت میں ہے کہ کا فرکو مسلمانوں پر کوئی راستہ نہیں جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ نقصان دینے کے لئے گواہی دے تو قابل قبول نہیں۔ لیکن مسلمان کے فائدے کے لئے گواہی دے تو مقبول ہے۔ اور اس مسئلے میں یہودی یا نصرانیہ عورت کا جسم مسلمان کے قبضے میں آرہا ہے جو مسلمان کے فائدے کی چیز ہے اس لئے یہ گواہی مقبول ہوگی (۲) گویا کہ ذمی نے زمیہ کے لئے گواہی دی۔ اور ذمی ذمی کے خلاف گواہی دے تو یہ مقبول ہے۔ اس لئے زمیہ کے نکاح میں روز می گواہ بن جائیں تو نکاح صحیح ہو جائے گا (۳) حدیث میں ہے عن جابر بن عبد الله ان رسول الله له اجاز شهادة اهل الكتاب بعضهم على بعض ( ج ) ( ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب شهادة اهل الكتاب بعضهم على بعض ص ۳۴۰ نمبر ۲۳۷۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اہل کتاب بعض بعض کے خلاف گواہی دے سکتا ہے۔ اور اس صورت میں زمیہ کے خلاف گواہی دینا ہوا اس لئے گواہ بننا جائز ہوگا۔
صلى الله
فائدہ امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ زمیہ کی شادی بھی دو مسلمان گواہوں کے علاوہ سے نہیں ہوگی۔
Qadhf [1730] (5) If a Muslim marries a dhimmi woman with the testimony of two dhimmi witnesses, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but Muhammad said it is not permissible unless two witnesses [are Muslim] – even in the presence of witnesses, the marriage will take place. The verse says: 'Those who accuse chaste women and then do not produce four witnesses, flog them with eighty stripes, and do not ever accept their testimony, and they are the sinful ones' (Surah al-Nur 24:4). But we say that the qadi should not accept the testimony of those punished for qadhf, but such a person can be a witness [for marriage]. It almost never happens that a marriage witness needs to testify before a judge, so there is no need to accept his testimony. Marriage witnessing is simpler because it is a daily affair. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i, the testimony of a fasiq and one punished for qadhf is not acceptable even in marriage. Their proof is the above hadith and verse. (1730) (5) So if a Muslim marries a dhimmi woman with the testimony of two dhimmi witnesses, it is permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad said it is not permissible except with the testimony of two Muslims. In this phrase, dhimmi woman means a Christian or Jewish woman. The meaning is that if a Muslim marries a Jewish or Christian woman with the testimony of two Jews or two Christians, then according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) the marriage will be valid. The reason is that if a dhimmi wants to testify against a Muslim to his detriment, it is not acceptable. The verse says: 'And Allah will never give the disbelievers a way over the believers' (Surah al-Nisa 4:141). This verse means that if they testify to cause harm, it is not accepted. But if they testify for the benefit of a Muslim, it is accepted. In this case, the body of the Jewish or Christian woman comes into the possession of the Muslim, which is a benefit for the Muslim, so this testimony is accepted. So it is as if the dhimmi testified for the dhimmi woman. And a dhimmi's testimony against another dhimmi is acceptable. Therefore, if dhimmis become witnesses in the marriage of a dhimmi woman, the marriage will be valid. Also narration: from Jabir ibn 'Abdullah that the Messenger of Allah permitted the testimony of the People of the Book against one another. From this hadith it is known that the People of the Book can testify against one another. In this scenario, they are testifying against the dhimmi woman, so becoming witnesses is permissible. Benefit: Imam Muhammad says that the marriage of a dhimmi woman will not be valid except with two Muslim witnesses.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a Muslim man's marriage to a dhimmi woman (Christian or Jewish) when the witnesses are also dhimmis. The text is a continuation of the discussion on qadhif witnesses but introduces a new numbered point (5). The ruling: According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs), such a marriage is valid with dhimmi witnesses. Imam Muhammad disagrees, insisting that Muslim witnesses are required for the validity of any marriage involving a Muslim. The proof offered by the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is based on the Quranic verse (4:141) which states that Allah will not give disbelievers a way over believers. They interpret this to mean that testimony harmful to Muslims is invalid, but testimony beneficial to Muslims is valid. In this case, the dhimmi woman's marriage to a Muslim benefits the Muslim, so dhimmi witnesses are testifying to a benefit, not harm. Furthermore, the hadith of Jabir ibn 'Abdullah permits the testimony of ahl al-kitab (People of the Book) against one another, and here the witnesses are testifying against the dhimmi woman (since they are witnesses for her marriage, but their testimony is considered against her in a sense). Therefore, their testimony is acceptable. The text also includes a 'fa'idah' (benefit) reiterating Imam Muhammad's stricter position. This dispute has practical implications: in the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it is easy for a Muslim to marry a dhimmi woman even in a community where only dhimmi witnesses are available; but according to Imam Muhammad, Muslim witnesses must be found or the marriage is invalid.

Key Terms
ذمی (dhimmī): A non-Muslim subject living under the protection (dhimma) of the Islamic state, here specifically a Christian or a Jew.
ذمیہ (dhammiyya): A dhimmi woman, specifically a Christian or Jewish woman.
شہادت (shahādat): Testimony; here it refers to serving as a witness to the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is the ruling if a Muslim marries a Jewish woman with two Jewish witnesses?
A) The marriage is invalid because the witnesses must be Muslim
B) The marriage is valid because the testimony benefits the Muslim and is not harmful
C) The marriage is valid only if the witnesses are 'adil
D) The marriage is invalid unless there are also Muslim witnesses

Key Takeaway
The majority Hanafi view allows dhimmi witnesses for a Muslim's marriage to a dhimmi woman, based on Quran 4:141 and the hadith of Jabir.

Nikah — Marriage

Testimony of Slanderers in Marriage
Hanafi vs Shafi'i on slanderer witnesses in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the testimony of a slanderer in marriage, explain the dalil (Quran 24:4) and the limitation to judicial acceptance, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A slanderer can witness marriage because the Quran bans judicial acceptance, not witnessing itself.

The Quran (24:4) commands never to accept the testimony of those flogged for false accusation of adultery. Does this prohibit their witnessing a marriage contract? The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools diverge. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi distinction between capacity to witness and judicial acceptance, and why marriage witnesses are treated differently.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds: a person lashed for slander (mahdud fil-qadhf) can be a witness in marriage, but his testimony cannot be accepted in court.
This is based on a contextual reading of the verse.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the prohibition is absolute, covering all contexts including marriage.
Their evidence is the same verse and a hadith.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: the verse addresses judges ('do not accept'), not the act of witnessing. Marriage witnesses rarely need to testify in court.
The practical need for ease in marriage contracts supports this view.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi law, a marriage witnessed by a slanderer is valid; under Shafi'i, it is invalid.
This difference affects the validity of the marriage contract.

The commentary al-Thamiri, part three. Λ. The Book of Marriage. Slander [1730 (5)]: If a Muslim marries a dhimmi woman with the testimony of two dhimmis, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said it is not permissible unless two [Muslim] witnesses testify. Even with the presence of two witnesses, the marriage will occur. The verse says: Do not accept the testimony of those who have been lashed for slander. The verse is: 'And those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses, flog them with eighty lashes and never accept their testimony, and those are the disobedient.' (Surah al-Nur 24:4, part a). But we say: The judge does not accept their testimony, but they can serve as witnesses. And almost always, the witnesses in marriage do not need to testify before a judge, so there is no need to accept their testimony. (2) There is some ease in being a witness for marriage because it is an everyday matter. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i, even in marriage, the testimony of a sinner or one lashed for slander is not acceptable. Their evidence is the above hadith and verse which forbid accepting their testimony. (1730 (5)) So if a Muslim marries a dhimmi woman with the testimony of two dhimmis, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf it is permissible. And Muhammad said it is not permissible except with the testimony of two Muslims. In this phrase, dhimmi woman means Christian or Jewish woman. So the meaning is: if a Muslim marries a Jewish or Christian woman with the testimony of two Jews or two Christians, according to the two shaykhs the marriage is valid. The reason is that a dhimmi's testimony is not acceptable if it is detrimental to a Muslim. The verse says: 'And Allah will never give the disbelievers a way over the believers' (Surah al-Nisa 4:141, part b). This verse means that testimony given for harm is not acceptable. But testimony given for the benefit of a Muslim is acceptable. And in this case, the body of the Jewish or Christian woman comes into the possession of the Muslim, which is to his benefit, so this testimony is acceptable. (2) It is as if the dhimmi testified for the dhimmi woman. And the testimony of a dhimmi against another dhimmi is acceptable. So if they become witnesses in the marriage of a dhimmi woman, the marriage will be valid. (3) The hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah that the Messenger of Allah permitted the testimony of the People of the Book against each other (Ibn Majah, chapter on testimony of People of the Book against each other, p. 340, no. 2374, part c). From this hadith it is known that the People of the Book can testify against each other. And in this case, testifying against the dhimmi woman occurs, so becoming a witness is permissible. Benefit: Imam Muhammad says that even the marriage of a dhimmi woman is not valid without two Muslim witnesses. Footnote (a): Those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses, flog them with eighty lashes and never accept their testimony, and they are the disobedient. (b) Allah has not given the disbelievers any way over the believers. (c) He permitted the testimony of the People of the Book against each other.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage begins by addressing a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the use of non-Muslim witnesses in a Muslim's marriage to a dhimmi woman. It also compares the Hanafi position with that of Imam al-Shafi'i on the testimony of those who have been punished for slander (qadhf). The author first mentions the Quranic verse (24:4) that commands never to accept the testimony of those who have been lashed for false accusation of adultery. The Hanafi position distinguishes between the judge's acceptance of testimony (which is prohibited) and the act of being a witness (which is allowed), especially in marriage where witnesses rarely need to testify in court. Then the main issue is presented: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit the marriage of a Muslim to a dhimmi woman with the testimony of two dhimmis, while Imam Muhammad requires two Muslim witnesses. The commentary explains the evidence: the verse 'Allah will never give the disbelievers a way over the believers' indicates that dhimmi testimony is acceptable if it benefits Muslims. Here, the dhimmi woman's body comes into the Muslim's possession, which is a benefit. Additionally, a hadith from Ibn Majah allows the testimony of People of the Book against each other, and here the dhimmi witnesses are testifying for the dhimmi woman (as if against her? Actually, it is for her, but the point is that their testimony is accepted among themselves). The passage concludes with Imam Muhammad's stricter view. The footnotes provide translations of the Quranic verses and Hadith.

Key Terms
محدود في القذف (mahdud fil-qadhf): A person who has been flogged for falsely accusing someone of adultery (qadhf).
قذف (qadhf): The crime of falsely accusing a chaste person of adultery.
شهادة (shahadah): Testimony or witness. In this context, the act of being a witness to the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why can a person who has been flogged for slander (mahdud fil-qadhf) serve as a witness in marriage?
A) Because the Quranic verse is abrogated
B) Because marriage witnesses rarely need to testify before a judge
C) Because the person has repented
D) Because marriage is a private contract

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a slanderer to witness marriage by limiting the Quranic ban to judicial acceptance, ensuring practical ease in marriage contracts.

Testimony of Dhimmis in a Muslim's Marriage to a Dhimmi Woman
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dhimmi witnesses in nikah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dhimmi witnesses in a Muslim's marriage to a dhimmi woman, explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between the two shaykhs and Imam Muhammad, and apply the evidence from Quran 4:141 and the hadith of Jabir.

Core Idea
Two dhimmi witnesses suffice for a Muslim marrying a dhimmi woman because their testimony benefits the Muslim.

When a Muslim man marries a Jewish or Christian woman (dhimmi), can the witnesses be dhimmis themselves? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit it, while Imam Muhammad requires Muslim witnesses. In this lesson, we examine the evidence—Quran 4:141 and a hadith about People of the Book testifying against each other—and see how the majority view is supported.

Guided Path
1
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They hold that a Muslim may marry a dhimmi woman with the testimony of two dhimmi witnesses. The marriage is valid.
This is the majority position.
2
State the position of Imam Muhammad
Muhammad holds that two Muslim witnesses are required; otherwise the marriage is not valid.
This is a minority intra-Hanafi view.
3
Analyze the evidence for the majority
Quran 4:141 ('Allah will never give the disbelievers a way over the believers') is interpreted to mean that dhimmi testimony is accepted if it benefits a Muslim, as here the woman comes into the Muslim's possession. Also, a hadith allows People of the Book to testify against each other, and here the witnesses are testifying for the dhimmi woman (which is akin to testifying against her? Actually, they are testifying for her but the hadith is cited to show their testimony is accepted among themselves).
The Hanafi reasoning: the testimony benefits the Muslim husband.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The text leans toward the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The practical consequence: a Muslim can marry a dhimmi woman with dhimmi witnesses, and the marriage is valid.
Imam Muhammad's view would render such a marriage invalid unless Muslim witnesses are present.

The commentary al-Thamiri, part three. Λ. The Book of Marriage. Slander [1730 (5)]: If a Muslim marries a dhimmi woman with the testimony of two dhimmis, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said it is not permissible unless two [Muslim] witnesses testify. Even with the presence of two witnesses, the marriage will occur. The verse says: Do not accept the testimony of those who have been lashed for slander. The verse is: 'And those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses, flog them with eighty lashes and never accept their testimony, and those are the disobedient.' (Surah al-Nur 24:4, part a). But we say: The judge does not accept their testimony, but they can serve as witnesses. And almost always, the witnesses in marriage do not need to testify before a judge, so there is no need to accept their testimony. (2) There is some ease in being a witness for marriage because it is an everyday matter. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i, even in marriage, the testimony of a sinner or one lashed for slander is not acceptable. Their evidence is the above hadith and verse which forbid accepting their testimony. (1730 (5)) So if a Muslim marries a dhimmi woman with the testimony of two dhimmis, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf it is permissible. And Muhammad said it is not permissible except with the testimony of two Muslims. In this phrase, dhimmi woman means Christian or Jewish woman. So the meaning is: if a Muslim marries a Jewish or Christian woman with the testimony of two Jews or two Christians, according to the two shaykhs the marriage is valid. The reason is that a dhimmi's testimony is not acceptable if it is detrimental to a Muslim. The verse says: 'And Allah will never give the disbelievers a way over the believers' (Surah al-Nisa 4:141, part b). This verse means that testimony given for harm is not acceptable. But testimony given for the benefit of a Muslim is acceptable. And in this case, the body of the Jewish or Christian woman comes into the possession of the Muslim, which is to his benefit, so this testimony is acceptable. (2) It is as if the dhimmi testified for the dhimmi woman. And the testimony of a dhimmi against another dhimmi is acceptable. So if they become witnesses in the marriage of a dhimmi woman, the marriage will be valid. (3) The hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah that the Messenger of Allah permitted the testimony of the People of the Book against each other (Ibn Majah, chapter on testimony of People of the Book against each other, p. 340, no. 2374, part c). From this hadith it is known that the People of the Book can testify against each other. And in this case, testifying against the dhimmi woman occurs, so becoming a witness is permissible. Benefit: Imam Muhammad says that even the marriage of a dhimmi woman is not valid without two Muslim witnesses. Footnote (a): Those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses, flog them with eighty lashes and never accept their testimony, and they are the disobedient. (b) Allah has not given the disbelievers any way over the believers. (c) He permitted the testimony of the People of the Book against each other.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage begins by addressing a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the use of non-Muslim witnesses in a Muslim's marriage to a dhimmi woman. It also compares the Hanafi position with that of Imam al-Shafi'i on the testimony of those who have been punished for slander (qadhf). The author first mentions the Quranic verse (24:4) that commands never to accept the testimony of those who have been lashed for false accusation of adultery. The Hanafi position distinguishes between the judge's acceptance of testimony (which is prohibited) and the act of being a witness (which is allowed), especially in marriage where witnesses rarely need to testify in court. Then the main issue is presented: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit the marriage of a Muslim to a dhimmi woman with the testimony of two dhimmis, while Imam Muhammad requires two Muslim witnesses. The commentary explains the evidence: the verse 'Allah will never give the disbelievers a way over the believers' indicates that dhimmi testimony is acceptable if it benefits Muslims. Here, the dhimmi woman's body comes into the Muslim's possession, which is a benefit. Additionally, a hadith from Ibn Majah allows the testimony of People of the Book against each other, and here the dhimmi witnesses are testifying for the dhimmi woman (as if against her? Actually, it is for her, but the point is that their testimony is accepted among themselves). The passage concludes with Imam Muhammad's stricter view. The footnotes provide translations of the Quranic verses and Hadith.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim citizen of the Islamic state, specifically here Jewish or Christian women.
شهادة (shahadah): Testimony or witness. In this context, the act of being a witness to the marriage contract.
ذمية (dhimmiyyah): A dhimmi woman, specifically Jewish or Christian.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is the ruling on a Muslim marrying a dhimmi woman with two dhimmi witnesses?
A) Not permissible, witnesses must be Muslim.
B) Permissible, but only if the witnesses are also relatives.
C) Permissible, and the marriage is valid.
D) Permissible, but the marriage requires confirmation by a judge.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority permits dhimmi witnesses in a Muslim's marriage to a dhimmi woman, relying on the benefit to the Muslim and the principle that dhimmi testimony is accepted when it does not harm Muslims.

The Permanently Prohibited Female Relatives (Mahramat) in Marriage
List of female relatives permanently prohibited in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven categories of female relatives permanently forbidden in the Hanafi school and identify the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Marriage to blood relatives in the direct line and first collateral line is permanently forbidden by clear Quranic text.

This lesson introduces the first category of mahramat: female relatives who are permanently forbidden for marriage due to blood ties. The Hanafi school, like all schools, bases this on the explicit text of the Quran. Understanding these categories is fundamental to knowing the limits of permissible marriage. We will examine the list from the commentary and see how it expands to include grandmothers and granddaughters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
First, recognize that the passage states a prohibition: it is not lawful (la yahillu) for a man to marry these women. This is a clear hukm of haram.
The word 'haram' is used in the commentary.
2
List the explicit categories
The text lists: mother, grandmothers (both sides), daughter, granddaughter (son's daughter down), sister, sister's daughters (nieces), paternal aunt, maternal aunt. Write them down.
The verse also includes brother's daughters, but the initial list may not mention them. Check the commentary.
3
Note the expansions (inclusions)
The commentary expands 'mother' to include paternal and maternal grandmothers, and 'daughter' to include all female descendants through sons (granddaughters). Understand why: these are included by implication.
The Quranic term 'ummahat' (mothers) linguistically includes grandmothers.
4
Locate the Quranic proof
The verse cited is Surah al-Nisa 4:23. Find its exact wording. The commentary provides the relevant portion.
The verse begins 'Hurrimat 'alaykum' (Forbidden to you).
5
Analyze the proof (wajh al-dalalah)
The word 'hurrimat' is a passive verb indicating a divine prohibition. The listing of each category directly forbids marriage to them. The Hanafi principle is that the text is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah, so the ruling is definitive.
No istihsan overrides this clear text.

The commentary al-Thamiri, part three, page 9, Book of Marriage. Muslims [131 (6)]: It is not lawful for a man to marry his mother, nor his grandmothers from the male and female sides, nor his daughter, nor his son's daughter even if they go down [in lineage], nor his sister, nor his sister's daughters, nor his paternal aunt, nor his maternal aunt. Explanation of forbidden women: [1731] (6): It is not permissible for a man to marry his mother, nor his paternal grandmother, nor his maternal grandmother. Marriage to one's mother, grandmother, and maternal grandmother is forbidden. The verse says: 'Forbidden to you are your mothers, your daughters, your sisters, your paternal aunts, your maternal aunts, and the daughters of your brother and the daughters of your sister.' (Surah al-Nisa 4:23, part b). This verse mentions fourteen types of women marriage to whom is forbidden. Among them is the mother, and under mother, paternal and maternal grandmothers are included, so marriage to them is also forbidden. [1732] (7): And it is not lawful for a man to marry his daughter, nor his granddaughter, even if she is far down. Marriage to one's daughter and similarly one's granddaughter is forbidden. The above verse explicitly states that marrying one's daughter is forbidden, and within daughter are included granddaughters and great-granddaughters, regardless of how far down. [1733] (8): And it is not permissible to marry one's sister, nor one's sisters' daughters (nieces), nor one's paternal aunt, nor one's maternal aunt. Marriage to one's sister, niece, paternal aunt, and maternal aunt is forbidden. 'Sister's daughters' means nieces. The verse says 'your daughters' and then 'the daughters of your brother and the daughters of your sister,' which means nieces (both brother's daughter and sister's daughter). Footnote (a): O you who believe, the testimony among you, when death approaches one of you, at the time of bequest, should be two just witnesses from among you. (b) Forbidden to you are your mothers, your daughters, your sisters, your paternal aunts, your maternal aunts, and the daughters of your brother and the daughters of your sister.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the text of the commentary enumerating the female relatives who are permanently prohibited for marriage (mahramat). It begins with a list: mother, grandmothers (both paternal and maternal), daughter, granddaughter (downwards), sister, sister's daughter (niece), paternal aunt, and maternal aunt. The commentary explains each category, citing the Quranic verse (4:23) as the primary proof. For grandmothers, it notes that they are included under 'mother' in the verse. For granddaughters, they are included under 'daughters.' The text clarifies that sister's daughter (niece) and brother's daughter (mentioned in the verse but not explicitly listed in the initial ruling? Actually, the initial ruling says 'sister's daughters' but the verse includes both brother's daughters and sister's daughters. The commentary mentions both. The footnote gives the full verse. The passage is straightforward: it lists the prohibited women and provides the Quranic evidence.

Key Terms
محرمات (mahramat): Women who are perpetually forbidden to marry a man due to blood relation, affinity, or fosterage. Here specifically blood relatives.
جدة (jaddah): Grandmother, including paternal and maternal grandmothers, and up the line.
بنت الولد (bint al-walad): Son's daughter, i.e., granddaughter. The text specifies 'even if far down' includes all female descendants.

Permanent Prohibition by Lineage: Mothers, Grandmothers, Daughters, Granddaughters
Ruling with Quranic proof on prohibited lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permanently prohibited female relatives by lineage according to the Hanafi school and explain how the Quranic text covers grandmothers and granddaughters.

Core Idea
The Quranic prohibition of 'mothers' and 'daughters' includes all ascending and descending generations by linguistic extension.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational ruling from the matn of al-Hidayah that lists the women a man is forever forbidden to marry due to blood lineage. The prohibition is direct from the Quran and agreed upon by all schools. We will focus on how the Hanafi school reads the text to include grandmothers and granddaughters, and why this ruling is absolutely binding.

Guided Path
1
List the prohibited women
Identify from the source: mother, grandmothers (both paternal and maternal), daughter, and granddaughter (child's daughter). Note the phrase 'even if she descends' means any number of generations down.
The matn explicitly states 'his mother, his grandmothers... his daughter, the daughter of his child'.
2
Understand the linguistic extension
Recognize that the Quranic verse only says 'your mothers' and 'your daughters'. The Hanafi school uses the principle of dalalat al-nass to extend these terms to include all ancestors and descendants, because the underlying cause ('illah) is the direct lineage relation.
This is based on the understanding that the word 'mother' linguistically includes any female ancestor, and 'daughter' includes any female descendant.
3
State the evidence
Cite the Quranic verse (al-Nisa 4:23) as the primary evidence. Note that the imperative 'حرمت' indicates definitive prohibition. The proof is qat'i in both transmission and meaning.
All four schools agree on this ruling, making it from the qat'iyyat of the religion.
4
Conclude the ruling
The ruling is haram. If a marriage contract is made with any of these women, it is batil (void) and must be annulled. There is no exception or possibility of making it halal.
This prohibition is permanent; it does not change with time or circumstance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يحل للرجل ان يتزوج بامه ولا بجداته من قبل الرجال والنساء ولا ببنته ولا ببنت ولده وان سفلت قال الله تعالى حرمت عليكم امهاتكم وبناتكم واخواتكم و عماتكم و خالاتكم وبنات الاخ وبنات الاخت (النساء: 23)
And it is not permissible for a man to marry his mother, nor his grandmothers from the paternal and maternal sides, nor his daughter, nor the daughter of his child even if she descends. Allah Almighty said: 'Forbidden to you are your mothers, your daughters, your sisters, your paternal aunts, your maternal aunts, daughters of brother and daughters of sister.' (al-Nisa: 23)
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn prohibiting marriage with immediate and extended direct ancestors and descendants. The proof is the Qur'anic verse from Surah al-Nisa which explicitly lists these relatives. The Hanafi school interprets 'mothers' (ummahat) to include all grandmothers, paternal and maternal, by analogy (qiyas) because they share the same relationship of ancestry. Similarly, 'daughters' (banat) includes all granddaughters. The phrase 'even if she descends' (wa in saflat) means regardless of how many generations down. This prohibition is absolute and permanent; there is no exception for any circumstance. All schools of law (madhahib) agree on this ruling, making it from the definite matters (qat'iyyat) of the religion.

Key Terms
جدات (jaddāt): Grandmothers, both paternal and maternal, any number of generations up
سفلت (saflat): Descending generations, i.e., grandchildren and beyond

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Mother, grandmother, daughter, granddaughter
B) Mother only
C) Mother and daughter only, not grandmothers or granddaughters
D) Grandmothers only if paternal

Key Takeaway
The Quranic prohibition of marrying mothers and daughters extends to all female ancestors and descendants, making such marriages absolutely haram and void.

Prohibition of Marrying Sisters, Nieces, and Aunts
Lists prohibited women: sisters, nieces, aunts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven categories of women prohibited by blood relation according to Surah al-Nisa 4:23 and explain why the prohibition is considered qat'i (definitive).

Core Idea
Sisters, aunts, and nieces are permanently prohibited by explicit Qur'anic text — no ijtihad can permit them.

Marriage to certain blood relatives is permanently forbidden by Allah's command. This lesson continues the enumeration of prohibited women, covering sisters (full and half), nieces (daughters of brother or sister), and aunts (paternal and maternal). The prohibition is derived directly from the Qur'an and is unanimously agreed upon by all schools. Understanding these categories is essential to avoid falling into haram relationships unknowingly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Prohibited Women
Locate each category mentioned in the Arabic text: sister (اخت), sister's daughter (بنت الأخت), paternal aunt (عمة), maternal aunt (خالة). Note that 'brother's daughter' (بنت الأخ) is also prohibited, though not explicitly listed in this short passage; the commentary confirms it via the verse.
The full verse covers all seven: mother, daughter, sister, paternal aunt, maternal aunt, brother's daughter, sister's daughter.
2
Recognize the Qur'anic Proof
The author cites Surah al-Nisa 4:23, which uses the passive verb 'ḥurrimat' (forbidden), indicating an absolute, permanent prohibition. The listing is explicit and requires no interpretation for these categories.
The word 'ḥurrimat' is in the past tense, conveying a definitive legal ruling.
3
Understand the Scope and Continuity
The prohibition applies to all sisters (full and half), all aunts (paternal and maternal, including great-aunts by qiyas), and all nieces (daughters of full or half brothers/sisters). Cousins (daughters of aunts/uncles) are not included; they are permissible.
This is not a closed list; analogical reasoning extends the same ruling to aunts and nieces further up/down the lineage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا باخته ولا ببنات اخته ولا بعمته ولا بخالته قال الله تعالى حرمت عليكم امهاتكم وبناتكم واخواتكم و عماتكم و خالاتكم وبنات الاخ وبنات الاخت (النساء: 23)
And [he may not marry] his sister, nor the daughters of his sister, nor his paternal aunt, nor his maternal aunt. Allah Almighty said: 'Forbidden to you are your mothers, your daughters, your sisters, your paternal aunts, your maternal aunts, daughters of brother and daughters of sister.' (al-Nisa: 23)
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage continues the enumeration of permanently prohibited women from blood relations. The prohibition includes: (1) one's own sister (full or half), (2) sister's daughters (nieces), (3) paternal aunt (father's sister), and (4) maternal aunt (mother's sister). The proof is the same Quranic verse from Surah al-Nisa, which explicitly mentions sisters, aunts, and brother's/sister's daughters. The Hanafi school holds these prohibitions as absolute and uncontested. The commentator notes that the verse covers both brothers' and sisters' daughters (بنات الاخ وبنات الاخت), so both paternal and maternal nieces are included. The prohibition applies regardless of the aunt being from the father's or mother's side, and regardless of the number of generations (e.g., great-aunts are also included by analogy).

Key Terms
بنت الأخت (bint al-ukht): Sister's daughter (niece)
عمة (ammah): Paternal aunt (father's sister)
خالة (khālah): Maternal aunt (mother's sister)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following women is prohibited for marriage according to this passage?
A) Paternal aunt
B) Daughter of paternal uncle (cousin)
C) Daughter of maternal aunt (cousin)
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Sisters, nieces, and aunts are permanently prohibited by the explicit text of the Qur'an, and no scholar differs on this ruling.

Prohibition of Marrying Brother's Daughters
Specifies the prohibition of marrying a brother's daughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on marrying a brother's daughter and identify the Quranic proof that establishes it.

Core Idea
Marrying your brother's daughter is permanently haram, explicitly forbidden in the Qur'an.

In this passage, the author specifies a particular prohibition within the broader category of prohibited marriages in the Quran. The focus is on the brother's daughter (paternal niece). The ruling is derived from a clear Quranic text, making it a matter of established prohibition with no room for ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited relation and ruling
The text specifies 'daughters of his brother' (banāti akhīhi) and states that these are prohibited. The ruling is haram.
The prohibition is absolute and permanent.
2
Examine the Quranic proof
The author directly cites Quran 4:23 which includes 'wa banāti al-akh' (and daughters of brother). This is a direct textual evidence (dalil naqli).
The Quran is qatʿī al-thubūt, so the ruling is firmly established.
3
Analyze the linguistic construction
The phrase 'banāti al-akh' is an idafa (genitive construction) meaning daughters of the brother. It is explicit and unambiguous (zāhir), leaving no room for interpretation.
In Hanafi usul, a clear text like this is qatʿī al-dalāla.
4
Understand the scope of prohibition
The term 'akh' includes full brothers and half-brothers (paternal or maternal). By extension, the prohibition applies to descendants (granddaughters) through qiyas.
This is the Hanafi position; no distinction is made between full and half relations.
5
Confirm consensus
This prohibition is unanimously agreed upon (muttafaq ʿalayh) across all madhahib. There is no valid disagreement.
The cross_madhhab_status is muttafaq_alayh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا ببنات اخيه قال الله تعالى وبنات الاخ (النساء: 23)
And [he may not marry] the daughters of his brother. Allah Almighty said: 'and daughters of brother' (al-Nisa: 23)
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This is a separate point emphasizing the prohibition of marrying a brother's daughter (paternal niece). The matn explicitly mentions 'bināti akhīhi' (daughters of his brother). The proof is the same verse from Surah al-Nisa which includes 'banāti al-akh' (daughters of brother). Although the earlier point already covered nieces generally, the author repeats to clarify that both brother's and sister's daughters are separately mentioned in the verse. The Hanafi school rules that this prohibition is permanent and applies to full and half brother's daughters as well as their descendants (great-nieces) by analogy.

Key Terms
بنت الأخ (bint al-akh): Brother's daughter (paternal niece)

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Absolute Prohibition of Marrying the Wife's Mother
Ruling with proof stating absolute prohibition of wife's mother

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on marrying the wife's mother and cite the Qur'anic verse and hadith that establish it unconditionally.

Core Idea
Marriage to a woman makes her mother forever haram, even if the marriage is not consummated.

This lesson addresses a clear and settled ruling: the wife's mother becomes permanently forbidden to the husband from the moment the marriage contract with the daughter is concluded. The prohibition does not depend on whether the marriage has been consummated. We will examine the primary evidence from the Qur'an and the complementary hadith that confirm this ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its scope
Identify the prohibited act (marrying the wife's mother) and the condition under which it applies (upon valid marriage contract with the daughter).
No exception for non-consummation.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the Qur'anic verse (4:23) and note the key phrase 'ummahātu nisā'ikum' (mothers of your wives). Explain why it is unconditional.
The genitive construction implies general inclusion of all wives' mothers.
3
Locate the secondary dalil
Examine the hadith from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb which explicitly states the ruling for both consummated and non-consummated marriages.
This removes any ambiguity.
4
Understand the unconditional nature
Recognize that there is no ikhtilaf among the schools; the prohibition is absolute and immediate.
The Hanafi position is unanimous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بام امرأته التي دخل بابنتها او لم يدخل قال الله تعالى وامهات نسائكم (النساء: 23) وعن عمر بن شعيب ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ايما رجل نكح امرأة فدخل بها او لم يدخل بها فلا يحل له نكاح امها وايما رجل نكح امرأة فدخل بها فلا يحل له نكاح ابنتها وان لم يدخل بها فلينكح ابنتها ان شاء (رواه البيهقي)
And [he may not marry] the mother of his wife whom he has consummated with her daughter or not consummated. Allah Almighty said: 'and the mothers of your wives' (al-Nisa: 23). And from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Any man who marries a woman, whether he consummates with her or not, it is not permissible for him to marry her mother; and any man who marries a woman and consummates with her, it is not permissible for him to marry her daughter; but if he has not consummated with her, he may marry her daughter if he wishes.' (Narrated by al-Bayhaqi)
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This point addresses the prohibition of marrying the wife's mother (mother-in-law). The ruling is absolute: the prohibition applies from the moment the marriage contract with the daughter is valid, regardless of whether the husband has consummated the marriage (dakhala) with the daughter or not. The proof is from the Qur'an (Surah al-Nisa 4:23) where Allah says 'wa ummahātu nisā'ikum' (and the mothers of your wives), which is unconditional. The commentary also cites a hadith from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb that explicitly states the prohibition of the mother-in-law whether or not consummation occurred with the daughter. This is a point of agreement among all schools; there is no difference of opinion. The Hanafi ruling is clear: once the marriage contract is concluded with a woman, her mother becomes permanently unlawful to the husband.

Key Terms
أم المرأة (umm al-mar'ah): Wife's mother (mother-in-law)

A) Yes, because the marriage was not consummated
B) No, because the marriage contract made the mother permanently prohibited
C) Yes, but only if the divorce is final (ba'in)
D) No, only if the daughter is deceased

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of the wife's mother is unconditional and immediate upon the marriage contract, based on Qur'an and Sunnah.

Conditional Prohibition of Marrying the Step-Daughter (Rabībah)
Ruling with Quranic proof and clarification of phrase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a step-daughter, identify the condition that triggers the prohibition, and apply it to new scenarios.

Core Idea
A step-daughter is prohibited only after consummation with her mother, not merely by marriage contract.

This lesson clarifies a common misconception about marriage prohibitions in the Hanafi school. The ruling on the step-daughter (rabībah) is conditional: it depends on whether the husband consummated the marriage with her mother. The Qur'anic verse and supporting hadith make this clear. We will unpack the evidence and show how to apply it correctly.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling and Its Condition
Identify the act (marrying the step-daughter) and the ruling: haram if consummation occurred with the mother, halal if not.
2
Cite the Quranic Proof
Locate the verse from Surah al-Nisa (4:23) in the passage. Note that it explicitly conditions prohibition on 'dakhaltum bihinna' (consummation).
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the verse proves the condition: the clause 'fa'in lam takūnū dakhaltum bihinna falā junāḥa 'alaykum' makes permissibility conditional on absence of consummation.
4
Address the Phrase 'Fī Ḥujūrikum'
Clarify that the phrase 'in your care' is descriptive, not a condition. The prohibition applies regardless of custody.
This is the most common misunderstanding addressed by the Hanafi school.
5
Note the Practical Consequence
Understand that once consummation occurs, the step-daughter becomes permanently prohibited (like a blood relation), even after divorce or the mother's death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بابنة امرأته التي دخل بها سواء كانت في حجره او في حجر غيره قال الله تعالى وربائبكم اللاتي في حجوركم من نسائكم اللاتي دخلتم بهن فان لم تكونوا دخلتم بهن فلا جناح عليكم (النساء: 23) وقد تقدم الحديث عن عمر بن شعيب
And [he may not marry] the daughter of his wife whom he has consummated with, whether she is in his care or in the care of another. Allah Almighty said: 'And your step-daughters who are in your care from your wives whom you have consummated with; but if you have not consummated with them, there is no sin upon you.' (al-Nisa: 23). And the hadith from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb has preceded.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This ruling addresses the step-daughter (rabībah). The prohibition is conditional: it applies only if the man has consummated (dakhala) the marriage with the step-daughter's mother (his wife). If he has not consummated with the mother, then marrying the step-daughter is permissible. The condition is explicitly stated in the Qur'an: 'wa rabā'ibukum al-lātī fī ḥujūrikum min nisā'ikum al-lātī dakhaltum bihinna fa'in lam takūnū dakhaltum bihinna falā junāḥa 'alaykum.' The phrase 'fī ḥujūrikum' (in your care) is mentioned but the Hanafi school holds that it is not a condition; the ruling applies regardless of whether the step-daughter is being raised in the man's home or elsewhere. The commentator confirms that the condition is solely consummation with the mother. The hadith previously cited ('Amr ibn Shu'ayb) also distinguishes: if he consummated with the mother, the daughter is prohibited; if not, he may marry the daughter. This is a unique ruling where prohibition depends on an act (consummation) rather than the contract alone.

Key Terms
ربيبة (rabībah): Step-daughter (wife's daughter from another marriage)
دخول (dukhūl): Actual sexual intercourse (consummation of marriage)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man marries a woman and consummates the marriage. Later he divorces her. Can he marry her daughter from a previous husband?
A) Yes, because the step-daughter is not his biological daughter
B) No, because consummation with the mother made the step-daughter permanently prohibited
C) Yes, but only if the step-daughter was not raised in his home
D) No, only if the mother is deceased

Key Takeaway
The step-daughter becomes permanently prohibited upon consummation with her mother, regardless of custody.

Prohibition of Marrying Brother's Daughters
States the prohibition with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on marrying a brother's daughter and identify the Quranic proof for its prohibition.

Core Idea
Marriage with one's brother's daughter is permanently prohibited by definitive Quranic text.

This lesson addresses a clear and unambiguous ruling in Islamic family law: a man cannot marry his paternal niece. The prohibition is established directly from the Quran and is agreed upon by all schools. We will examine the textual proof and understand why this ruling carries absolute authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
From the matn, note that the act is marriage with one's brother's daughter. The ruling stated is prohibition ('la yajuz').
The Urdu clarifies that 'bhatiji' means brother's daughter.
2
Locate the dalil
The sharh cites the Quranic verse 'وَبَنَاتُ الْأَخِ' (and daughters of your brother) from Surah an-Nisa. This is a direct textual proof.
3
Determine the epistemological weight
The Quran is qat'i al-thubut (certain transmission) and the phrase is qat'i al-dalalah (clear meaning). The ruling is therefore definitive and cannot be overridden.
Compare with rulings based on hadith ahad or qiyas, which are zanni.
4
Confirm consensus
The Hanafi position box notes that this ruling is muttafaq alayh (unanimously agreed upon). No ikhtilaf exists among the madhahib.
Thus, a fatwa must consistently uphold this prohibition.

Prohibition of Marrying the Mother-in-Law
States prohibition of marrying wife's mother regardless of consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying one's mother-in-law and cite the Quranic and Hadith evidence that makes the prohibition unconditional.

Core Idea
The mother-in-law is permanently haram whether or not the marriage was consummated.

This lesson examines the clear prohibition of marrying one's mother-in-law. The text from Al-Sharh al-Sameri affirms that the ruling is unconditional: consummation with the daughter is irrelevant. We will explore the Quranic verse and supporting Hadith that establish this permanent mahram relationship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Identify the act under discussion: marrying the mother of one's wife (mother-in-law). State the ruling: it is haram.
The matn says 'ولا بام امرأته' – prohibition is explicit.
2
Locate the Primary Dalil
Find the primary proof: Quran 4:23, the phrase 'وَأُمَّهَاتُ نِسَائِكُمْ' (the mothers of your wives). Recognize that this is a general command indicating prohibition.
The verse is cited in the sharh as the main evidence.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
Determine how the verse proves the unconditional nature. The term 'أمهات' (mothers) is absolute and unrestricted by any condition of consummation. In Hanafi usul, an absolute (mutlaq) command indicates that the prohibition applies to all instances.
This is contrasted with the step-daughter (rabiba) where the Quran adds the condition 'allati dakhaltum bihinna'.
4
Confirm with Secondary Dalil
Examine the hadith from Amr ibn Shu'ayb: 'Any man who marries a woman, whether he has entered with her or not, it is not permissible for him to marry her mother.' This reinforces the absolute prohibition.
The hadith is cited in the passage from Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
5
Distinguish from Step-Daughter Case
Note the key distinction: the mother-in-law is haram unconditionally, while the step-daughter is only haram if the marriage with her mother was consummated. This highlights the precision of the Quranic text.
This distinction is important for understanding the different rulings on mahram relationships.

The sharh emphasizes that this prohibition applies regardless of whether the marriage with the daughter was consummated (dakhala biha) or not. The primary proof is the Quranic verse 'وَأُمَّهَاتُ نِسَائِكُمْ' (the mothers of your wives), which is unconditional. Prohibition of Marrying the Step-Daughter After Consummation
States prohibition of marrying step-daughter after consummation with wife

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a step-daughter after consummation with her mother and identify the Quranic proof and the decisive condition.

Core Idea
Marriage with step-daughter is haram only if the mother was consummated; custody is irrelevant.

This lesson addresses a clear Quranic prohibition: a man cannot marry his wife's daughter (step-daughter) after he has consummated the marriage with the wife. The ruling is unanimous across schools and rests on a direct verse. Understanding the condition—consummation (dukhul)—is essential, as custody of the step-daughter has no legal effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is marrying one's step-daughter (rabiba). The ruling is haram (prohibited) when the marriage with her mother has been consummated.
If the mother was divorced or died before consummation, the step-daughter is halal.
2
Locate the dalil (Quranic verse)
Surah an-Nisa 4:23 explicitly mentions step-daughters and conditions the prohibition on dukhul (going in) with the mother.
The verse is quoted in the source: 'وَرَبَائِبُكُمُ اللَّاتِي فِي حُجُورِكُم مِّن نِّسَائِكُمُ اللَّاتِي دَخَلْتُم بِهِنَّ'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse uses the conditional phrase 'dakhal-tum bihinna' (you have gone in unto them) to indicate that prohibition is tied to consummation. This is a clear textual indication (dalala qati'a).
If the condition is absent (no dukhul), the permission clause applies: 'fain lam takunu dakhaltum bihinna fala junaha alaykum' (if you have not gone in unto them, there is no sin on you).
4
Identify the irrelevant factor
The source explicitly states that whether the step-daughter is under the husband's guardianship (hajr) or not does not affect the ruling.
This refutes a common misunderstanding.
5
Apply to a scenario
Scenario: A man marries a woman who has a daughter. He consummates the marriage, then divorces the mother. He cannot later marry the daughter. If he had divorced before consummation, he may marry the daughter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۱ ولا بابنة امرأته التي دخل بها سواء كانت في حجره او في حجر غيره
1736 (۱۱) اور نہ بیوی کی بیٹی کے ساتھ جس سے صحبت کر چکا ہو چاہے اس کی پرورش میں ہو یا دوسرے کی پرورش میں ہو۔ بیوٹی سے شادی کی لیکن ابھی اس سے صحبت نہیں کی اور اس کو طلاق دے کر اس کی بیٹی سے نکاح کرنا چاہے تو نکاح کر سکتا ہے۔ البتہ اگر بیوی سے صحبت کر لی تو اب اس کی بیٹی جو دوسرے شوہر سے ہے اس سے نکاح نہیں کر سکتا۔ چاہے وہ بیٹی اس بیوی کی پرورش میں ہو یا نہ ہو۔ آیت میں اس کی تصریح ہے کہ بیوی سے صحبت نہ کی ہو تو اس کی بیٹی سے نکاح کر سکتے ہو۔ آیت یہ ہے وربائبكم اللاتي في حجوركم من نسائكم التي دخلتم بهن فان لم تكونوا دخلتم بهن فلا جناح عليكم (آیت ۲۳ سورۃ النساء ۴) اس آیت میں ہے کہ بیوی سے صحبت کی ہو تو اس کی بیٹی سے نکاح حرام ہے۔ اور صحبت نہ کی ہو تو اس سے نکاح حلال ہے۔ البتہ گود میں ہو یا نہ ہو اس سے فرق نہیں پڑتا (۲) او پر مسئلہ نمبرہ میں حدیث گزر چکی ہے کہ بیوی سے صحبت نہ کی ہو تو اس کی بیٹی سے نکاح کرنا جائز ہے۔ حاشیہ : (ب) اور تمہاری سوتیلی بیٹی جو تمہاری پرورش میں ہے تمہاری بیویوں سے جس سے تم نے صحبت کی۔ اگر صحبت نہیں کی تو تم پر کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔
11 Nor the daughter of his wife with whom he has had intercourse, whether she is in his guardianship or in someone else's. [1736] (11) And not with the wife's daughter with whom he has had intercourse, whether she is in his upbringing or another's. ... (full translation from the passage)
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage addresses the prohibition of marrying a step-daughter (rabiba) after consummation with her mother. The matn states that the prohibition applies whether or not the step-daughter was in the husband's custody (hajr). The shurah explains the key distinction: if the marriage with the wife was not consummated, the step-daughter is permissible to marry after divorce; but if consummated, the step-daughter becomes permanently prohibited. The Quranic verse from Surah an-Nisa 4:23 is cited: 'And your step-daughters under your guardianship from your wives to whom you have gone in; but if you have not gone in unto them, there is no sin on you.' The hadith from the previous item is also referenced. The Hanafi ruling is clear: prohibition hinges on consummation (dakhul), not on custody.

Key Terms
ربيبة (rabiba): Wife's daughter from another marriage (step-daughter)
حجر (hajr): Guardianship or physical upbringing

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of marrying a step-daughter is conditional on consummation with the mother, not on custody.

Prohibition of Marrying Father's or Grandfather's Wife
States prohibition with Quran and hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition of marrying a father's or grandfather's wife and cite the Quranic and hadith proofs that establish it.

Core Idea
Marrying a father's or grandfather's wife is haram — proven by Quranic command and hadith severity.

This lesson examines the absolute prohibition of marrying the wife of one's father or grandfather. The passage presents a clear Quranic verse and a hadith that underscores the gravity of this act. Understanding this ruling protects Muslims from a major sin and invalid marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is marrying the wife of one's father or grandfather. The ruling is haram.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The verse 'Wa la tankihu ma nakaha aba'ukum min al-nisa' explicitly prohibits marrying women whom your fathers have married. The term 'aba' includes grandfathers in Hanafi interpretation.
The prohibition is expressed as a direct negative command (la tankihu).
3
Understand the hadith evidence
The hadith narrates that a man who married his father's wife was sentenced to death by the Prophet, showing the severity and categorical prohibition.
Hadith from Yazid ibn Barra'.
4
Confirm the school's agreement
This is a unanimous ruling (muttafaq alayh) across all schools, with no ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
1737 (۱۲) ولا بامرأة ابيه ولا اجداده
(۱۲) اور نہیں جائز ہے اپنے باپ کی بیوی سے اور نہ اپنے دادا کی بیوی سے۔ سوتیلی ماں جس سے باپ نے نکاح کیا ہے۔ اسی طرح اپنی دادی یا سوتیلی دادی جس سے دادا نے شادی کی ہو ان سے نکاح حرام ہے۔
اس آیت میں حرمت کا ثبوت ہے ولا تنكحوا ما نكح آباء كم من النساء الا ما قد سلف (آیت ۲۲ سورۃ النساء۴) اس آیت میں باپ کی منکوحہ سے نکاح سے منع فرمایا گیا ہے۔ اور دادی بھی باپ کے منکوحہ کے تحت بالا جماع حرام ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن يزيد بن براء عن ابيه قال لقيت عمى وقد اعتقد راية فقلت اين تريد ؟ قال بعثی رسول الله الله الى رجل نكح امرأة ابيه اضرب عنقه آخذ ماله (سنن البيهقي) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ باپ کی منکوحہ سے نکاح کرنا حرام ہے۔
1737 (12) Nor the wife of his father nor his grandfathers. (12) And it is not permissible from the wife of one's father and not from the wife of one's grandfather. A step-mother whom the father has married. Similarly, one's grandmother or step-grandmother whom the grandfather has married, marriage with them is forbidden. The proof of prohibition is in the verse: 'And marry not those women whom your fathers married, except what has already passed' (Surah an-Nisa 4:22). This verse forbids marrying the married women of one's father. And the grandmother is also under 'father's married women' by consensus, so she is forbidden. The hadith from Yazid ibn Barra' from his father: 'I met my uncle and he was carrying a banner. I said: Where are you going? He said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) sent me to a man who married his father's wife, to strike his neck and take his property.' From this hadith also it is known that marriage with father's married woman is forbidden.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage covers the prohibition of marrying the wife of one's father or grandfather. The matn includes 'ولا بامرأة ابيه ولا اجداده' meaning 'nor the wife of his father nor his grandfathers'. The sharh explains that this includes step-mothers (sauteli maan) and grandmothers (dadi) or step-grandmothers. The primary proof is the Quranic verse in Surah an-Nisa 4:22 which explicitly forbids marrying women whom one's father has married. The Hanafi position extends this to grandfathers analogically, as they are included in the term 'aba' (fathers) in the verse. The hadith of Yazid ibn Barra' illustrates the severity: the man who married his father's wife was subject to capital punishment. This ruling is based on both Quran and Sunnah, and is agreed upon by all schools.

Key Terms
زوجة الأب (zawjat al-ab): Father's wife (step-mother)
منكوجة (mankuhah): Woman married (to someone); used for father's wife in the verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is prohibited according to this passage?
A) Marrying one's step-mother after father's death
B) Marrying one's grandmother after grandfather's death
C) Both A and B
D) Neither A nor B

Key Takeaway
Marrying the wife of one's father or grandfather is absolutely haram, proven by Quran and Sunnah.

Nikah — Marriage

Prohibition of Marrying Son's or Grandson's Wife
States prohibition of marrying son's or grandson's wife with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage with a son's or grandson's wife, cite the Quranic proof, and distinguish between biological and adopted sons in this ruling.

Core Idea
Marrying the wife of your biological son or grandson is haram; the wife of an adopted son is halal.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri addresses an important ruling in nikah: whom a man may not marry due to previous relationships. The ruling is clear and supported by a direct Quranic verse. However, the key nuance lies in the phrase 'min aslabikum' which restricts the prohibition to biological lineage. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited categories
The text states it is forbidden to marry the wife of one's son (daughter-in-law) and the wives of one's grandsons (sons' children). Identify these as the two categories explicitly prohibited.
The matn uses 'woman of his son' and 'sons' children'.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The shurah cites Surah an-Nisa 4:23: 'wa halailu abnaikum alladhina min aslabikum' (the wives of your sons who are from your loins). This is the primary evidence.
The verse is from the Qur'an, thus qat'i al-thubut.
3
Explain the inclusion of grandsons
The text notes that 'abnaikum' (your sons) is plural and, according to Hanafi usul, a plural includes all categories of sons, including grandsons by lineal descent. Therefore, the prohibition extends to grandsons' wives.
This is an application of the usul principle that al-jam' yufid al-umum.
4
Understand the condition of biological lineage
The phrase 'min aslabikum' (from your loins) restricts the prohibition to biological sons. The text explicitly states that the wife of an adopted son is halal because he is not from the man's loins.
This exception is crucial and often misunderstood.
5
State the final Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi position: marriage with the wife of a biological son or grandson is haram; marriage with the wife of an adopted son is permissible (halal). The evidence is the Quranic verse interpreted with the usul principle of umum and the restrictive condition.
This ruling is muttafaq alayh among the madhahib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
1738 (۱۳) ولا بامرأة ابنه ولا بني اولاده
(۱۳) اور نہ اپنے بیٹے کی بیوی سے اور نہ پوتوں کی بیویوں سے۔
بیٹے کی بیوی یعنی اپنی بہو سے نکاح کرنا حرام ہے۔ اور اسی طرح پوتوں کی بیوی سے نکاح کرنا حرام ہے۔
و حلائل ابناء كم الذين من اصلا بكم ( آیت ۲۳ سورۃ النساء ۴) اس آیت میں فرمایا کہ اپنے بیٹوں کی بیوی سے نکاح کرنا حرام ابناء جمع کا صیغہ ہے اس لئے اس میں پوتے کی بیوی بھی داخل ہے، یعنی وہ بھی حرام ہے۔ البتہ لے پالک بیٹے کی بیوی حلال
1738 (13) Nor the wife of his son nor the wives of his sons' children. (13) And not from the wife of one's son and not from the wives of grandsons. The wife of one's son, i.e., one's daughter-in-law, marriage with her is forbidden. Similarly, marriage with the wife of a grandson is forbidden. The verse: 'And the wives of your sons who are from your loins' (Surah an-Nisa 4:23). This verse says that marriage with the wives of one's sons is forbidden. The word 'ibnaikum' is plural, so it includes the wife of a grandson as well, meaning she is also forbidden. However, the wife of an adopted son is permissible.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage prohibits marriage with the wife of one's son (daughter-in-law) or grandson. The matn states 'ولا بامرأة ابنه ولا بني اولاده'. The shurah explains that this includes biological sons and grandsons. The Quranic proof is from Surah an-Nisa 4:23: 'وَحَلَائِلُ أَبْنَائِكُمُ الَّذِينَ مِنْ أَصْلَابِكُمْ' (the wives of your sons who are from your loins). Hanafis interpret 'abna' (sons) broadly to include grandsons generationally. Importantly, the text notes an exception: the wife of an adopted son (who does not have a biological lineage) is not prohibited, as the prohibition is based on biological lineage (min aslabikum). This is a subtle point distinguishing between true sons and adopted sons.

Key Terms
حليلة الابن (halilat al-ibn): Wife of son (daughter-in-law)
من أصلابكم (min aslabikum): From your loins (biological descent)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because the Quran says 'from your loins'
B) No, because adopted sons are like real sons
C) Only if the adoption was before marriage
D) Only if the adopted son is a blood relative

Key Takeaway
Marriage with the wife of a biological son or grandson is haram; the wife of an adopted son is halal, based on Quran 4:23.

Prohibition of Marrying Foster Mother and Foster Sister
States prohibition of marrying foster mother and foster sister with Quran and hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that marriage with one's foster mother and foster sister is haram, and cite the Quranic verse and Hadith as evidence.

Core Idea
Foster relationships through breastfeeding create permanent marriage prohibitions just like blood ties.

This lesson addresses a key principle in Islamic family law: breastfeeding creates permanent foster relationships that make marriage prohibited. The source text states the ruling concisely and provides both Quranic and Hadith proofs. Understanding this ruling is essential for correct marriage contracts, as many overlook the implications of foster kinship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states that it is not permissible to marry one's foster mother or foster sister. The ruling is haram (prohibited).
The prohibition is absolute, not conditional.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites the Quranic verse from Surah an-Nisa 4:23: 'And your mothers who suckled you and your sisters from breastfeeding.'
This verse explicitly includes foster mothers and foster sisters in the list of perpetually prohibited women.
3
Understand the hadith proof
The hadith from Ibn Abbas reports the Prophet saying: 'What is forbidden through breastfeeding is the same as what is forbidden through lineage.' This establishes the general principle.
The principle is that foster relationships mirror blood relationships in forming mahram (unmarriageable) ties.
4
Note the scope of the principle
Based on the hadith, all relationships that are mahram by lineage become mahram by foster, under specific conditions of rada' (breastfeeding).
Hanafi school requires breastfeeding within the first two years and sufficient quantity (at least five feedings) to establish the prohibition.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The ruling is unanimous across schools regarding the basic prohibition, with differences only in the conditions of rada'.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is that marriage with foster mother and foster sister is haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
1739 (۱۴) ولا بامه من الرضاعة ولا باخته من الرضاعة
(۱۴) اور نہ اپنی رضاعی ماں سے اور نہ اپنی رضاعی بہن سے جائز ہے۔
اس ماں سے جس سے پیدا تو نہ ہوا ہولیکن بچپنے میں اس سے دودھ پیا ہو اس کو رضاعی ماں کہتے ہیں اس سے بھی نکاح حرام ہے۔ اور رضاعی بہن سے بھی صلبی بہن کی طرح نکاح کرنا حرام ہے۔
آیت میں اس کا ثبوت ہے وامهاتكم التي ارضعنكم واخواتكم من الرضاعة ( آیت ۲۳ سورۃ النساء۴) اس آیت میں رضاعی ماں اور رضاعی بہن سے نکاح کرنا حرام قرار دیا گیا ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عباس قال قال النبي له في بنت حمزة لا تحل لى يحرم من الرضاعة ما يحرم من النسب هى ابنة اخى من الرضاعة ( بخاری شریف، باب الشهادة على الانساب)
1739 (14) Nor his mother from breastfeeding nor his sister from breastfeeding. (14) And it is not permissible from one's foster mother and not from one's foster sister. That mother who did not give birth to him but he drank milk from her in childhood is called a foster mother; marriage with her is forbidden. And with a foster sister, just like a full sister, marriage is forbidden. Its proof is in the verse: 'And your mothers who suckled you and your sisters from breastfeeding' (Surah an-Nisa 4:23). This verse declares marriage with foster mother and foster sister forbidden. The hadith from Ibn Abbas: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said regarding Hamza's daughter: 'She is not permissible for me; what is forbidden through breastfeeding is the same as what is forbidden through lineage. She is the daughter of my brother by breastfeeding.' (Bukhari)
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage addresses the prohibition of marriage due to foster relationships (rida'). The matn includes 'ولا بامه من الرضاعة ولا باخته من الرضاعة'. The shurah defines a foster mother as a woman who breastfed the man in infancy, and a foster sister as a girl who was breastfed by the same woman (or by a woman related through milk). The proof is the Quranic verse from Surah an-Nisa 4:23: 'وَأُمَّهَاتُكُمُ اللَّاتِي أَرْضَعْنَكُمْ وَأَخَوَاتُكُم مِّنَ الرَّضَاعَةِ'. The hadith from Ibn Abbas, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) explains that foster relationships make marriage impermissible just like blood ties, is also cited. The Hanafi position follows this principle: all relationships that are mahram by nasab (blood) become mahram by rada' (breastfeeding) under specific conditions, provided the breastfeeding occurred within the first two years and in sufficient quantity.

Key Terms
رضاعة (rada'a): Breastfeeding that creates foster relationships
أم من الرضاعة (umm min al-rada'a): Foster mother (woman who breastfed the child)

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Marrying one's foster mother
B) Marrying one's foster sister
C) Both A and B
D) Marrying one's foster daughter only

Key Takeaway
Foster relationships through breastfeeding create permanent marriage prohibitions equivalent to blood lineage.

Prohibition of Marrying Father's or Grandfather's Wife
States the prohibition of marrying father's or grandfather's wife with Quranic and Hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on marrying a father's or grandfather's wife, identify the Quranic and hadith proofs, and explain why the prohibition is permanent.

Core Idea
A father's or grandfather's wife is permanently forbidden—the marriage contract itself creates the prohibition.

This lesson addresses a clear-cut prohibition in the Quran and Sunnah: marrying the wife of one's father or grandfather. Many assume that after dissolution of the marriage (divorce or death) the prohibition lifts, but the texts show it is permanent. We will examine the primary evidence and the scope of the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being prohibited? Marrying a woman who was married to one's father or grandfather. The ruling is haram.
This applies to both paternal and maternal grandfathers.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is Quran 4:22, which explicitly forbids such marriages. A hadith from Sunan al-Bayhaqi reinforces the severity.
The hadith mentions capital punishment, indicating the gravity of the offense.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'لا تنكحوا' (do not marry) is a direct prohibition (nahy), which in Hanafi usul indicates haram. The hadith's command to execute shows the ruling is irrevocable.
The prohibition is general and covers all similar cases.
4
Scope of the prohibition
It includes grandfathers (ajdad), and the prohibition applies whether the marriage was consummated or not, and even after divorce or death of the father/grandfather.
The term 'mankuhah' means any woman with whom a valid contract was made.
5
Note the permanent nature
Unlike some temporary prohibitions (e.g., during iddah), this prohibition is permanent. There is no exception for later changes in circumstances.
This is a fixed ruling from the Quran and Sunnah, agreed upon across madhhabs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بامرأة ابيه ولا اجداده. اس آیت میں حرمت کا ثبوت ہے ولا تنكحوا ما نكح آباء كم من النساء الا ما قد سلف (آیت ۲۲ سورۃ النساء ۴) اس آیت میں باپ کی منکوحہ سے نکاح سے منع فرمایا گیا ہے۔ اور دادی بھی باپ کے منکوحہ کے تحت بالا جماع حرام ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن يزيد بن براء عن ابيه قال لقيت عمى وقد اعتقد راية فقلت اين تريد ؟ قال بعثی رسول الله الله الى رجل نكح امرأة ابيه اضرب عنقه آخذ ماله (سن للبیہقی ، باب ما جاء فی قوله تعالى ولا تنكحوا ما نكح آباؤكم من النساءج سابع جم ۲۶۲، ۱۳۹۱۸) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ باپ کی منکوحہ سے نکاح کرنا حرام ہے۔
And it is not permissible [to marry] the wife of his father nor the wife of his grandfathers. In this verse is evidence of prohibition: 'And do not marry those women whom your fathers married, except what has already passed' (Surah an-Nisa 4:22). This verse forbids marrying the wife of one's father. And the grandmother [i.e., wife of grandfather] is also included under the prohibition of marrying the wife of the father. In hadith: from Yazid ibn Barra' from his father who said: I met my uncle carrying a flag and I asked 'Where are you going?' He said: 'The Messenger of Allah sent me to a man who married his father's wife: to strike his neck and take his wealth.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). This hadith also shows that marrying the wife of one's father is forbidden.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of al-Quduri, stating the permanent prohibition (haram) of marrying one's father's wife (stepmother) and likewise the wives of one's grandfathers (paternal and maternal). The author provides two proofs: first, the Quranic verse 4:22 which explicitly forbids such marriages in the past and for the future; second, a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ ordered capital punishment and confiscation of wealth for a man who married his stepmother, showing the severity of the prohibition. The Urdu commentary clarifies that the prohibition includes the grandmother (dadi) who is the wife of the grandfather, as she falls under the same category. Note that this ruling applies to the actual wife of the father or grandfather, whether the marriage was consummated or not; the mere contract of marriage creates the prohibition.

Key Terms
منکوحہ (mankuhah): A woman with whom a valid marriage contract has been made, whether consummated or not.
اجداده (ajdadih): Grandfathers (paternal and maternal) – the father's father and mother's father.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Marrying the wife of one's father or grandfather is permanently haram, established by the Quran and Sunnah, with no exceptions.
