Prohibition of Marrying Son's Wife and Grandsons' Wives
States prohibition of marrying daughter-in-law and granddaughters-in-law with Quranic verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying the wife of one's son and grandson, identify the Quranic proof, and explain why an adopted son's wife is excluded.

Core Idea
Marrying one's daughter-in-law or granddaughter-in-law is permanently haram; the Quranic 'sons' includes grandsons, but excludes adopted children.

This passage addresses a clear prohibition in the Quran regarding certain female relatives. The author clarifies that the prohibition extends to both sons and grandsons, based on the plural form of 'sons' in the verse. However, an important distinction is made: adopted sons are not included because the verse restricts the prohibition to biological offspring.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act and its ruling
The passage explicitly forbids marrying the wife of one's son (daughter-in-law) and the wives of grandsons. The ruling is haram (prohibited) permanently.
This is a major sin unless the marriage was already contracted before revelation.
2
Locate the Quranic dalil and its text
The author quotes Surah an-Nisa 4:23: 'And the wives of your sons who are from your loins.' This is the primary evidence for the prohibition.
The Arabic phrase 'min aslabikum' (from your loins) is crucial for the exception.
3
Understand the linguistic principle that includes grandsons
The word 'abna' (sons) is a plural form. In Hanafi usul, the general term 'sons' includes grandsons as well, since they are also descendants through male lineage.
This is based on the principle that 'amm (general) is qat'i (definitive) until specified otherwise.
4
Note the exception for adopted sons and the reason
The Quranic restriction 'min aslabikum' (from your loins) excludes adopted sons because they are not biologically related. Hence, marrying the wife of an adopted son is permissible.
This exception is a reminder that Islamic rulings are based on biological kinship, not social constructs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بامرأة ابنه ولا بني اولاده. بیٹے کی بیوی یعنی اپنی بہو سے نکاح کرنا حرام ہے۔ اور اسی طرح پوتوں کی بیوی سے نکاح کرنا حرام ہے۔ و حلائل ابناء كم الذين من اصلا بكم (آیت ۲۳ سورۃ النساء ۴) اس آیت میں فرمایا کہ اپنے بیٹوں کی بیوی سے نکاح کرنا حرام ہے۔ ابناء جمع کا صیغہ ہے اس لئے اس میں پوتے کی بیوی بھی داخل ہے، یعنی وہ بھی حرام ہے۔ البتہ لے پالک بیٹے کی بیوی حلال ہے۔
And not with the wife of his son nor the wives of his grandsons. The wife of one's son (i.e., daughter-in-law) – marrying her is forbidden. Similarly, marrying the wife of one's grandson is forbidden. 'And the wives of your sons who are from your loins' (Surah an-Nisa 4:23). In this verse it is stated that marrying the wife of your son is forbidden. The word 'abna' (sons) is plural, so it includes the wife of the grandson, meaning she is also forbidden. However, the wife of an adopted son is permissible.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage addresses the prohibition of marrying one's daughter-in-law (son's wife) and similarly the wives of grandsons (sons' sons). The author quotes the Quranic verse 4:23 which explicitly forbids marrying the wives of your sons who are from your loins. The Arabic word 'abna' (sons) is grammatically plural, and according to Hanafi usul, the general term 'sons' includes grandsons as well, since they are also 'sons' in a broad sense. The Urdu commentary adds an important distinction: this prohibition applies only to biological sons and grandsons. The wife of an adopted son (who is not from one's loins) remains permissible to marry, because the Quran restricts it to 'those from your loins' (aslabikum). This is based on the Hanafi understanding that adoption does not create blood relationships for marital prohibitions.

Key Terms
حلائل (halail): Wives (plural of 'halilah' meaning lawful wife).
اصلاب (aslab): Loins (plural of 'sulb') – indicating biological offspring.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No, because adoption creates the same prohibition
C) Only if the marriage was not consummated
D) It is makruh but not haram

Key Takeaway
Marrying the wife of one's son or grandson is haram; the wife of an adopted son is halal.

Prohibition of Combining Two Sisters in Marriage
States prohibition of simultaneously marrying two sisters or having intercourse with two slave sisters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining two sisters in marriage or concubinage, cite the Quranic evidence, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving slave sisters.

Core Idea
Combining two sisters in marriage or concubinage is forbidden simultaneously; the Quran’s general prohibition covers both.

This lesson examines the prohibition of simultaneously having two sisters as wives or as slave concubines. The Quran, hadith, and a companion’s ruling establish this. We will see how the Hanafi school extends the prohibition to milk al-yamin based on the generality of the Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining two sisters simultaneously through marriage or right hand possession. The ruling is haram (forbidden).
Combine means to have both under your marital or sexual authority at the same time.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary evidence is Quran 4:23: 'And that you combine between two sisters except what has already passed.' This explicitly prohibits the combination.
The verse is from Surah an-Nisa, ayat 23.
3
Understand the generality (umum)
The verse uses the general term 'an tajma'u' (that you combine), which covers both marriage contracts and concubinage (milk yamin). The Hanafi principle holds that an amm text applies to all its instances unless specified otherwise.
No specific exclusion exists for milk yamin; therefore, the prohibition applies to both.
4
Examine supporting evidence
The hadith of Umm Habibah (Bukhari) and the athar from Imam Ali (Bayhaqi) confirm that the prohibition extends to slave sisters. In the hadith, the Prophet refused to marry his wife's sister. In the athar, Ali required separation before intercourse with the second slave sister.
These proofs strengthen the Hanafi position and show practice of the Companions.
5
Apply to a case
If a man owns two slave sisters, he may have intercourse with only one at a time. To have intercourse with the other, he must first remove the first from his ownership (sell, gift, or marry her off) or completely sever the right to intercourse.
This directly applies the ruling from the athar of Ali.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجمع بين الاختين بنکاح ولا بملک یمین وطنا. دوسگی بہنوں سے نکاح کرے یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح دو بہنیں باندی تھیں۔ دونوں کو اپنی ملکیت میں لیا تو ایک سے ولی کر سکتا ہے دونوں سے دولی نہیں کر سکتا۔ اور اگر دوسرے سے وطی کرنا چاہے تو پہلی کو یا تو ملکیت سے الگ کرے یا پھر اس کی شادی کسی سے کرا دے اور اس کے بضعہ سے مکمل قطع تعلق کر لے تب دوسری سے وطی کر سکتا ہے۔ آیت میں دونوں بہنوں کو جمع کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ وان تجمعوا بين الاختين الا ما قد سلف (آیت ۲۳ سورة النساء) اس آیت میں دونوں بہنوں کو نکاح میں جمع کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اور وہ عام ہے اس لئے دو باندی بہنوں کو بھی وطی کر کے جمع کرنا حرام ہوگا۔ چنانچہ اثر میں اس کی تصریح ہے۔ عن علی ساله رجل له امتان اختان وطی احداهما ثم اراد ان يطأ الاخرى قال لا حتى يخرجها من ملكه (سن للبيتي ، باب ماجاء فی تحریم الجمع بین الاختین و بین امرأة وابنتها في الوطء بملک الیمین ، ج سابع میں ۲۶۷، نمبر ۱۳۹۳۸/ مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ۵۰ فی الرجل يكون عنده الاختان مملوكتان فيطاً هما جميعا ، ج ثالث ص ۴۷۱ نمبر ۱۶۲۴۶) اس اثر میں حضرت علی نے فرمایا کہ جب تک پہلی کو اپنی ملکیت سے جدا نہ کرے دوسری باندی سے صحبت نہیں کر سکتا۔ حدیث میں بھی دو بہنوں کو جمع کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ آپ پر آپ کی بیوی ام حبیبہ نے اپنی بہن پیش کی تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ وہ میرے لئے حلال نہیں ہے۔ اور حدیث کے آخر میں آپ نے فرمایا فلا تعرضن على بنا تكن ولا اخواتكن (بخاری شریف ، باب وان تجمعوا بین الاضت بین الا ما قد سلف ص ۷۶۶ نمبر ۵۱۰۷) اس حدیث میں اپنی بیویوں کو کہا کہ تم لوگ اپنی بیٹیوں اور بہنوں کو میرے اوپر نکاح کے لئے پیش نہ کیا کرو۔ کیونکہ دو بہنوں کو جمع کرنا حرام ہے۔
And he should not combine two sisters in marriage nor through right hand possession [with the intention of] intercourse. Marrying two blood sisters is not permissible. Similarly, if two slave sisters are both owned, he can have intercourse with one but cannot have intercourse with both. If he wishes to have intercourse with the second, he must either remove the first from his ownership or marry her off to someone and completely sever connection with her genitalia, then he may have intercourse with the second. The Quran prohibits combining two sisters: 'And that you combine between two sisters except what has already passed' (Surah an-Nisa 4:23). This verse prohibits combining two sisters in marriage, and it is general, so it also forbids combining two slave sisters through intercourse. An athar from Ali: A man asked him about having two slave sisters; he had intercourse with one and wanted to do so with the other. Ali said: 'No, until he removes her from his ownership.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). This athar shows that until the first is separated from his ownership, he cannot have intercourse with the second. Also a hadith: The Prophet's wife Umm Habibah offered her sister in marriage to him, and he said: 'She is not lawful for me. Do not present to me your daughters or your sisters.' (Sahih al-Bukhari). Thus combining two sisters is forbidden.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage explains the prohibition of simultaneously having two sisters as wives or as slave concubines (with whom one has intercourse). The Quranic verse 4:23 forbids combining two sisters in marriage. The author explains that the same applies to female slaves: if a man owns two sisters as slave-girls, he may have intercourse with only one at a time. If he wants to have intercourse with the other, he must first terminate his relationship with the first, either by selling her, gifting her, or marrying her off so that she is no longer in his possession with the right of intercourse. This is based on an athar from Imam Ali ibn Abi Talib. The hadith of Umm Habibah further illustrates this: when she offered her sister to the Prophet, he declined because it would mean combining two sisters. The Hanafi position is clear that the prohibition applies equally to marriage contracts and to right hand possession (milk yamin). The prohibition lasts as long as both sisters are simultaneously under the man's marital or sexual authority.

Key Terms
ملک یمین (milk al-yamin): Female slaves owned by a man with whom he may have intercourse without marriage.

Prohibition of Combining a Woman with Her Paternal or Maternal Aunt
States prohibition of simultaneously marrying a woman and her paternal or maternal aunt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition of simultaneously marrying a woman and her paternal or maternal aunt and explain the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
A man cannot marry a woman and her paternal or maternal aunt simultaneously; the Prophet ﷺ explicitly forbade it.

This lesson examines a clear prohibition in marriage law: combining a woman with her father's sister or mother's sister as co-wives. The ruling is derived from an authentic hadith and is agreed upon by all schools. We will explore the textual evidence and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act
What exactly is forbidden? It is the simultaneous marriage of a man to a woman and her paternal aunt (father's sister) or maternal aunt (mother's sister). The two women are co-wives.
The prohibition is on the combination, not on marrying either individually.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade marrying a woman while having her paternal aunt or maternal aunt as a wife.' This is found in Sahih Bukhari.
The hadith uses the phrase 'على عمتها او خالتها' indicating simultaneous marriage.
3
Analyze the wording and derive the ruling
The explicit prohibition (نهی) in the imperative form indicates tahrim (forbiddance). In Hanafi usul, such a prohibition yields haram. The hadith is clear and unconditional.
The ruling is definitive (qat'i al-dalalah) though the transmission is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
4
Understand the scope and limits
The prohibition is temporary: it applies only as long as both women are married to the same man. If the marriage to one ends (by death or divorce), the other becomes permissible. It does not apply if the aunt is divorced or dies before the new marriage.
This is a key point to avoid misunderstanding.
5
Note the wisdom behind the prohibition
The rationale is to prevent enmity and jealousy between close relatives. A woman's aunt is like a mother figure; co-wife rivalry could harm family bonds.
This wisdom is derived by scholars, not explicit in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجمع بين المرأة وعمتها او خالتها. مثلا خالدہ اور اس کی پھوپی کو ایک نکاح میں جمع کرے۔ اور ایک ہی شوہر کے نکاح میں ہو یہ حرام ہے۔ اسی طرح خالدہ اور اس کی خالہ ایک ہی شوہر کے نکاح میں ہوں یہ حرام ہے۔ حدیث میں ایسا کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ سمع جابر قال نھی رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ان تنكح المرأة على عمتها او خالتها
And do not combine a woman with her paternal aunt or her maternal aunt. For example, if one marries Khalidah and her paternal aunt together in one marriage, or they are under one husband, this is forbidden. Similarly, Khalidah and her maternal aunt under one husband is forbidden. The hadith prohibits this: Jabir said: The Messenger of Allah forbade marrying a woman while having her paternal aunt or maternal aunt as a wife.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage presents the prohibition of combining a woman and her paternal or maternal aunt (i.e., the father's sister or mother's sister) simultaneously in marriage. The example given is if a man marries Khalidah and also wants to marry Khalidah's paternal aunt (her 'amma) or maternal aunt (her khala) at the same time, it is forbidden. The proof is the hadith narrated by Jabir ibn Abdullah that the Prophet ﷺ explicitly forbade this. The rationale is to prevent harm and jealousy that may arise between close relatives. Note that this prohibition applies only to simultaneous marriage; if the aunt's marriage ends (by death or divorce), the niece may marry the same man later. Also, the prohibition is on the side of the wife: a woman cannot be combined with her paternal aunt or maternal aunt as co-wives. This ruling is part of the broader category of temporary prohibitions (like combining sisters) that cease when the relationship causing the prohibition ends.

Key Terms
عمتہا (ammatuha): Paternal aunt (father's sister) of the woman.
خالتہا (khalatuha): Maternal aunt (mother's sister) of the woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, if the aunt is older
B) No, it is forbidden
C) Yes, with the woman's permission
D) Only if the aunt is not a Muslim

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of combining a woman with her paternal or maternal aunt is established by explicit hadith and is temporary upon the termination of the first marriage.

Prohibition of Marrying a Woman and Her Aunt
Ruling forbidding marrying a woman simultaneously with her paternal or maternal aunt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a woman and her aunt simultaneously and identify the hadith evidence that prohibits it.

Core Idea
It is haram to marry a woman and her paternal or maternal aunt at the same time.

This lesson examines a clear prohibition in marriage contracts: combining a woman with her aunt under one husband. The ruling is derived from authentic hadith and is agreed upon by all schools of fiqh. You will learn the evidence and the underlying wisdom behind this prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is to be married simultaneously to a woman and her paternal aunt ('ammah) or maternal aunt (khālah). The ruling is haram (forbidden).
The prohibition applies regardless of which woman is married first.
2
Locate the Dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith narrated by Jābir: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade that a woman be married to her paternal aunt or maternal aunt.' This is reported in Sahih al-Bukhari, Sahih Muslim, and Sunan al-Tirmidhi.
The hadith is considered ghasīr (reliable) and is the basis for the ruling.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The explicit prohibition (nahy) in the hadith indicates the ruling is haram in Hanafi usul. The phrase 'on her paternal aunt' (ʿalā ʿammatihā) means marrying a woman while already having her aunt as a wife.
The imperative form of prohibition is understood as definitive.
4
Note the Ijma
This prohibition is agreed upon by all four schools (Hanafi, Maliki, Shafi‘i, Hanbali). There is no valid difference of opinion.
Consensus (ijmāʿ) strengthens the ruling.
5
Apply the Ruling
If a man is married to a woman, he cannot marry her paternal or maternal aunt while remaining married to the niece. Any such contract would be invalid (bāṭil). He must divorce the first wife or wait until the marriage ends.
The same ruling applies if the aunt is related by fosterage (riḍāʿah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجمع بين المرأة وعمتها او خالتها. اور نہ جمع کرے عورت کو اور اس کی پھوپی کو اور اس کی خالہ کو۔ مثلا خالدہ اور اس کی پھوپی کو ایک نکاح میں جمع کرے۔ اور ایک ہی شوہر کے نکاح میں ہو یہ حرام ہے۔ اسی طرح خالدہ اور اس کی خالہ ایک ہی شوہر کے نکاح میں ہوں یہ حرام ہے۔ حدیث میں ایسا کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ سمع جابر قال نھی رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ان تنكح المرأة على عمتها او خالتها (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب لا تنكح المرأة على عمتها نمبر ۱۰۸ ۵ر مسلم شریف، باب تحریم الجمع بين المرأة وعمتها او خالتها في النكاح ص ۴۵۲ ( لامع على ۵۱۰۸ ،باب بين المرأة ومتنا او التهانی ص ۴۵۲ نمبر ۱۴۰۸/ ترمذی شریف نمبر ۱۱۲۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پھوپی اور خالہ کو ایک نکاح میں جمع کرنا جائز نہیں ہے (۲) دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ بھیجی اور بھوپی، اسی طرح بہن کی بیٹی اور خالہ کے درمیان محبت ہوتی ہے۔ اگر دونوں کو ایک نکاح میں جمع کر دیں تو شوکن کی فطری دشمنی شروع ہو جائے گی۔ اس لئے ان دونوں کو ایک شوہر کے پاس جمع ہونے سے منع فرمایا۔
And he shall not combine between a woman and her paternal aunt or maternal aunt. And do not collect a woman and her paternal aunt and her maternal aunt. For example, Khalida and her paternal aunt combine in one marriage, and they are in the marriage of one husband; this is forbidden. Similarly, Khalida and her maternal aunt are in the marriage of one husband; this is forbidden. The hadith forbids such action: Jabir heard: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade that a woman be married to her paternal aunt or maternal aunt' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Bab la tankihu al-mar'atu 'ala 'ammatiha, no. 108?; Sahih Muslim, Bab tahrim al-jam' bayna al-mar'ah wa 'ammatiha aw khalatiha fi al-nikah, p. 452; Sunan al-Tirmidhi, no. 1125). From this hadith it is known that combining a paternal aunt and a maternal aunt in one marriage is not permissible. (2) Another reason is that there is affection between a woman and her paternal aunt, and similarly between a woman's daughter and maternal aunt. If both are combined in one marriage, natural rivalry between co-wives will begin. Therefore they were forbidden to be combined under one husband.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof prohibiting a man from being married simultaneously to a woman and her paternal aunt ('ammah) or maternal aunt (khalah). The text gives an example: if a man is married to Khalida, he cannot also marry her paternal aunt or maternal aunt. The proof comes from multiple hadith, including one from Jabir that the Prophet forbade marrying a woman to her paternal or maternal aunt. The commentary offers a second rationale: there is natural affection between nieces and aunts, so combining them would create jealousy and discord. This ruling is based on hadith evidence and is a consensus among all schools of fiqh. The Hanafi school applies this prohibition strictly: it applies whether the aunt is related by blood or fosterage, as mentioned in the margin of the original text.

Key Terms
عمة (‘ammah): Father's sister (paternal aunt).
خالة (khālah): Mother's sister (maternal aunt).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No, it is forbidden by hadith.
C) Yes, if Fatima consents.
D) No, but only if they are related by blood.

Key Takeaway
It is haram to be married simultaneously to a woman and her paternal or maternal aunt, based on explicit hadith and scholarly consensus.

Prohibition of Marrying a Woman and Her Niece
Extension of prohibition to nieces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that it is haram to simultaneously marry a woman and her niece (brother's daughter or sister's daughter) and explain the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Marrying a woman and her niece is forbidden because it necessarily combines a woman with her aunt.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a man cannot marry two sisters simultaneously. Now we extend this principle: a man also cannot marry a woman and her niece, because that would effectively combine the niece with her aunt (the first wife). This ruling is derived from the same hadith that prohibits marrying a woman to her aunt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is marrying a woman and her niece (brother's daughter or sister's daughter) at the same time. The ruling is haram.
2
Cite the primary dalil
The hadith from Abu Hurairah: 'A woman shall not be married to her paternal aunt nor to her maternal aunt' (Sahih Muslim).
The hadith explicitly forbids combining a woman with her aunt.
3
Establish the wajh al-dalalah
If a man marries a woman and then her niece, the niece becomes a co-wife to her aunt. This is the same prohibited combination as in the hadith.
4
Confirm the extension
The prohibition applies whether the niece is from the wife's brother or sister, and whether the aunt is paternal or maternal.
5
Note the consensus
This ruling is agreed upon by all schools (muttafaq alayh). There is no significant ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا ابنة اختها ولا ابنة اخيها. اور نہ اس کی بھانجی کواور نہ بھتیجی کو۔ یہ مسئلہ نمبر 1 کی ہی تشریح ہے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ شوہر کے پاس پہلے سے خالہ ہو تو اس پر اس کی بھانجی سے شادی نہیں کر سکتا۔ اسی طرح شوہر کے پاس پہلے سے پھولی ہوتو اس پر اس کی بھتیجی سے شادی نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ ان صورتوں میں بھی خالہ اور بھانجی کا ایک شوہر کے تحت جمع ہونا لازم آئے گا۔ اسی طرح پھوپی اور تیجی کا ایک شوہر کے تحت جمع ہونا لازم آئے گا۔ جو حدیث کی رو سے حرام ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا تنكح المرأة على عمتها ولا على خالتها (ب) (مسلم شریف، باب تحريم الجمع بين المرأة وعمتها او خالتھا فی النکاح ص ۴۵۲ نمبر ۳۴۴۰/۱۴۰۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پہلے سے پھوپی ہو تو بھیجی سے شادی نہیں کر سکتا اور خالہ ہو تو اس پر بھانجی سے شادی نہیں کر سکتا۔
And nor the daughter of her sister nor the daughter of her brother. And nor his niece and nor his nephew's sister? This is an explanation of issue number 1. The meaning is that if the husband already has a maternal aunt (khalah), then he cannot marry her niece (the daughter of the sister). Similarly, if he already has a paternal aunt (phupi), he cannot marry her niece (daughter of the brother). Because in these situations, combining the maternal aunt and her niece under one husband becomes necessary, and similarly combining the paternal aunt and her niece under one husband becomes necessary, which is forbidden by hadith. (2) In a hadith, Abu Huraira said: 'The Messenger of Allah said: A woman shall not be married to her paternal aunt nor to her maternal aunt' (Sahih Muslim, Bab tahrim al-jam' bayna al-mar'ah wa 'ammatiha aw khalatiha fi al-nikah, p. 452, no. 1408). This hadith states: If there is a paternal aunt already, he cannot marry her niece; if there is a maternal aunt, he cannot marry her niece.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling to include nieces (both brother's daughter and sister's daughter). The text explains that if a man is married to a woman (the aunt), he cannot marry her brother's daughter (his wife's niece through her brother) or her sister's daughter (his wife's niece through her sister). This is because that would effectively combine a woman with her aunt, which is already forbidden. The principle is that combining a woman and her aunt is prohibited, and by extension, combining a woman and her niece also violates the same prohibition, since the aunt and niece would be co-wives. The hadith cited (Muslim) confirms that a woman should not be married to her paternal or maternal aunt—implying the prohibition also works in reverse: if you have the niece, you cannot marry the aunt, because that would place the aunt under the same husband. The commentary explicitly draws this connection, showing that the ruling is logically consistent.

Key Terms
بنت الأخ (bint al-akh): Brother's daughter (niece).
بنت الأخت (bint al-ukht): Sister's daughter (niece).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because she is a non-mahram.
B) Yes, if the aunt consents.
C) No, because it would combine a woman with her aunt.
D) No, because she is his wife's relative.

Key Takeaway
It is haram to marry a woman and her niece simultaneously because it necessarily creates the prohibited combination of aunt and niece as co-wives.

General Principle of Prohibited Degrees by Analogy
General maxim with examples by analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida that prohibits combining two women who are mahram to each other in marriage, using qiyas to identify prohibited pairs.

Core Idea
If two women are mahram to each other (like aunt and niece), they cannot be co-wives — the prohibition extends by analogy.

This lesson presents a fundamental legal maxim in Hanafi nikah: any two women related by blood, milk, or affinity such that if one were male marriage would be forbidden cannot be married to the same man. The passage uses the example of a woman and her aunt (paternal or maternal) to demonstrate how the specific hadith prohibition is generalized via qiyas. Understanding this maxim is essential for correctly determining prohibited combinations in marriage.

Guided Path
1
State the general maxim
Read the qawida: ' ولا يجمع بين امرأتين لو كانت كل واحدة منهما رجلا لم يجز له ان يتزوج بالاخرى'. Understand its plain meaning: it is forbidden to combine in marriage any two women who, if one were a male, would be prohibited from marrying the other.
The maxim is derived from the specific hadith about aunts.
2
Understand the hypothetical
The rule uses a thought experiment: suppose one of the two women is a male. Then check if marriage between that assumed male and the other woman would be haram. If yes, combining them in marriage is haram.
The hypothetical applies to each woman separately.
3
Trace the analogy
The original case (hadith) prohibits combining a woman with her paternal aunt. The illa (effective cause) is that they are mahram. Extend this to any mahram pair.
Examples: woman and maternal aunt; woman and niece (brother's or sister's daughter).
4
Identify the illa
The common feature is the mahram relationship. If the two women are mahram to each other, the illa is present.
Mahram relationships include those from blood, fosterage, and affinity.
5
Apply the rule
Given any pair of women, determine if they are mahram. If yes, the combination is haram. If not (e.g., cousins), it is permissible.
The rule is a general principle (qawida kulliya).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجمع بين امرأتين لو كانت كل واحدة منهما رجلا لم يجز له ان يتزوج بالاخرى. اور نہیں جائز ہے ایسی دو عورتوں کو نکاح میں جمع کرنا کہ اگر ان دونوں میں سے ایک مرد ہو تو اس کے لئے جائز نہیں ہو کہ دوسرے سے شادی کرے۔ ایسی دو عورتوں کو ایک مرد کے نکاح میں جمع کرنا حرام ہے کہ ان میں سے ایک عورت کو مرد فرض کر لیں تو اس کی شادی دوسری عورت سے حرام ہو۔ مثلا بھیجی اور پھوپی میں سے بھیجی کو مرد فرض کرلیں تو وہ بھیجا ہوگا۔اور بھتیجے کا پھوپی سے شادی کرنا حرام ہے۔ اس لئے بھیجی اور پھوپی کو ایک نکاح میں جمع کرنا حرام ہوگا۔ اور میجی اور پھوپی میں سے پھوپی کو مرد فرض کر لیں تو وہ چا ہوگا۔ اور چا کا بھتیجی سے نکاح کرنا حرام ہے۔ اسی طرح خالہ اور بھانجی میں سے بھانجی کو مرد فرض کر لیں تو بھانجا ہوگا۔ اور بھانجے کے لئے خالہ سے شادی کرنا حرام ہے۔ اور اگر خالہ کو مرد فرض کر لیں تو وہ ماموں ہوگا۔ اور ماموں کے لئے بھانجی سے شادی کرنا حرام ہے۔ اس لئے خالہ اور بھانجی کو ایک شوہر کے نکاح میں جمع کرنا حرام ہے۔ حدیث پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔ اسی بنیاد پر مصنف نے یہ قاعدہ کلیہ بیان کیا ہے۔
And do not combine between two women such that if each of them were a man, it would not be permissible for him to marry the other. It is not permissible to combine in marriage two women such that if one of them were a man, it would not be permissible for him to marry the other. It is forbidden to combine two women in one man's marriage, such that if we suppose one of them to be a man, his marriage to the other would be forbidden. For example, in the case of a woman and her paternal aunt: if we suppose the woman to be a man, he becomes a nephew, and a nephew's marriage to his paternal aunt is forbidden. Therefore, combining a woman and her paternal aunt in one marriage is forbidden. And in the case of a woman and her maternal aunt: if we suppose the woman to be a man, he becomes a nephew, and a nephew's marriage to his maternal aunt is forbidden. Similarly, in the case of a maternal aunt and her niece: if we suppose the niece to be a man, he becomes a nephew, and a nephew's marriage to his maternal aunt is forbidden; and if we suppose the aunt to be a man, he becomes an uncle, and an uncle's marriage to his niece is forbidden. Therefore, combining an aunt and her niece in one marriage is forbidden. The hadith has already passed. On this basis, the author has stated this general rule.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage presents a general legal maxim (qawida kulliya) in Hanafi fiqh: any two women who, if one were a male, would be prohibited from marrying the other, cannot be simultaneously married to the same man. The text illustrates this with examples: a woman and her paternal aunt (if the woman were a nephew, marriage to the aunt is haram), a woman and her maternal aunt (analogous), and a woman and her niece (if the niece were a nephew, marriage to the aunt is haram). This principle extends the specific prohibitions from the Quran and hadith to all cases where a mahram relationship exists. The basis is that the hadith about aunts implies a broader rule: the prohibition of combining women who are mahram to each other (like aunt and niece). This is a classic example of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul: extracting a general rule from specific texts. The author mentions that the hadith has already been cited, and this rule is derived from it.

Key Terms
قاعدة كلية (qā‘ida kulliyya): A general legal principle that applies to multiple cases of similar nature.
محرم (maḥram): A person with whom marriage is permanently forbidden due to blood, milk, or affinity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits combining any two women in one marriage if they are mahram to each other, as established by analogy from the hadith on aunts.

Permissibility of Marrying a Woman and Her Stepdaughter
Ruling statement on permissibility of combining a wife and her stepdaughter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a woman and her stepdaughter simultaneously and distinguish it from prohibited combinations based on mahram relationships.

Core Idea
Marrying a woman and her stepdaughter is allowed because they are not mahram to each other.

This lesson examines a clear ruling from Hanafi fiqh: it is permissible for a man to be married to a woman and also to her stepdaughter (the husband's daughter from a previous marriage). Many mistakenly think this is prohibited due to a vague notion of kinship, but the stepdaughter is not a blood relative of the woman. The margin note cites a hadith about aunts to highlight the contrasting case where prohibition applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining a wife and her stepdaughter in marriage. The ruling is mubah (permissible) as stated by 'la ba'sa' (no harm).
2
Understand the basis of permissibility
The stepdaughter is not a mahram to the woman. They are not blood relatives, nor is there a relationship through milk or marriage that would create permanent prohibition.
Mahram relationships are strictly defined by Qur'an and Sunnah.
3
Distinguish from prohibited combinations
The margin note mentions the hadith forbidding marrying a woman to her paternal or maternal aunt. That prohibition is based on mahram relationship (aunt is blood relative). No such relationship exists between the woman and her stepdaughter.
The hadith is cited to contrast, not to indicate prohibition here.
4
Apply the principle
General rule: any two women who are not mahram to each other can be married simultaneously. This is an exception to the general prohibition of combining two women who are mahram.
Always verify the specific relationship before issuing a ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بان يجمع بين المرأة وابنة زوجها. اور کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے کہ جمع کرے عورت کو اور شوہر کی بیٹی کو جو پہلی بیوی سے ہو۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے روکا کہ عورت سے نکاح کرے اس کی پھوپی پر یا اس کی خالہ پر (ب) آپ نے فرمایا نہ نکاح کرے عورت سے اس کی پھوپی پر اور نہ اس کی خالہ پر۔

Margin note: (a) The Prophet forbade marrying a woman to her paternal aunt or maternal aunt. (b) He said: Do not marry a woman to her paternal aunt nor to her maternal aunt.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: it is permissible to be married simultaneously to a woman and her stepdaughter (the husband's daughter from a previous marriage). The phrasing uses 'la ba'sa' (no harm), indicating permissibility (jawaaz). The stepdaughter is not mahram to the wife (the stepmother), because they are not blood relatives. The wife and the stepdaughter are not related in a way that if one were male they would be forbidden to marry. Therefore, the general prohibition of combining women does not apply. The margin note mentions the hadith about aunts, which confirms that the prohibition is specific to cases where there is a mahram relationship between the two women. The stepdaughter is not mahram to the stepmother, so it is allowed. This is consistent with the general principle: stepmother and stepdaughter do not fall under the prohibited categories because they are not blood relatives or permanently prohibited by milk or affinity.

Key Terms

The General Principle for Prohibited Marriage Combinations
General principle and its illustration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi general principle for prohibited marriage combinations and apply it to identify prohibited polygyny.

Core Idea
If two women would be forbidden to marry each other if one were a man, combining them in marriage is haram.

This lesson introduces a key Hanafi legal maxim (qa'idah kulliyyah) that systematically determines which pairs of women cannot be simultaneously wives of one man. The principle uses a hypothetical gender reversal test to uncover relationships of mahram. Understanding this principle enables you to consistently identify prohibited combinations in polygyny beyond the specific cases mentioned in the hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two women
Consider the two women that a man wishes to combine in marriage.
2
Assume one as male and test
Hypothetically consider one of the women as a man. Check if marriage between this hypothetical man and the other woman would be prohibited due to a permanent blood or marital relationship (mahram).
Focus on permanent prohibitions like lineage, not temporary ones like being married to someone else.
3
Repeat with the other woman
Now assume the other woman as a man and test the same way.
4
Determine the ruling
If either test results in a prohibition, then combining the two women in one marriage is haram. If both tests show no prohibition, the combination is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۷۴۳) (۱۸) اور نہیں جائز ہے ایسی دو عورتوں کو نکاح میں جمع کرنا کہ اگر ان دونوں میں سے ایک مرد ہو تو اس کے لئے جائز نہیں ہو کہ دوسرے سے شادی کرے۔ ایسی دو عورتوں کو ایک مرد کے نکاح میں جمع کرنا حرام ہے کہ ان میں سے ایک عورت کو مرد فرض کر لیں تو اس کی شادی دوسری عورت سے حرام ہو۔ مثلا بھیجی اور پھوپی میں سے بھیجی کو مرد فرض کرلیں تو وہ بھیجا ہوگا۔اور بھتیجے کا پھوپی سے شادی کرنا حرام ہے۔ اس لئے بھیجی اور پھوپی کو ایک نکاح میں جمع کرنا حرام ہوگا۔ اور میجی اور پھوپی میں سے پھوپی کو مرد فرض کر لیں تو وہ چا ہوگا۔ اور چا کا بھتیجی سے نکاح کرنا حرام ہے۔ اسی طرح خالہ اور بھانجی میں سے بھانجی کو مرد فرض کر لیں تو بھانجا ہوگا۔ اور بھانجے کے لئے خالہ سے شادی کرنا حرام ہے۔ اور اگر خالہ کو مرد فرض کر لیں تو وہ ماموں ہوگا۔ اور ماموں کے لئے بھانجی سے شادی کرنا حرام ہے۔ اس لئے خالہ اور بھانجی کو ایک شوہر کے نکاح میں جمع کرنا حرام ہے۔ حدیث پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔ اسی بنیاد پر مصنف نے یہ قاعدہ کلیہ بیان کیا ہے۔
(1743) (18) And it is not permissible to combine two women in marriage such that if one of them were a man, it would not be permissible for him to marry the other. Such a combination of two women under one man's marriage is haram. For example, if from the niece and the paternal aunt, we suppose the niece to be a man, then she would be a nephew, and the nephew's marriage to his paternal aunt is haram. Therefore, combining the niece and the paternal aunt in one marriage is haram. Similarly, if from the niece and the paternal aunt, we suppose the paternal aunt to be a man, then she would be an uncle, and the uncle's marriage to his niece is haram. Likewise, in the case of the maternal aunt and her sister's daughter, if we suppose the sister's daughter to be a man, he would be a nephew, and the nephew's marriage to his maternal aunt is haram. And if we suppose the maternal aunt to be a man, she would be a maternal uncle, and the uncle's marriage to his niece is haram. Therefore, combining the maternal aunt and her sister's daughter under one husband is haram. The hadith has preceded. On this basis, the author has stated this general principle.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage presents a general legal principle (qa'idah kulliyyah) for determining prohibited combinations in polygyny. The author, basing on the hadith and the earlier ruling, formulates a test: if two women are such that if one of them were a man, marriage between them would be prohibited due to consanguinity or affinity, then they cannot be simultaneously wives of one man. The commentary provides examples to illustrate: (1) niece and paternal aunt: if the niece were a man, she would be a nephew, and a nephew cannot marry his paternal aunt; similarly, if the paternal aunt were a man, she would be an uncle, and an uncle cannot marry his niece. (2) maternal aunt and her sister's daughter (niece): similar reasoning applies. The principle covers all such cases where a man would be prohibited from marrying one woman if the other woman were a male relative. This principle is derived from the general prohibition of combining women who are in a prohibited relationship with each other, as indicated by the hadith.

Key Terms
قاعدة كلية (qa'idah kulliyyah): A general legal principle that covers multiple specific cases.
جمع (jam'): Combining two women in one marriage (polygyny).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A woman and her paternal aunt
B) A woman and her maternal aunt
C) Both A and B
D) A woman and her stepdaughter

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi general principle for prohibited marriage combinations uses a hypothetical gender reversal test to identify mahram relationships, making the prohibition systematic and comprehensive.

Combining a Stepmother and Stepdaughter: A Hanafi Exception
Exception to mahram-like combination rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on combining a stepmother and stepdaughter (mubah) and apply the hypothetical gender reversal test to determine permissibility.

Core Idea
A stepmother and her stepdaughter may be co-wives because the prohibition is only one-sided under the gender reversal test.

In Hanafi fiqh, the general principle prohibits combining two women related by a mahram-like tie unless the prohibition is mutual. This passage presents an exception: a man may marry a woman and her stepdaughter (from her previous marriage) because the prohibition is not absolute from both sides. Let us explore the reasoning and the evidence from early scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the general rule
The act is combining a stepmother (the current wife) and her stepdaughter (the wife's stepdaughter from her previous husband) in one marriage. The general rule in fiqh prohibits combining women who are related by a mahram-like relationship unless the prohibition is mutual.
The mahram relationship is not biological; it arises through marriage.
2
Understand the hypothetical gender reversal test
To test mutual prohibition, scholars apply a hypothetical gender reversal: if one woman were a man, would her marriage to the other be haram? Apply this to the stepmother and stepdaughter.
If the stepdaughter were a man (stepson), marriage to her stepmother is haram. If the stepmother were a man (stranger), marriage to the stepdaughter is halal. Since the prohibition is only one-sided, the combination is allowed.
3
Examine the athar evidence
The text cites the action of 'Abdullah ibn Ja'far, who combined the daughter of 'Ali and the wife of 'Ali (stepmother and stepdaughter). Ibn Sirin approved, and al-Hasan al-Basri initially disliked but later permitted. In Hanafi usul, actions of Companions are considered proof (dalil) when no explicit nass exists.
This athar is recorded in Bukhari and al-Daraqutni.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Zufar disagreed, arguing that because one side gives prohibition, the combination should be impermissible. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) held it permissible, and this is the mufta bihi position.
The difference is based on the weight given to the hypothetical test: Zufar requires prohibition on both sides, while the majority requires absolute prohibition only if both sides are prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۷۴۴] (۱۹) ولا بأس بان يجمع بين امرأة وابنة زوج كان لها من قبل. شوہر کی بیٹی جو پہلی بیوی سے ہو اس کو سوتیلی بیٹی کہتے ہیں۔ یعنی سوتیلی ماں اور سوتیلی بیٹی کو ایک مرد کے نکاح میں جمع کرنے میں کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔ سوتیلی ماں اور بیٹی کے درمیاں اگر بیٹی کو مرد فرض کریں تو سوتیلا بیٹا ہوا۔ اور سوتیلے بیٹے کی شادی سوتیلی ماں سے حرام ہے۔ لیکن اگر ماں کو مرد فرض کر لیں تو اجنبی مرد ہوا ۔ اور اجنبی مرد کا اس لڑکی کے ساتھ نکاح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اس لئے ماں کو مرد فرض کرنے کی صورت میں آپس میں نکاح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اس لئے اس مسئلے میں ایک طرف سے جائز ہوتا ہے اور دوسری طرف سے حرام ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے علماء نے فرمایا کہ سوتیلی ماں اور سوتیلی بیٹی کو ایک نکاح میں جمع کرنا جائز ہے (۲) اثر میں اس کا جواز ہے وجمع عبد الله بن جعفر بين ابنة على وامرأة على وقال ابن سيرين لا بأس به وكرهه الحسن مرة ثم قال لا بأس به (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب ما تحل من النساء و ما محرم ص ۲۵ ۷ نمبر ۱۰۵ ۵ر دار قطنی کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۲۲۰ نمبر ۳۸۲۲) اور اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ سوتیلی ماں اور سوتیلی بیٹی کو ایک نکاح میں جمع کرنا جائز ہے قانده امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں کہ جمع نہیں کر سکتے۔ کیونکہ ایک طرف سے حرمت ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی بیٹی کو مرد فرض کریں تو بیٹے کے لئے سوتیلی ماں سے نکاح کرنا حرام ہوتا ہے (۲) او پر گزرا كه وكرهه الحسن مرة (بخاری شریف نمبر ۵۱۰۵) که حضرت حسن ایسے نکاح کو مکروہ سمجھتے تھے۔
[1744] (19) And there is no harm in combining a woman and the daughter of her husband from a previous wife. The husband's daughter from a previous wife is called stepdaughter. That is, there is no objection to combining a stepmother and a stepdaughter in the marriage of one man. Between the stepmother and the daughter, if we suppose the daughter to be a man, then he would be a stepson, and the stepson's marriage to his stepmother is haram. But if we suppose the mother to be a man, then he would be a stranger, and a stranger's marriage to this girl is permissible. Therefore, in the case of supposing the mother to be a man, marriage between them is permissible. So in this issue, it is permissible from one side and haram from the other. Therefore, the scholars have said that it is permissible to combine a stepmother and a stepdaughter in one marriage. (2) There is an athar (narration) permitting it: 'Abdullah ibn Ja'far combined the daughter of 'Ali and the wife of 'Ali (in marriage).' Ibn Sirin said there is no harm in it. Al-Hasan once disliked it, then said there is no harm in it. (Bukhari, Chapter: What is permitted and prohibited among women, p. 257, no. 5105; al-Daraqutni, Kitab al-Nikah, vol. 3, p. 220, no. 3822). From this athar, it is understood that combining a stepmother and stepdaughter in one marriage is permissible. Imam Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him) holds that they cannot be combined, because there is prohibition from one side: if the daughter is assumed to be a man, then a stepson's marriage to his stepmother is haram. And it has passed that al-Hasan once considered it makruh (disliked).
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage discusses an exception to the general principle: combining a stepmother (a woman) and her stepdaughter (the husband's daughter from a previous marriage) in one marriage is permissible. The reasoning is that the general principle is only applicable if the prohibition would be absolute from both sides. Here, if we apply the hypothetical gender reversal test: if the stepdaughter were a man (a stepson), marriage to his stepmother would be haram; but if the stepmother were a man, she would be a stranger to the stepdaughter, and marriage between a stranger and the stepdaughter is permissible. Since the prohibition is only on one side, the combination is allowed. The text cites an athar (narration) where 'Abdullah ibn Ja'far married both the daughter of 'Ali (i.e., his stepdaughter?) and the wife of 'Ali (i.e., his stepmother?). The scholars Ibn Sirin and al-Hasan (after initial dislike) approved of it. Imam Zufar, however, dissented, arguing that because one side gives prohibition, it should be impermissible. The statement also notes that al-Hasan once considered it makruh, but later retracted. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is permissible (ja'iz), as this is the view of the majority of Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms
سوتیلی بیٹی (sutilī bīṭī): Stepdaughter (husband's daughter from a previous wife).
سوتیلی ماں (sutilī māṅ): Stepmother (woman married to the stepdaughter's father).
اثر (athar): Narration from a Companion or Successor (not directly from the Prophet).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A woman and her paternal aunt
B) A woman and her maternal aunt
C) A stepmother and her stepdaughter
D) A woman and her sister's daughter

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a man to be married to both a woman and her stepdaughter because the prohibition is not mutual under the hypothetical gender reversal test.

Permanent Prohibition from Zina: Mother and Daughter of the Adulteress
Ruling with proof: Zina creates affinity prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that zina creates permanent prohibition of marriage with the adulteress's mother and daughter, and explain the proof based on hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
Zina creates permanent marriage bars with the adulteress's mother and daughter, just as marriage does.

This lesson addresses a key Hanafi ruling: the effect of zina (unlawful intercourse) on marriage prohibitions. While zina is a grave sin, the Hanafi school holds that it also establishes a relationship of affinity (musahara) that permanently bars marriage with the adulteress's mother and daughter. This ruling is based on a hadith attributed to the Prophet ﷺ and on analogical reasoning to valid marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? What is the hukm level? The act is zina with a woman; the ruling is that her mother and daughter become permanently forbidden (haram mu'abbad) to the man.
The prohibition applies even if the zina was consensual and regardless of punishment.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The text cites a hadith from 'A'isha (رضي الله عنها) concerning a dispute. The key principle extracted is 'al-walad li al-firash wa li al-'ahir al-hajar' (the child belongs to the bed, and the fornicator gets nothing).
This hadith does not explicitly mention the mother/daughter, but the Hanafis use it as an indication that zina creates legal consequences.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the prohibition? The fornicator has no claim to the child, meaning the relationship is akin to a stranger. By analogy (qiyas), if zina does not establish lineage, it still creates affinity because the act itself blurs the lines of mahram. The Hanafis argue that to prevent confusion, the same prohibitions as marriage apply by way of ihtiyat (precaution).
The relationship becomes like mother-in-law and stepdaughter.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Do other schools agree? The Hanafi position is mukhtalaf fih; some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not consider zina as creating affinity prohibitions. They restrict such prohibitions to valid marriage only.
The cross-madhhab difference has practical implications for marriage arrangements.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Why is the Hanafi position mufta bihi? The Hanafis rely on the zahir of the hadith, general principles of ihtiyat, and the need to block means to immorality. There is no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; all imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۷۴۵] (۲۰) ومن زنى بامرأة حرمت عليه أمها وابنتها. مثلا زینب سے کسی نے زنا کیا تو اس مرد پر زینب کی ماں بھی ہمیشہ کے لئے حرام ہوگئی اور زینب کی بیٹی بھی ہمیشہ کے لئے حرام ہو گئی۔ زنا کرنا اگر چہ حرام ہے پھر بھی زنا کی وجہ سے جزئیت ثابت ہو گئی۔ اور گویا کہ مزنیہ کی ماں حرمت مصاہرہ کی وجہ سے ساس بن گئی اور مزنیہ کی بیٹی سوتیلی بیٹی اور رہائب بن گئی۔ جس کی وجہ سے ہمیشہ کے لئے ان سے نکاح حرام ہو گیا (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن عائشة انها قالت اختصم سعد بن ابي وقاص وعبد بن زمعة في غلام فقال سعد هذا يا رسول الله ابن اخي عتبة بن ابی وقاص عهد الى انه ابنه انظر الى شبهه وقال عبد بن زمعة هذا اخى يا رسول الله ولد على فراش ابي من وليدته فنظر رسول الله الله الى شبهه فراى شبها بينا بعتبة فقال هو لك يا عبد الولد للفراش وللعاهر الحجر واحتجى منه يا سودة بنت زمعة قالت فلم يرسودة قط (ب) (مسلم شریف، باب الولد للفراش و توقى الشبهات ص۴۷۰ نمبر ۱۴۵۷) حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عبداللہ بن جعفر نے حضرت علی کی بیٹی اور حضرت علی کی بیوی کو جمع کیا ایک نکاح میں۔ حضرت ابن سیرین نے فرمایا کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔ اور حضرت حسن نے کبھی نا پسند کیا پھر کہا کہ کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے (ب) سعد بن ابی وقاص اور عبد بن زمعہ نے ایک لڑکے کے بارے میں جھگڑا کیا۔ پس حضرت سعد نے فرمایا یہ میرے بھائی عقبہ بن ابی وقاص کا بیٹا ہے۔ مجھ سے عہد کیا کہ وہ ان کا بیٹا ہے۔ دیکھئے لڑ کا کتنا ان کے مشابہ ہے۔ اور عہد بن زمعہ نے کہا یہ میرا بھائی ہے یارسول اللہ ! میرے باپ کے فراش پر پیدا ہوا ہے اس کی باندی سے۔ حضور نے لڑکے کو عتبہ بن ابی وقاص کے مشابہ دیکھا۔ پھر بھی آپ (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر)
[1745] (20) And whoever commits zina with a woman, her mother and her daughter become forbidden to him. For example, if someone commits zina with Zaynab, then Zaynab's mother becomes permanently forbidden to that man, and Zaynab's daughter also becomes permanently forbidden. Although zina is haram, nevertheless due to zina, a marital relationship (musahara) is established. It is as if the mother of the adulteress becomes his mother-in-law due to the prohibition of affinity (hurmat al-musaharah), and the daughter of the adulteress becomes his stepdaughter and a ward (rabiba?), so marriage with them becomes permanently forbidden. (2) The hadith indicates this. From 'A'isha that she said: Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and 'Abd ibn Zam'ah disputed concerning a slave. Sa'd said: 'O Messenger of Allah, this is the son of my brother 'Utbah ibn Abi Waqqas. He entrusted me that he is his son. Look at his resemblance.' 'Abd ibn Zam'ah said: 'This is my brother, O Messenger of Allah. He was born on my father's bed from his slave-wife.' The Messenger of Allah looked at his resemblance and saw a clear resemblance to 'Utbah. He said: 'He is yours, O 'Abd. The child belongs to the bed, and for the fornicator is the stone. And veil yourself from him, O Sawdah bint Zam'ah.' She said: 'He never saw Sawdah thereafter.' (Muslim, Kitab al-Walad li al-Firash wa Tuqiya al-Shubuhat, p. 470, no. 1457) Footnote: (a) 'Abdullah ibn Ja'far combined the daughter of 'Ali and the wife of 'Ali in one marriage. Ibn Sirin said there is no harm. And al-Hasan once disliked it, then said there is no harm. (b) Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and 'Abd ibn Zam'ah disputed about a boy... (remaining on next page)
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage addresses the effect of zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) on marriage prohibitions. The ruling is: if a man commits zina with a woman, then that woman's mother and daughter become permanently forbidden (haram mu'abbad) to him. This is because zina, despite being sinful, creates a relationship of musahara (affinity) similar to that created by a valid marriage. Thus, the adulteress's mother becomes like a mother-in-law (hamat), and her daughter becomes like a stepdaughter (rabibah), both of whom are permanently forbidden to the man due to affinity (hurmat al-musaharah). The text cites a hadith from 'A'isha concerning a dispute between Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and 'Abd ibn Zam'ah. The hadith is used to establish the principle 'al-walad li al-firash wa li al-'ahir al-hajar' (the child belongs to the bed, and the fornicator gets nothing). While this specific hadith does not explicitly mention the prohibition of the mother and daughter, the commentary uses it as an indication (isharah) of the general principle that zina establishes certain legal consequences. The Hanafi school holds that the prohibition extends to the mother and daughter of the woman with whom zina was committed, ensuring that the relationship is treated analogously to marriage for the purpose of determining mahram relationships. The footnote added mentions the permissibility of combining stepmother and stepdaughter (already covered in the previous lesson) and the hadith continues on the next page.

Key Terms
زنا (zina): Unlawful sexual intercourse between a man and a woman who are not married to each other.
حرمت مصاہرہ (hurmat al-musaharah): Prohibition of marriage due to affinity (relationships created by marriage).
مزنیہ (mazniyyah): The woman with whom zina was committed (adulteress).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Her daughter only
B) Her mother only
C) Both her mother and daughter
D) None, because zina does not create any marriage prohibition

Key Takeaway
Zina creates a permanent bar to marriage with the adulteress's mother and daughter, analogous to the prohibition created by valid marriage.

Combining a Woman and Her Step-Daughter in Marriage
Ruling on combining step-mother and step-daughter in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining a woman and her step-daughter in marriage and explain the evidence from the athar of Abdullah ibn Ja'far.

Core Idea
Combining a woman and her step-daughter is permissible in Hanafi fiqh, even though some scholars disagreed.

This passage addresses a subtle issue in marriage affinity prohibitions. While combining a biological mother and daughter is universally forbidden, the step-daughter (from a previous husband) is not a blood relative to the new wife. Therefore, the Hanafi school, based on the practice of the companion Abdullah ibn Ja'far, permits a man to marry both a woman and her step-daughter simultaneously.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining a woman and her step-daughter (the wife's daughter from a previous husband) in the same marriage contract. The Hanafi ruling is that it is permissible (mubah).
The step-daughter is not a mahram by lineage.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the athar (narration) of Abdullah ibn Ja'far, who married the daughter of Ali (step-daughter) while remaining married to Ali's wife (step-mother).
This is reported in Bukhari and Dar Qutni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The action of a companion serves as evidence that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not forbid this practice, and companion practice is a source of law in the Hanafi school.
The dalal is zanni but sufficient for permissibility.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) held that combining them is not permissible because if the step-daughter were a son, marriage to the step-mother would be forbidden.
Hasan al-Basri initially disliked it but later agreed with permissibility.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon because the explicit practice of Abdullah ibn Ja'far overrides the hypothetical analogy of Imam Zufar.
The mufta bihi is permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الثالث) ۱۴ كتاب النكاح يجمع بين امرأة وابنة زوج كان لها من قبل ۱۷۴۵ (۲۰) ومن زنى بامرأة حرمت عليه شوہر کی بیٹی جو پہلی بیوی سے ہو اس کو سوتیلی بیٹی کہتے ہیں۔ یعنی سوتیلی ماں اور سوتیلی بیٹی کو ایک مرد کے نکاح میں جمع کرنے میں کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔ سوتیلی ماں اور بیٹی کے درمیاں اگر بیٹی کو مرد فرض کریں تو سوتیلا بیٹا ہوا۔ اور سوتیلے بیٹے کی شادی سوتیلی ماں سے حرام ہے۔ لیکن اگر ماں کو مرد فرض کر لیں تو اجنبی مرد ہوا ۔ اور اجنبی مرد کا اس لڑکی کے ساتھ نکاح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اس لئے ماں کو مرد فرض کرنے کی صورت میں آپس میں نکاح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اس لئے اس مسئلے میں ایک طرف سے جائز ہوتا ہے اور دوسری طرف سے حرام ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے علماء نے فرمایا کہ سوتیلی ماں اور سوتیلی بیٹی کو ایک نکاح میں جمع کرنا جائز ہے (۲) اثر میں اس کا جواز ہے وجمع عبد الله بن جعفر بين ابنة على وامرأة على وقال ابن سيرين لا بأس به وكرهه الحسن مرة ثم قال لا بأس به (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب ما تحل من النساء و ما محرم ص ۲۵ ۷ نمبر ۱۰۵ ۵ر دار قطنی کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۲۲۰ نمبر ۳۸۲۲) اور اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ سوتیلی ماں اور سوتیلی بیٹی کو ایک نکاح میں جمع کرنا جائز ہے قانده امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں کہ جمع نہیں کر سکتے۔ کیونکہ ایک طرف سے حرمت ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی بیٹی کو مرد فرض کریں تو بیٹے کے لئے سوتیلی ماں سے نکاح کرنا حرام ہوتا ہے (۲) او پر گزرا كه وكرهه الحسن مرة (بخاری شریف نمبر ۵۱۰۵) که حضرت حسن ایسے نکاح کو مکروہ سمجھتے تھے۔
The Sharh al-Thamiri, part three, 14, Book of Nikah. He combines a woman and the daughter of a husband that he had from before 1745 (20). And whoever commits zina with a woman, her mother and her daughter become forbidden to him. The wife's daughter from a previous husband is called a step-daughter. That is, there is no harm in combining a step-mother and step-daughter in the marriage of one man. If the daughter is considered as a male, then she becomes a step-son, and the step-son's marriage to the step-mother is forbidden. But if the mother is considered as a male, then she becomes a foreign man, and marriage of a foreign man to that girl is permissible. Therefore, in the case of considering the mother as a male, marriage between them is permissible. So in this issue, it is permissible from one side and forbidden from the other. Hence the scholars said: Combining a step-mother and step-daughter in one marriage is permissible. (2) There is evidence of its permissibility in the athar: Abdullah ibn Ja'far combined between the daughter of Ali and the wife of Ali. Ibn Sirin said: There is no harm in it. Hasan once disliked it, then said: There is no harm in it. (Bukhari, chapter on what is permissible and forbidden among women, p. 257, no. 5105; Dar Qutni, al-Nikah, vol. 3, p. 220, no. 3822). So from the athar it is understood that combining a step-mother and step-daughter in one marriage is permissible. Imam Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him) holds that they cannot be combined. Because there is prohibition from one side: if the daughter is considered as male, then marriage of the son to the step-mother is forbidden. (2) As passed, that Hasan once disliked it (Bukhari no. 5105).
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on combining a woman and her step-daughter (the wife's daughter from a previous marriage) in the same marriage contract. The matn states: 'He combines a woman and the daughter of a husband that he had from before' — meaning it is permissible for a man to marry a woman and also marry her step-daughter (i.e., the daughter of his wife from a previous husband). The commentary explains that there is no harm in this combination, unlike a real mother and daughter who cannot be married together. The reasoning is that if we consider the step-daughter as a male (hypothetically), she would be a step-son, and marriage between a step-son and step-mother is forbidden. But if we consider the mother as a male, she becomes a foreign man, and marriage to the step-daughter is permissible. So the ruling is permissible from one perspective. The proof is the athar (narration) of Abdullah ibn Ja'far, who married the daughter of Ali (his step-daughter from his marriage to Fatima?) and also remained married to Ali's wife (his mother-in-law?). This shows the Hanafi permissibility. Ibn Sirin agreed, and Hasan al-Basri initially disliked it but later said there is no harm. Imam Zufar disagreed, arguing that from one side there is prohibition (like a step-son and step-mother), but the Hanafi position is that the combination is permissible because the prohibited relationship is only from one side and does not create a real mahram tie.

Key Terms
سوتیلی بیٹی (sauteli beti): Step-daughter: the daughter of one's wife from a previous husband.
سوتیلی ماں (sauteli maa): Step-mother: the wife of one's father from a previous marriage? Here it refers to the woman married to the man, who is the step-mother of his wife's daughter? Actually, the context is confusing. 'Step-mother' here refers to the woman whose step-daughter is being married. She is the wife of the man?
حرمت مصاہرہ (hurmat musahara): Prohibition due to marriage affinity; relationships that become forbidden through marriage (like mother-in-law, step-daughter, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No, it is forbidden.
C) It is makruh.
D) It is permissible only if the step-daughter is not his mahram.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, it is permissible to combine a woman and her step-daughter (from a previous husband) in one marriage contract, as evidenced by the practice of Abdullah ibn Ja'far.

Nikah — Marriage

8 min
The Hanafi Ruling: Zina Creates Hurmat Musahara
Ruling that zina creates marriage prohibition with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that zina establishes a permanent marriage prohibition with the woman's mother and daughter, and identify the three key proofs (hadith of Sawda, mursal hadith, athar of Umar).

Core Idea
Zina creates a prohibition like marriage — the mother and daughter become permanently haram.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that committing zina (fornication) with a woman makes her mother and daughter forever forbidden to the fornicator. While the act itself is sinful, it establishes a relationship (jinsiyya) analogous to marriage, triggering the rules of hurmat musahara. We will explore the primary textual evidence from the Sunnah and the practice of the Companions that support this ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its implications
Identify the exact hukm: if a man commits zina with a woman, her mother and daughter become permanently haram for him. Understand that this applies even if the daughter is from a different father, and the prohibition is mu'abbad (permanent).
This is a specific case of hurmat musahara — prohibitions arising from affinity.
2
Examine the hadith of Sa'd and Abd ibn Zam'a
Analyze the story where the Prophet (ﷺ) ordered Sawda to veil from the boy born from zina, despite attributing lineage to the husband. The order to veil indicates a relationship that affects marriage (she would not need to veil from a true mahram).
The phrase 'ihtajibi minhu' (veil from him) is key — it implies non-mahram status due to zina.
3
Consider the mursal hadith on looking at private parts
The hadith 'Whoever looks at the private part of a woman, her mother and daughter are not halal for him' is cited. Even though it is mursal, it is accepted as evidence in the Hanafi school, and the principle of qiyas al-awla (even more so) applies: if mere looking creates prohibition, then actual zina does so more strongly.
Mursal hadith are considered valid in Hanafi usul under certain conditions.
4
Review the athar of Umar
Umar (ra) uncovered his slave girl and then told his son she was not halal for him. This shows that even mere looking (or touching with desire) establishes hurmat musahara, reinforcing the Hanafi view.
The Hanafi school often relies on the practice of the Companions (athar) as supplementary evidence.

کی فراش رہی ہے اس لئے لڑکا میرا بھائی ہے۔ آپ نے لڑکے کا نسب زمعہ سے ثابت کیا کیونکہ اس کی ماں اس کا فراش تھی۔ لیکن زمعہ کی بیٹی حضرت سودہ سے فرمایا کہ حقیقت میں یہ لڑکا تمہارا بھائی نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس سے پردہ کرتے رہو۔ اور زندگی بھر اس سے پردہ کرتی رہی۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ زنا کی وجہ سے زانی کے ساتھ تعلق رہتا ہے اور حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہوتی ہے (۲) ایک حدیث میں اس کی صراحت ہے۔ عن ابی ھانی قال قال رسول الله من نظر الى فرج امرأة لم تحل له امها ولا ابنتها (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی شيبة ۴۸ الرجل باقع علی ام امرأته ادابته امراته ما حال امرأته ؟ ج ثالث ص ۴۶۹ ، نمبر ۶۲۲۹ ارسفن سمیہقی ، باب الزنا لا تحرم الحلال، ج سابع ص ۲۷۶، نمبر ۱۳۹۶۹) اس حدیث مرسل سے پتہ چلا کہ اجنبی عورت کا رج دیکھ لیا تو حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ اور اس سے اس عورت کی ماں اور بیٹی حرام ہو جائے گی۔ اور جب صرف فرج دیکھنے سے حرام ہوگی تو زنا کرنے سے بدرجہ اولی حرام ہوگی (۳) عن مكحول ان عمر جرد جاريته فسأله اياها بعض بنيه فقال انها لا تحل لك (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی هيبة ۲۸ في الرجل يحجر المرأة ويلتمسها من لا تجمل لابنه وان فعل الاب ج ثالث ص ۴۶۷، نمبر ۱۶۲۱۲) اس اثر میں حضرت عمر نے اپنی باندی کے کپڑے کھولے تو اپنے بیٹے سے فرمایا کہ اب یہ تیرے لئے حلال نہیں رہی۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ صرف چھونے سے حرمت مصاہرہ ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ ناند و امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ زنا کرنے سے یا شہوت کے ساتھ چھونے سے حرمت مصاہرت ثابت نہیں ہوگی اور نہ مزنیہ کی ماں اور اس کی بیٹی زانی پر حرام ہوں گی۔ (۱) او پر مسلم اور ترندی کی حدیث گزری کہ فراش والے کے لئے نسب ثابت کیا اور زانی کو محروم کردیا اور فرمایا الولد للفراش وللعاهر الحجر (ج) (مسلم شریف ص ۴۷۰ نمبر ۱۳۵۷) جس کی وجہ سے مزنیہ کی ماں اور بیٹی زانی پر حرام نہیں ہوں گی (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة قالت سئل رسول الله الله عن رجل زنا بامرأة فاراد ان يتزوجها او ابنتها ، قال لا يحرم الحرام الحلال انما يحرم ما كان بنكاح ( و ) ( سنن دار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۸۸ نمبر ۳۶۳۸ سفن للبیہقی ، باب الز تالا حرم الحلال ج حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) آپ نے فرمایا یہ تمہارا بھائی ہے اے عبد بن زمعہ ا کیونکہ بچہ فراش والے کے لئے ہے اور زانی کو پتھر ہے۔ اور اے سودہ بنت زمعہ تم اس لڑکے سے پردہ کرو۔ کہتے ہیں کہ سودہ نے کبھی اس لڑکے کو نہیں دیکھا (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کسی نے کسی عورت کا فرج دیکھ لیا تو اس کے لئے اس عورت کی ماں حلال نہیں اور نہ اس کی بیٹی حلال ہے (ب) حضرت عمر نے اپنی باندی کا ستر کھولا پھر ان کے بعض بیٹے نے وہ باندی مانگی تو حضرت عمر نے فرمایا یہ باندی اب تیرے لئے حلال نہیں ہے (ج) بچہ بیوی والے کے لئے ہے اور زانی کے لئے پتھر ہے یعنی زانی سے نسب ثابت نہیں ہو گا (1) آپ سے ایک آدمی کے بارے میں پوچھا جس نے ایک عورت سے زنا کیا پھر اس سے شادی کرنا چاہتا ہے یا اس کی بیٹی سے شادی کرنا چاہتا ہے تو آپ نے فرما یا حرام یعنی زنا حلال چیز کو حرام نہیں کرتا، صرف نکاح کے ذریعہ حرام ہوگی۔
And whoever commits zina with a woman, her mother and her daughter are forbidden to him. For example, if someone committed zina with Zaynab, then Zaynab's mother becomes permanently forbidden to that man, and Zaynab's daughter also becomes permanently forbidden. Although zina is forbidden, still due to zina, a type of affinity (jinsiyya) is established. It is as if the mother of the woman with whom zina was committed becomes the mother-in-law due to the prohibition of musahara, and the daughter becomes the step-daughter and step-granddaughter (?) Therefore, marriage to them becomes permanently forbidden. (2) There is a reference to this in the hadith: On the authority of Aisha, she said: Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and Abd ibn Zam'a disputed about a boy. Sa'd said: O Messenger of Allah, this is the son of my brother Utba ibn Abi Waqqas; he pledged to me that he is his son; look at his resemblance. Abd ibn Zam'a said: This is my brother, O Messenger of Allah; he was born on my father's bed from his slave woman. The Messenger of Allah looked at his resemblance and saw a clear resemblance to Utba. He said: He is for you, O Abd; the child belongs to the bed, and for the fornicator is the stone. Veil from him, O Sawda bint Zam'a. She said: So he never saw her (i.e., Sawda veiled from him). (Muslim, chapter on the child belongs to the bed, no. 1457) In this hadith, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas claimed that the boy was his nephew because in the pre-Islamic period his brother Utba had committed zina with the mother. And look, the boy exactly resembles my brother. Abd ibn Zam'a claimed that the boy's mother was in his father's bed, so the boy is his brother. The Prophet attributed the boy's lineage to Zam'a because his mother was his bed. But he said to Zam'a's daughter, Sawda: In reality, this boy is not your brother, so you must veil from him. And she veiled from him for the rest of her life. This shows that zina creates a relationship with the fornicator and establishes the prohibition of musahara. (2) There is explicit mention in another hadith: On the authority of Abu Hani, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever looks at the private part of a woman, her mother and her daughter are not halal for him. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 6229; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, no. 13969) This mursal hadith indicates that if a man looks at the private part of a foreign woman, then the prohibition of musahara is established, and the woman's mother and daughter become forbidden to him. And if it is forbidden by mere looking, then by zina it is even more forbidden. (3) On the authority of Makhul: Umar uncovered his slave girl (i.e., looked at her private parts), and one of his sons asked for her. He said: She is not halal for you. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 16212) In this athar, Umar uncovered his slave girl and said to his son: She is no longer halal for you. This shows that mere touching (looking) establishes the prohibition of musahara. Now, Imam Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) says that committing zina or touching with desire does not establish the prohibition of musahara, and the mother and daughter of the woman with whom zina was committed are not forbidden to the fornicator. (1) The hadith from Muslim and Tirmidhi passed earlier that lineage is established for the one who has the bed and the fornicator is deprived: 'The child belongs to the bed, and for the fornicator is the stone.' Therefore, the mother and daughter of the woman with whom zina was committed are not forbidden to the fornicator. (2) Another hadith: On the authority of Aisha, she said: The Messenger of Allah was asked about a man who committed zina with a woman and then wanted to marry her or her daughter. He said: The forbidden does not make the halal forbidden; only marriage makes things forbidden. (Sunan Dar Qutni, vol. 3, no. 3638; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on zina does not make halal forbidden). Footnote: (from previous page) The Prophet said: He is your brother, O Abd ibn Zam'a, because the child belongs to the bed and the fornicator gets the stone. And O Sawda bint Zam'a, veil from this boy. They say Sawda never saw him. (a) The Prophet said: If someone looks at a woman's private part, then her mother and daughter are not halal for him. (b) Umar uncovered his slave girl's private parts; then one of his sons asked for that slave girl, and Umar said: This slave girl is no longer halal for you. (c) The child belongs to the wife and the fornicator gets the stone, meaning lineage is not established for the fornicator. (1) The Prophet was asked about a man who committed zina with a woman and then wants to marry her or her daughter. He said: The forbidden (zina) does not make the halal forbidden; only marriage makes things forbidden.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling that zina (fornication) with a woman establishes the same marriage prohibitions as a valid marriage (hurmat musahara). According to the Hanafi madhhab, if a man commits zina with a woman, her mother and her daughter become permanently forbidden to him, just as if he had married her. The commentary explains the reasoning: although zina is sinful, it creates a kind of relationship (jinsiyya) analogous to marriage, making the woman's mother his mother-in-law and her daughter his step-daughter. This is supported by several evidences. The first evidence is the hadith of Sa'd and Abd ibn Zam'a: the Prophet attributed the child to the husband (the owner of the bed) and said the fornicator gets nothing, but he still ordered Sawda to veil from the boy, recognizing a relationship due to zina. The second evidence is a mursal hadith that looking at a woman's private part makes her mother and daughter forbidden (this is even stronger for actual zina). The third is an athar from Umar who looked at his slave girl's private part and then forbade her to his son, indicating that mere looking establishes prohibition. The passage then presents the Shafi'i view: zina does not establish any marriage prohibition. Their evidences include the same hadith about the child belonging to the bed (meaning no lineage or relationship from zina) and a specific hadith that 'the forbidden does not make the halal forbidden; only marriage makes things forbidden.' The Hanafi response, implied in the text, is that despite the child's lineage, the Prophet's order to Sawda to veil shows that zina does create some relationship. The Hanafi position is stronger because of the cumulative evidences.

Key Terms
حرمت مصاہرہ (hurmat musahara): Prohibition due to marriage affinity; relationships that become forbidden through marriage or, in Hanafi view, through zina.
مزنیہ (mazniyya): The woman with whom zina has been committed.
فراش (firash): The marital bed; the husband or the one who rightfully possesses the woman (e.g., owner of a slave girl). Used to establish lineage: 'al-walad li-l-firash' (the child belongs to the bed).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on a man marrying the mother of a woman with whom he has committed zina?
A) It is halal because zina does not create relationships.
B) It is haram permanently because zina establishes hurmat musahara.
C) It is makruh but not haram.
D) It is haram only if the woman was virgin.

Key Takeaway
Zina with a woman makes her mother and daughter permanently forbidden for the fornicator, based on the hadith of Sawda and other proofs.

Module 2 · Lesson 37

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
The Shafi'i Objection: Only Marriage Creates Prohibition
Shafi'i counter-argument and Hanafi response on hurmat musahara from zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Shafi'i argument that zina does not establish marriage prohibition, identify their key proofs, and evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal.

Core Idea
Zina does not make halal haram; only a valid nikah can create marriage prohibitions.

In the previous lesson we learned the Hanafi position. Now we turn to the Shafi'i objection. Imam al-Shafi'i and his followers argue that since zina is a sin and does not create any lawful bond, it cannot establish the permanent prohibitions of marriage (hurmat musahara). They cite explicit hadiths and the principle that a forbidden act cannot make permissible things forbidden. This lesson explores their evidence and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that if a man commits zina with a woman, her mother and daughter remain halal for him to marry. No prohibition arises from zina.
This is a clear difference from the Hanafi school.
2
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: 'al-walad li-l-firash'
The hadith of the boy from Sa'd and Abd ibn Zam'a includes the phrase 'al-walad li-l-firash wa li-l-'ahir al-hajar'. The Shafi'is interpret this to mean that the fornicator gets nothing — no lineage, no rights, and by extension no marriage prohibition.
They emphasize the exclusion clause.
3
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: 'la yuharrimu al-haram al-halal'
A specific hadith states that the forbidden (zina) does not make the halal forbidden; only marriage does. This is a direct textual argument against the Hanafi position.
This hadith is explicit and appears in Dar Qutni and Bayhaqi.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis respond that the order to Sawda to veil shows that zina does create a relationship affecting marriage, even if lineage is not established. The second hadith is interpreted to mean that the act of zina itself does not cause prohibition in the way that marriage does, but hurmat musahara is a separate ruling derived from the other proofs (mursal hadith, athar of Umar).
The Hanafi method is to give precedence to the specific evidence over general statements.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is significant: under Hanafi, the man can never marry the woman's mother or daughter; under Shafi'i, he can. This affects actual marriage contracts and family relations.
This is not merely academic; it has real consequences for Muslims.
