کیا اور زانی کو محروم کردیا اور فرمایا الولد للفراش وللعاهر الحجر (ج) (مسلم شریف ص ۴۷۰ نمبر ۱۳۵۷) جس کی وجہ سے مزنیہ کی ماں اور بیٹی زانی پر حرام نہیں ہوں گی (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة قالت سئل رسول الله الله عن رجل زنا بامرأة فاراد ان يتزوجها او ابنتها ، قال لا يحرم الحرام الحلال انما يحرم ما كان بنكاح ( و ) ( سنن دار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۸۸ نمبر ۳۶۳۸ سفن للبیہقی ، باب الز تالا حرم الحلال ج حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) آپ نے فرمایا یہ تمہارا بھائی ہے اے عبد بن زمعہ ا کیونکہ بچہ فراش والے کے لئے ہے اور زانی کو پتھر ہے۔ اور اے سودہ بنت زمعہ تم اس لڑکے سے پردہ کرو۔ کہتے ہیں کہ سودہ نے کبھی اس لڑکے کو نہیں دیکھا (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کسی نے کسی عورت کا فرج دیکھ لیا تو اس کے لئے اس عورت کی ماں حلال نہیں اور نہ اس کی بیٹی حلال ہے (ب) حضرت عمر نے اپنی باندی کا ستر کھولا پھر ان کے بعض بیٹے نے وہ باندی مانگی تو حضرت عمر نے فرمایا یہ باندی اب تیرے لئے حلال نہیں ہے (ج) بچہ بیوی والے کے لئے ہے اور زانی کے لئے پتھر ہے یعنی زانی سے نسب ثابت نہیں ہو گا (1) آپ سے ایک آدمی کے بارے میں پوچھا جس نے ایک عورت سے زنا کیا پھر اس سے شادی کرنا چاہتا ہے یا اس کی بیٹی سے شادی کرنا چاہتا ہے تو آپ نے فرما یا حرام یعنی زنا حلال چیز کو حرام نہیں کرتا، صرف نکاح کے ذریعہ حرام ہوگی۔
And whoever commits zina with a woman, her mother and her daughter are forbidden to him. For example, if someone committed zina with Zaynab, then Zaynab's mother becomes permanently forbidden to that man, and Zaynab's daughter also becomes permanently forbidden. Although zina is forbidden, still due to zina, a type of affinity (jinsiyya) is established. It is as if the mother of the woman with whom zina was committed becomes the mother-in-law due to the prohibition of musahara, and the daughter becomes the step-daughter and step-granddaughter (?) Therefore, marriage to them becomes permanently forbidden. (2) There is a reference to this in the hadith: On the authority of Aisha, she said: Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and Abd ibn Zam'a disputed about a boy. Sa'd said: O Messenger of Allah, this is the son of my brother Utba ibn Abi Waqqas; he pledged to me that he is his son; look at his resemblance. Abd ibn Zam'a said: This is my brother, O Messenger of Allah; he was born on my father's bed from his slave woman. The Messenger of Allah looked at his resemblance and saw a clear resemblance to Utba. He said: He is for you, O Abd; the child belongs to the bed, and for the fornicator is the stone. Veil from him, O Sawda bint Zam'a. She said: So he never saw her (i.e., Sawda veiled from him). (Muslim, chapter on the child belongs to the bed, no. 1457) In this hadith, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas claimed that the boy was his nephew because in the pre-Islamic period his brother Utba had committed zina with the mother. And look, the boy exactly resembles my brother. Abd ibn Zam'a claimed that the boy's mother was in his father's bed, so the boy is his brother. The Prophet attributed the boy's lineage to Zam'a because his mother was his bed. But he said to Zam'a's daughter, Sawda: In reality, this boy is not your brother, so you must veil from him. And she veiled from him for the rest of her life. This shows that zina creates a relationship with the fornicator and establishes the prohibition of musahara. (2) There is explicit mention in another hadith: On the authority of Abu Hani, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever looks at the private part of a woman, her mother and her daughter are not halal for him. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 6229; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, no. 13969) This mursal hadith indicates that if a man looks at the private part of a foreign woman, then the prohibition of musahara is established, and the woman's mother and daughter become forbidden to him. And if it is forbidden by mere looking, then by zina it is even more forbidden. (3) On the authority of Makhul: Umar uncovered his slave girl (i.e., looked at her private parts), and one of his sons asked for her. He said: She is not halal for you. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 16212) In this athar, Umar uncovered his slave girl and said to his son: She is no longer halal for you. This shows that mere touching (looking) establishes the prohibition of musahara. Now, Imam Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) says that committing zina or touching with desire does not establish the prohibition of musahara, and the mother and daughter of the woman with whom zina was committed are not forbidden to the fornicator. (1) The hadith from Muslim and Tirmidhi passed earlier that lineage is established for the one who has the bed and the fornicator is deprived: 'The child belongs to the bed, and for the fornicator is the stone.' Therefore, the mother and daughter of the woman with whom zina was committed are not forbidden to the fornicator. (2) Another hadith: On the authority of Aisha, she said: The Messenger of Allah was asked about a man who committed zina with a woman and then wanted to marry her or her daughter. He said: The forbidden does not make the halal forbidden; only marriage makes things forbidden. (Sunan Dar Qutni, vol. 3, no. 3638; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on zina does not make halal forbidden). Footnote: (from previous page) The Prophet said: He is your brother, O Abd ibn Zam'a, because the child belongs to the bed and the fornicator gets the stone. And O Sawda bint Zam'a, veil from this boy. They say Sawda never saw him. (a) The Prophet said: If someone looks at a woman's private part, then her mother and daughter are not halal for him. (b) Umar uncovered his slave girl's private parts; then one of his sons asked for that slave girl, and Umar said: This slave girl is no longer halal for you. (c) The child belongs to the wife and the fornicator gets the stone, meaning lineage is not established for the fornicator. (1) The Prophet was asked about a man who committed zina with a woman and then wants to marry her or her daughter. He said: The forbidden (zina) does not make the halal forbidden; only marriage makes things forbidden.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling that zina (fornication) with a woman establishes the same marriage prohibitions as a valid marriage (hurmat musahara). According to the Hanafi madhhab, if a man commits zina with a woman, her mother and her daughter become permanently forbidden to him, just as if he had married her. The commentary explains the reasoning: although zina is sinful, it creates a kind of relationship (jinsiyya) analogous to marriage, making the woman's mother his mother-in-law and her daughter his step-daughter. This is supported by several evidences. The first evidence is the hadith of Sa'd and Abd ibn Zam'a: the Prophet attributed the child to the husband (the owner of the bed) and said the fornicator gets nothing, but he still ordered Sawda to veil from the boy, recognizing a relationship due to zina. The second evidence is a mursal hadith that looking at a woman's private part makes her mother and daughter forbidden (this is even stronger for actual zina). The third is an athar from Umar who looked at his slave girl's private part and then forbade her to his son, indicating that mere looking establishes prohibition. The passage then presents the Shafi'i view: zina does not establish any marriage prohibition. Their evidences include the same hadith about the child belonging to the bed (meaning no lineage or relationship from zina) and a specific hadith that 'the forbidden does not make the halal forbidden; only marriage makes things forbidden.' The Hanafi response, implied in the text, is that despite the child's lineage, the Prophet's order to Sawda to veil shows that zina does create some relationship. The Hanafi position is stronger because of the cumulative evidences.

Key Terms
حرمت مصاہرہ (hurmat musahara): Prohibition due to marriage affinity; relationships that become forbidden through marriage or, in Hanafi view, through zina.
الولد للفراش وللعاهر الحجر (al-walad li-l-firash wa li-l-ahir al-hajar): The child belongs to the bed (the husband), and for the fornicator is the stone (i.e., nothing).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a Shafi'i evidence against hurmat musahara from zina?
A) The hadith ordering Sawda to veil from the boy.
B) The statement: 'The forbidden does not make the halal forbidden; only marriage makes things forbidden.'
C) The athar of Umar forbidding his slave girl to his son.
D) The mursal hadith about looking at private parts.

Key Takeaway
The Shafi'i school holds that zina creates no marriage prohibition, based on explicit hadiths; the Hanafi school disagrees, relying on the implication of other texts.

Does Zinā Create Mahramiyyat? The Hanafi–Shafi‘i Dispute
Hanafi vs Shafi‘i dispute on whether zinā creates affinity prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on mahramiyyat from zinā, identify the condition of shahwa, and evaluate the Shafi‘i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Zinā with desire makes the fornicator's marriage to the woman's mother and daughter haram.

This lesson examines a key disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi‘i schools: does unlawful intercourse (zinā) establish a permanent prohibition of affinity (hurmat al-musāhara)? The Hanafi school holds that it does, but only when accompanied by desire (shahwa) in the act or in looking/touching. The Shafi‘i school denies any such effect. We will explore the evidence each side presents and understand the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school rules that zinā, if accompanied by looking at the private part with desire or touching with desire, makes the fornicator's marriage to the woman's mother and daughter haram.
The condition of shahwa is crucial; without it, no prohibition arises.
2
Identify the Shafi‘i objection
Imam al-Shafi‘i holds that zinā creates no prohibition whatsoever; the fornicator may marry the woman’s mother or daughter.
3
Examine the Shafi‘i proofs and the Hanafi response
The Shafi‘is cite the hadith 'al-walad li al-firāsh' and the hadith from ‘Aishah. The Hanafis respond that the first is about lineage, not prohibition, and the second is mursal and weak. They present their own mursal hadith and the athar of ‘Umar and Ibrahim.
Hanafi usul gives weight to mursal hadith when supported by other evidence.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in the Hanafi view, a man who commits zinā with a woman cannot later marry her mother or daughter; in the Shafi‘i view, he can.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) آپ نے فرمایا یہ تمہارا بھائی ہے اے عبد بن زمعہ ا کیونکہ بچہ فراش والے کے لئے ہے اور زانی کو پتھر ہے۔ اور اے سودہ بنت زمعہ تم اس لڑکے سے پردہ کرو۔ کہتے ہیں کہ سودہ نے کبھی اس لڑکے کو نہیں دیکھا (الف) آپ نے فرمایا کسی نے کسی عورت کا فرج دیکھ لیا تو اس کے لئے اس عورت کی ماں حلال نہیں اور نہ اس کی بیٹی حلال ہے (ب) حضرت عمر نے اپنی باندی کا ستر کھولا پھر ان کے بعض بیٹے نے وہ باندی مانگی تو حضرت عمر نے فرمایا یہ باندی اب تیرے لئے حلال نہیں ہے (ج) بچہ بیوی والے کے لئے ہے اور زانی کے لئے پتھر ہے یعنی زانی سے نسب ثابت نہیں ہو گا (1) آپ سے ایک آدمی کے بارے میں پوچھا جس نے ایک عورت سے زنا کیا پھر اس سے شادی کرنا چاہتا ہے یا اس کی بیٹی سے شادی کرنا چاہتا ہے تو آپ نے فرما یا حرام یعنی زنا حلال چیز کو حرام نہیں کرتا، صرف نکاح کے ذریعہ حرام ہوگی۔

نوں علماء حنفیہ نے لکھا ہے کہ شہوت سے چھوٹے گا یا فرج داخل دیکھے گا تب مزینہ سے حرمت مصاہرت ثابت ہوگی ورنہ نہیں۔ ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ قال ابراهيم وكانوا يقولون : اذا اطلع الرجل على المرأة على ما لا تحل له او لمسها لشهوة فقد حرمتا عليه جميعا (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۴۹ الرجل يقع علی ام امرأته الخ ج ثالث ص ۴۶۹ ، نمبر ۱۶۲۳۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ شہوت سے چھوٹے گا تو حرام ہوگی۔
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on whether zinā (unlawful intercourse) establishes mahramiyyat (prohibition of marriage by affinity). The author begins by citing the famous hadith of the child belonging to the bed (al-walad li al-firāsh) to show that although the Prophet affirmed lineage to the husband of the bed, he commanded Sawdah to observe hijab from the boy, indicating a relationship due to zinā. The author then presents three Hanafi evidences: (1) a mursal hadith that looking at a woman's private part makes her mother and daughter forbidden; (2) the athar of 'Umar, who uncovered his slave-girl and forbade her to his son, showing that mere touching with desire establishes prohibition; and (3) the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha‘i that looking or touching with desire makes both women forbidden. The Shafi‘i position is presented next: zinā or even touching with desire does not create any prohibition, citing two hadith—the first emphasizing that the child belongs to the bed and the fornicator gets nothing, and the second from ‘Aishah that the Prophet said: 'What is unlawful does not make permissible unlawful; prohibition is only through marriage.' The Hanafi response is then given: the first hadith is about lineage, not prohibition; the second hadith is mursal and therefore weak. Moreover, the Hanafis qualify the ruling: merely looking without desire or touching without desire does not establish prohibition. Only when there is shahwa (sexual desire) does the prohibition take effect. Thus, the operative Hanafi position is that if a man commits zinā with a woman, or looks at her private part with desire, or touches her with desire, then her mother and daughter become haram for him to marry. The Shafi‘is maintain that no such prohibition arises.

Key Terms
حرمت مصاہرت (hurmat al-musāhara): Prohibition of marriage due to affinity, established by marriage or, in Hanafi view, by zinā with desire or looking/touching with desire.
زنا (zinā): Unlawful sexual intercourse. In this context, it is discussed as a potential cause of mahramiyyat.
فرج (farj): The private part. Looking at it with desire triggers prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what condition is necessary for zinā to establish mahramiyyat (prohibition of marriage) between the fornicator and the woman's mother or daughter?
A) The zinā must be witnessed by four witnesses.
B) The fornicator must have looked at the woman's private part or touched her with desire.
C) The woman must have been married.
D) The fornicator must have ejaculated.

Key Takeaway
Zinā only creates a prohibition of affinity in the Hanafi school if it involves desire in the act or in looking/touching; otherwise, no prohibition arises.

Marrying the Sister of a Ba'in-Divorced Wife During Iddah: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Ruling on marrying sister of ba'in-divorced wife during iddah with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on marrying the sister of a ba'in-divorced wife during iddah and explain the thamarah al-khilaf with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Even after a ba'in divorce, the iddah preserves a partial marital bond, making the sister prohibited.

This passage addresses a dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding whether a man may marry the sister of his wife during the wife's iddah after a ba'in divorce. Both schools rely on athar from the Sahaba, but differ in their interpretation of the legal status of a woman during iddah. The Hanafi view is that the woman remains a wife in certain aspects until iddah expires, while the Shafi'i view holds that the marriage is completely severed immediately.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling according to the Hanafi school: it is not permissible for a man to marry the sister of his wife during her iddah after a ba'in divorce. He must wait until the iddah expires.
The source begins with this ruling clearly.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is permissible to marry the sister during the iddah of the divorced wife, because a ba'in divorce severs all marital ties immediately.
The text explicitly compares the two positions.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: athar from Urwa ibn Zubayr and Qasim ibn Muhammad stating that a man may marry a fifth woman or the sister immediately after a ba'in divorce without waiting for iddah.
The opponent's dalil is based on the complete severance of the marriage.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: during iddah, the woman still receives nafaqah and cannot leave the house without permission, so she is still considered a wife 'min wajh' (from some aspect). Therefore, marrying the sister is prohibited as if the divorce had not occurred.
The Hanafi response focuses on the residual legal effects of iddah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: under Hanafi law, a man must wait for iddah to end before marrying the sister; under Shafi'i law, he may marry her immediately. This affects the validity of a marriage contracted during iddah.
The difference is not merely theoretical; it impacts actual marriage contracts.

(الف) حضرت علی نے فرمایا پانچویں عورت سے شادی نہ کرے یہاں تک کہ اس کی عدت گزر جائے جس کو طلاق دی ہے ( ب ) حضرت عمر بن شعیب نے کہا کہ ایک آدمی نے طلاق دی پھر اس کی بہن سے شادی کی تو ابن عباس نے مروان سے کہا دونوں میں جدائیگی کر دو یہاں تک کہ جس کو طلاق دی ہے اس کی عدت گزر جائے۔ ان عروة بن زبیر والقاسم بن محمد كانا يقولان في الرجل تكون عنده ا ده اربع نسوة فيطلق احداهن البتة انه يتزوج اذا شاء ولا ينتظر حتى تمضى عدتها (الف) (سن للبیهقی ، باب الرجل يطلق اربع نسوة له طلاقا با ناحل له ان تنکح مكانهن اربعاج سابع ص ۲۴۲۳ نمبر ۱۳۸۵۰/ مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۱۸ امن قال لابأس ان بیتز وج الخامسة قبل انقضاء عدة التی طلق ج ثالث جس ۵۱۷ نمبر ۱۶۷۴۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ طلاق بائن دی ہو تو اس کی عدت گزرنے سے پہلے پانچویں عورت سے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ اور اس کی بہن سے بھی شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ وہ گویا کہ بہت سے احکام میں بیوی نہیں رہی۔ حاشیہ : (الف) عروہ بن زبیر اور قاسم بن محمد فرماتے تھے کہ کوئی آدمی کے پاس چار بیویاں ہوں پھر ایک کو بائنہ طلاق دے تو وہ شادی کر سکتا ہے جب چاہے۔ اور اس کی عدت گزرنے کا انتظار نہ کرے
And if a man divorces his wife with a ba'in divorce, it is not permissible for him to marry her sister until [the iddah expires]. This hadith shows that zina does not establish prohibition by marriage affinity (hurmat musaharat), because zina is haram and haram cannot make a halal woman haram. Prohibition is only through valid marriage. The Hanafi scholars have written that if he touches with desire or looks at the private part with desire, then prohibition by affinity is established from zina, otherwise not. Their evidence is this athar: Ibrahim said, they used to say: if a man looks at a woman in a way that is not permissible for him or touches her with desire, both become forbidden to him. From this athar it is understood that if he touches with desire, she becomes haram. [1746](21) If a husband gives his wife a ba'in divorce, it is not permissible for him to marry her sister until her iddah passes. Explanation: The husband gave a ba'in divorce, whether one or three. If the iddah has not passed and he wants to marry her sister, he cannot until the iddah of that wife completely ends and she is fully separated. (1) As long as the iddah remains, the wife receives nafaqah for iddah from the husband and cannot leave the house without his permission, because she is observing iddah for him. So in a way she is still a wife during iddah, and since she is a wife, he cannot marry her sister. (2) Evidence of this: from Ali: 'He should not marry a fifth until the iddah of the one he divorced passes.' (3) From Umar ibn Shuaib: 'A man divorced a woman then married her sister. Ibn Abbas said to Marwan: separate them until the iddah of the divorced woman passes.' From this athar it is understood that if he has four wives and divorces one with ba'in, he cannot marry a fifth until her iddah passes, and similarly he cannot marry her sister. Benefit: Imam al-Shafi'i says that if he gave a ba'in or a severe (mugallazah) divorce, he can marry her sister during iddah, or if he divorced the fourth, he can marry a fifth during iddah. He says that in ba'in and mugallazah divorce, the woman is cut off from the husband even if iddah has not passed, so he can marry her sister. (Footnote: (a) Ali said: do not marry a fifth woman until the iddah of the one you divorced passes. (b) Umar ibn Shuaib said: a man divorced then married her sister, so Ibn Abbas said to Marwan: separate them until the iddah of the divorced woman passes.) And the narration of Urwa ibn Zubayr and Qasim ibn Muhammad: they used to say about a man who has four wives and divorces one absolutely, that he may marry whenever he wishes and not wait for her iddah to end. From this athar it is understood that if he gave a ba'in divorce, he can marry a fifth woman before her iddah ends, and also her sister, because she is no longer a wife in many rulings. (Footnote: (a) Urwa ibn Zubayr and Qasim ibn Muhammad used to say: a man who has four wives and divorces one with ba'in talaq may marry when he wishes and not wait for her iddah to pass.)
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the permissibility of marrying the sister of a woman who has been given a ba'in divorce during the latter's iddah. The Hanafi position, supported by ahadith from Ali and Ibn Abbas, is that it is prohibited because during iddah the woman is still considered a wife in some aspects (she receives nafaqah, cannot leave the house). The commentator explains that even after a ba'in divorce, the marital bond is not completely severed until iddah expires. Imam Shafi'i argues that ba'in divorce severs all ties immediately, so the sister may be married during iddah. The Hanafi response points to the continued obligations (nafaqah, residence) as evidence that the woman remains partially a wife. This difference leads to practical consequences: under Hanafi law, one must wait for iddah; under Shafi'i, one may marry immediately. The relied-upon position is the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that severs marital ties immediately, but the wife observes iddah.
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death before remarrying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when may a husband marry the sister of a woman he has divorced with a ba'in talaq?
A) Immediately after the divorce, as the marriage is severed
B) Only after the iddah of the divorced wife has expired
C) He may never marry the sister
D) Only if the divorced wife consents

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits marrying the sister of a ba'in-divorced wife until her iddah expires, due to the partial marital bond that persists during iddah.

Ruling on Master Marrying His Slave Woman
Ruling that a master cannot marry his own slave woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a master marrying his own slave woman and explain the reasoning based on milk al-yamin.

Core Idea
Ownership and marriage cannot combine: a master cannot marry his slave woman.

In this passage, Al-Sharh al-Sameri states a clear ruling: a master is not permitted to marry his own female slave. While this may seem surprising to some, the Hanafi reasoning is grounded in the legal consequences of milk al-yamin (right hand possession). Understanding this ruling helps clarify the boundaries between ownership and marriage in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? A master marrying his own slave woman. State the ruling: it is not permissible (haram).
In Hanafi fiqh, 'not permissible' generally means haram (prohibited).
2
Understand the reasoning
Why is it not permissible? Because the master already has the right of intimacy via ownership, and marriage would grant the wife rights (e.g., nafaqah, inheritance) that conflict with ownership.
The passage states: 'marriage brings rights that a slave cannot have.'
3
Distinguish between one's own slave and another's slave
This ruling applies only to one's own slave. Marrying another person's slave woman is permissible with the owner's permission, as she is not owned by the husband.
The prohibition is specific to milk al-yamin of the husband.
4
Apply the principle of milk al-yamin
Ownership grants the right to intimacy without a marriage contract. Therefore, marriage is unnecessary and legally problematic because it would create incompatible rights.
The master can have relations without marriage, so marriage adds nothing but conflicts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۷۴۷ (۲۲) اور مولی کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ اپنی باندی سے شادی کرے۔ مولی اپنی باندی سے بغیر شادی کے بھی صحبت کر سکتا ہے تو اس سے شادی کرنے کی کیا ضرورت ہے (۲) شادی میں بیوی حقوق وصول کرنے میں شوہر کے قریب ہو جاتی ہے جبکہ مملوکہ اس طرح نہیں کر سکتی۔ اس لئے مملوکہ سے کیسے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔
[1747] (22) And it is not permissible for a master to marry his slave woman. A master can have intercourse with his slave woman without marriage, so what need is there to marry her? (2) In marriage, the wife becomes close to the husband in obtaining rights, while a female slave cannot do so. Therefore, how can he marry a female slave?
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This is a ruling statement: a master (mawla) is not permitted to marry his own slave woman (amat). The reasoning is straightforward: since the master already has the right of ownership (milk al-yamin), which permits intimacy without marriage, marriage would introduce unnecessary complications. Marriage elevates the wife to a status of equality in certain rights (e.g., nafaqah, inheritance), which is incompatible with the slave's status of ownership. Therefore, the marriage is not valid. This ruling is specific to one's own slave; marrying another's slave woman is permissible under certain conditions.

Key Terms
مولی (mawla): The master or owner of a slave.
باندی (bandi): A female slave owned by a master.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why may a master not marry his own slave woman according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because it is disliked but not prohibited
B) Because he already has the right of ownership and intimacy without marriage, and marriage would create incompatible rights
C) Because the slave woman must consent, and she usually does not
D) Because it would make her free immediately

Key Takeaway
A master cannot marry his own slave woman because the rights of ownership and marriage are incompatible in Hanafi law.

Ruling on a Free Woman Marrying Her Own Slave
Ruling that a free woman cannot marry her male slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a free woman marrying her male slave and explain the legal reasoning (dalil) from the athar of Umar ibn al-Khattab.

Core Idea
A free woman cannot marry her own slave – incompatible statuses invalidate the marriage.

This lesson examines a specific prohibition in Hanafi marriage law: a free woman marrying her male slave. The passage presents the ruling and supports it with an athar (practice) of Caliph Umar. We will analyze the legal basis for this prohibition and understand the underlying rationale regarding status and authority in marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a free woman (sayyidah) contracting marriage with her own male slave (ghulam). The ruling is that it is not permissible (ghayr ja'iz), i.e., haram/invalid.
2
Understand the rationale
The slave is owned (mamluk) with limited rights; making him a husband contradicts his status as owned and requires him to be a qawwam (provider/leader), which is incompatible.
3
Examine the dalil
The passage cites an athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab: he punished a woman who did this, separated them, and forbade her from marrying others as a punishment.
4
Derive the legal principle
The athar establishes the prohibition and shows that such a marriage is not only invalid but also incurs a punitive measure.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dimension
Some scholars may allow it under certain conditions, but the Hanafi school holds it as impermissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۷۴۸ (۲۳) اور نہ عورت اپنے غلام سے شادی کرے۔ تشریح سیدہ اور آقا کے پاس اپنا غلام ہے۔ سیدہ اس سے شادی کرنا چاہے تو جائز نہیں ہے۔ غلام مملوک ہے اس لئے اس کا حق بہت کم ہے۔ اگر اس کو شوہر بنائے گی تو ایک اندازے میں مالک اور قوام بنانا پڑے گا جو ملوکیت کے خلاف ہے۔ اس لئے سیدہ اپنے غلام سے نکاح نہیں کر سکتی (۲) اثر میں ہے ان عمر بن الخطاب اتي بامرأة قد تزوجت عبدها فعاقبها وفرق بينها و بين عبدها وحرم عليها الازواج عقوبة لها (ب) ( سن اليقی ، باب النكاح و ملک الیمین لا يجتمعان ج سابع ص ۲۰۶، نمبر ۱۳۷۳۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ سیدہ اور غلام کی شادی جائز نہیں ہے۔
[1748] (23) And a woman should not marry her slave. Explanation: A mistress (sayyidah) and master has her own slave. If the mistress wants to marry him, it is not permissible. The slave is owned so his rights are very few. If she makes him a husband, she would in a sense have to make him a master and qawwam (provider), which contradicts his status as owned. Therefore, a mistress cannot marry her slave. (2) There is an athar that Umar ibn al-Khattab was brought a woman who had married her slave; he punished her, separated them, and prohibited marriage to her as a punishment. This athar shows that marriage between a mistress and her slave is not permissible.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This is a ruling statement: a free woman (sayyidah) cannot marry her male slave (‘abd). The explanation given is that the slave's low status as a maamluk (owned) conflicts with the marital role of a husband, who is expected to be a qawwam (provider and leader). Marrying a slave would invert the natural hierarchy. The text also quotes an athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab who punished a woman who married her slave, separated them, and forbade her from marrying others as a punishment. This hadith is cited as evidence for the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
غلام (ghulam): A male slave owned by a free person.
سیدہ (sayyidah): A free mistress who owns a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the punishment given by Umar ibn al-Khattab to the woman who married her slave, as cited in the text?
A) He allowed the marriage but set the slave free
B) He separated them and forbade her from marrying others as a punishment
C) He ordered her to pay a fine
D) He declared the marriage valid but voidable

Key Takeaway
A free woman cannot marry her male slave because the marriage would combine ownership with marital authority, which is legally invalid; the athar of Umar supports this prohibition.

Ruling on Marrying Kitabiyyah
Ruling with proof on marrying kitabiyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a kitabiyyah and explain the Quranic evidence and the basis for its disliked status.

Core Idea
Marrying a kitabiyyah is permissible but discouraged to protect religious harmony.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on marriage to Jewish and Christian women (kitabiyyah). The text presents the ruling as permissible (ja'iz) but 'not good,' meaning it is disliked (makruh tanzihan). We will explore the Quranic evidence and the reasoning behind the discouragement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon—marriage to a kitabiyyah—and the hukm level. The text says it is ja'iz (permissible) but 'not good,' indicating makruh tanzihan.
The ruling is not simply mubah; it carries a dislikedness due to potential harms.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: Quran 5:5, which explicitly permits marriage to chaste women from the People of the Book.
The verse is quoted in part; the full text is provided in the footnote.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the verse proves permissibility. The operative phrase 'muhsinat min alladhina utu al-kitab' establishes the ruling for kitabiyyah.
The condition of chastity and payment of mahr is also derived from the verse.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that while the Hanafi school permits, other schools have restrictions. The text does not elaborate, but the ruling is mukhtalaf fih.
This lesson focuses on the Hanafi position as stated.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Understand that the mufta bihi is permissibility with dislike. The text does not cite a specific tarjih authority but reflects the standard Hanafi view.
The dislike is based on considerations of religious well-being.

Source Text

۱۷۴۹ (۲۴) اور جائز ہے کتابیہ سے نکاح کرنا۔ تشریح کتابیہ سے مراد یہود یہ اور نصرانیہ عورتیں ہیں ۔ ان لوگوں سے شادی کرنا جائز ہے بشرطیکہ واقعی اہل کتاب ہو، دہر یہ نہ ہو۔ لیکن پھر بھی اچھا نہیں ہے۔ جواز کی دلیل آیت ہے۔ والمحصنات من المؤمنات والمحصنات من الذى اوتوا الكتاب من قبلكم اذا اتيتموهن اجورهن (ج) (آیت ۵ سورۃ المائدۃ (۵) اس آیت میں اہل کتاب عورت سے نکاح حلال قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ لیکن اچھا اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ حاشیه : (ج) اور پاکدامن مؤمن عورتیں اور پاکدامن وہ عورتیں جن کو تم سے پہلے کتاب دی گئی ہو جب ان کو اس کا مہر دے دو تو نکاح جائز ہے۔
[1749] (24) And it is permissible to marry a kitabiyyah. Explanation: Kitabiyyah refers to Jewish and Christian women. Marrying them is permissible provided they are truly People of the Book, not atheists. But still it is not good. The evidence for permissibility is the verse: 'And the chaste women from among the believers and the chaste women from among those who were given the Scripture before you, when you have given them their due bridal money...' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:5). This verse made marriage to women of the Book lawful. But it is not good because... (Footnote: (j) And chaste believing women and chaste women of those given the Scripture before you, when you give them their dowries, marriage is permissible.)
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding marriage to kitabiyyah (Jewish and Christian women). The text states it is permissible (ja'iz) but not preferred (achha nahi, i.e., makruh tanzihan). The permissibility is derived from the Quranic verse in Surah al-Ma'idah (5:5), which explicitly permits marriage to chaste women from the People of the Book. The condition is that they are genuine People of the Book (ahl al-kitab), not dahriyyah (atheists) or those who reject scripture. The 'not good' aspect likely refers to concerns about religious compatibility and potential negative influence on children. The footnote provides the full wording of the verse.

Key Terms
کتابیہ (kitabiyyah): A woman from the People of the Book, i.e., Jewish or Christian.
اہل کتاب (ahl al-kitab): Those who follow a revealed scripture, specifically Jews and Christians.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Haram (forbidden)
B) Mustahab (recommended)
C) Mubah (permissible) but 'not good' (makruh tanzihan)
D) Wajib (obligatory) if one desires religious diversity

Key Takeaway
Marrying a kitabiyyah is permissible (mubah) but discouraged (makruh tanzihan) due to concerns for religious harmony; the permissibility is grounded in Quran 5:5.

Marrying the Fifth Wife Before Iddah of Ba'in Talaq
Ruling on marrying the fifth wife before iddah of ba'in talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a fifth woman before the iddah of a ba'in talaq and explain the proof from the athar.

Core Idea
A ba'in divorce severs the marriage, so no waiting for iddah to remarry.

The ruling on when a man with four wives can marry a fifth after divorcing one may seem strict, but the Hanafi school holds that an irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) completely ends the marriage. In this lesson, we examine an athar from Urwa ibn al-Zubayr and al-Qasim ibn Muhammad that permits immediate remarriage without waiting for the divorced wife's iddah. This ruling highlights the legal effect of ba'in talaq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon and what the hukm (legal classification) is. The act is marrying a fifth woman after giving a ba'in talaq to one of four wives. The ruling is mubah (permissible).
The hukm level is based on the absence of prohibition as shown by the athar.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited. The passage quotes an athar from Urwa ibn al-Zubayr and al-Qasim ibn Muhammad recorded in Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
This is a Sunnah-type proof (qawl al-sahabi/athar).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the dalil proves the ruling. The athar explicitly states 'he may marry when he wishes and does not wait until her iddah passes', indicating that the iddah does not create an impediment for the husband to marry another woman.
The key phrase 'wa la yantazir hatta tamdiya iddatuha' is the operative part.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify any disagreement. The Shafi'i school holds that the husband must wait for the iddah to expire before marrying a new woman, based on general iddah verses.
The cross-madhhab difference is rooted in the interpretation of the iddah's purpose.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Consider why the Hanafi position is preferred. The athar provides specific guidance, and the rationale is that ba'in talaq completely severs the marital bond, so the woman is like a stranger regarding remarriage by the husband.
This ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شادی کر سکتا ہے (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ ان عروة بن زبیر والقاسم بن محمد كانا يقولان في الرجل تكون عنده ا ده اربع نسوة فيطلق احداهن البتة انه يتزوج اذا شاء ولا ينتظر حتى تمضى عدتها (الف) (سن للبیہقی ، باب الرجل يطلق اربع نسوة له طلاقا با ناحل له ان تنكح مكانهن اربعاج سابع ص ۲۴۲۳ نمبر ۱۳۸۵۰/ مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۱۸ امن قال لابأس ان بیتز وج الخامسة قبل انقضاء عدة التی طلق ج ثالث جس ۵۱۷ نمبر ۱۶۷۴۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ طلاق بائن دی ہو تو اس کی عدت گزرنے سے پہلے پانچویں عورت سے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ اور اس کی بہن سے بھی شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ وہ گویا کہ بہت سے احکام میں بیوی نہیں رہی۔
He can marry. (2) There is proof of this in the athar. Indeed, Urwa ibn al-Zubayr and al-Qasim ibn Muhammad used to say about a man who has four wives and divorces one of them irrevocably (al-batta), that he may marry when he wishes and does not wait until her iddah passes. (a) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on a man divorcing his four wives irrevocably...; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, ...) From this athar it is understood that if a ba'in talaq is given, he can marry a fifth woman before her iddah passes. And he can also marry her sister. Because she is no longer a wife in many rulings.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling based on an athar (report from the Companions). The ruling states that when a man has four wives and gives one a ba'in (irrevocable) talaq, he may immediately marry another woman without waiting for her iddah to expire. This is because the ba'in talaq severs the marital relationship completely, so the divorced woman is like a stranger in terms of remarriage for the husband. The athar from Urwa ibn al-Zubayr and al-Qasim ibn Muhammad supports this. The author also notes that this extends to marrying the sister of the divorced woman, since the prohibition due to being in-laws is no longer applicable.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately, so the husband cannot take back his wife without a new marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) After her iddah expires
B) Immediately, without waiting for iddah
C) Only after one year
D) He cannot marry any more because he already has four

Key Takeaway
A ba'in talaq completely ends the marriage, so the husband is free to marry another woman immediately, even before the divorced wife's iddah ends.

Prohibition of Master Marrying His Slave Woman or Woman Marrying Her Slave
Ruling on prohibition of marriage between master and slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage between a master and his own slave woman, explain the rationale, and identify the evidence from the athar of Umar ibn al-Khattab.

Core Idea
A master cannot marry his own slave woman because ownership already grants intimacy, and marriage clashes with ownership rights.

This lesson covers a specific prohibition in Hanafi fiqh: a master marrying his own slave woman, and a free woman marrying her male slave. The ruling is based on the conflict between the rights of ownership and the rights of marriage. The proof is provided through the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who punished a woman for marrying her slave and separated them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states it is not permissible (jā'iz) for a master to marry his own female slave, and similarly not for a free woman to marry her male slave. Note that the prohibition applies while ownership exists.
This is a clear, unconditional prohibition.
2
Understand the rationale (illah)
The master already has the right to intimacy with his slave woman without marriage. Marriage would give her increased rights (like inheritance, maintenance) that conflict with her status as owned property. Similarly, a woman making her slave her husband would elevate him to a guardian role, contradicting his owned status.
The underlying cause is the incompatibility of ownership and marriage in the same relationship.
3
Examine the dalil (evidence)
The author cites an athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab (reported in Sunan al-Bayhaqi): a woman who married her slave was brought to Umar; he punished her, separated them, and forbade her from marrying as punishment.
This is a Sunnah ahad (single narration) with zanni thubut and zanni dalala, but accepted in the school.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Umar's action of punishing and annulling the marriage indicates the act is prohibited (haram) and invalid. The separation and punishment show explicit disapproval and serve as a precedent.
The Hanafi school relies on this as a strong indicator of prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور مولی کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ اپنی باندی سے شادی کرے۔ مولی اپنی باندی سے بغیر شادی کے بھی صحبت کر سکتا ہے تو اس سے شادی کرنے کی کیا ضرورت ہے (۲) شادی میں بیوی حقوق وصول کرنے میں شوہر کے قریب ہو جاتی ہے جبکہ مملوکہ اس طرح نہیں کر سکتی۔ اس لئے مملوکہ سے کیسے شادی کر سکتا ہے۔ [۱۷۴۸] (۲۳) اور نہ عورت اپنے غلام سے شادی کرے۔ تشریح سیدہ اور آقا کے پاس اپنا غلام ہے۔ سیدہ اس سے شادی کرنا چاہے تو جائز نہیں ہے۔ غلام مملوک ہے اس لئے اس کا حق بہت کم ہے۔ اگر اس کو شوہر بنائے گی تو ایک اندازے میں مالک اور قوام بنانا پڑے گا جو ملوکیت کے خلاف ہے۔ اس لئے سیدہ اپنے غلام سے نکاح نہیں کر سکتی (۲) اثر میں ہے ان عمر بن الخطاب اتي بامرأة قد تزوجت عبدها فعاقبها وفرق بينها و بين عبدها وحرم عليها الازواج عقوبة لها (ب) ( سن اليقی ، باب النكاح و ملک الیمین لا يجتمعان ج سابع ص ۲۰۶، نمبر ۱۳۷۳۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ سیدہ اور غلام کی شادی جائز نہیں ہے۔
And it is not permissible for a master to marry his own slave woman. The master can have intercourse with his slave woman without marriage, so what need is there to marry her? (2) In marriage, the wife becomes close to the husband in claiming rights, whereas the female slave cannot do that. So how can he marry a slave woman? [1748] (23) And also a woman cannot marry her own slave. Explanation: A mistress has her own slave. If the mistress wishes to marry him, it is not permissible. The slave is owned, so his right is very little. If she makes him her husband, she would have to make him a master and guardian in a way, which contradicts ownership. Therefore, a mistress cannot marry her slave. (2) There is an athar: Umar ibn al-Khattab was brought a woman who had married her slave, so he punished her, separated between her and her slave, and forbade her from marrying as a punishment. (b) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi...) This athar indicates that marriage between a mistress and her slave is not permissible.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling that marriage between a master and his own slave is prohibited. The reasoning is that the master already has the right of intercourse with his slave woman without marriage, and marriage would elevate her to a status conflicting with ownership. Similarly, a free woman cannot marry her own male slave because it would contradict his status as owned property; she would be making her property a guardian over her. The athar from Umar provides a precedent where such marriage was punished and annulled.

Key Terms
مولي (mawla): Master or owner, referring to the male owner of a slave woman.
سيده (sayyidah): Mistress, female owner of a male slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Umar ibn al-Khattab do when a woman married her own slave?
A) He allowed the marriage
B) He praised her
C) He punished her and separated them
D) He ignored the matter

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school absolutely prohibits marriage between a person and his/her own slave based on the incompatibility of ownership and marriage, supported by the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab.

Marriage with Kitabi Women and Prohibition for Muslim Women
Ruling on marrying Kitabi women and prohibition of Muslim woman marrying Kitabi man

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Muslim men marrying Kitabi women, identify the Quranic proof, and explain why Muslim women are absolutely prohibited from marrying non-Muslim men.

Core Idea
Muslim men may marry Kitabi women but it is discouraged; Muslim women may never marry non-Muslim men.

This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on interfaith marriage: permissible for men with discouragement, prohibited for women. The primary proof is Quran 5:5, but the school also relies on Companion practice to restrict the permission. We also examine the critical distinction of who qualifies as a 'Kitabi'—a point that has implications for contemporary Muslim communities in non-Muslim societies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the passage
Distinguish the ruling for Muslim men (permissible but discouraged) and for Muslim women (prohibited). Note the different authority levels: Quran for men, ijma' for women.
The prohibition for women is unanimous across schools.
2
Analyze the primary dalil for men – Quran 5:5
Locate the verse citation in the passage. Identify the operative phrase (المحصنات من الذين أوتوا الكتاب) and how it grants permission. Note the Hanafi understanding that this permission is permissive (mubah) not obligatory.
The verse uses 'halal' (lawful) language, indicating permissibility.
3
Examine the reports from Umar that discourage the practice
The passage includes athar from Umar and Hudhayfa. Understand that these reports shift the ruling from pure mubah to makruh tanzih (discouraged) due to fear of religious influence on the household.
These reports are used by Hanafis to qualify the initial permission.
4
Understand the Kitabi qualification for Arab Christians
The passage cites Ata and others that Arab Christians are not from the People of the Book. Apply this to modern contexts: European Christians may be considered Kitabi, but the status must be verified. This adds a condition to the permissibility.
This is a minority view within Hanafis; the majority still accept Arab Christians as Kitabi.
5
Distill the prohibition for Muslim women
The passage explicitly states that Muslim women cannot marry Kitabi men. The proof is the verse's wording (women from those given the Book) implying permission only for men, plus ijma' and the report of Umar.
The prohibition is absolute and not subject to discouragement.

خالص آوارہ گردی ہے۔ اور ان سے شادی کرنا کیسے جائز ہوگا ؟ قال عطاء ليس نصارى العرب باهل الكتاب انما اهل الكتاب بنو اسرائيل والذين جائتهم التوراة والانجـيـل فـامـا مـن دخل فيهم من الناس فليسوا منهم قال الشيخ وقدروينا عن عمر و على في نصاري العرب بمعنى هذا وانه لا توكل ذبائحهم (ب) ( سنن للبیہقی ، باب ما جاء فی تحریم حرائر اهل الشرك دون اهل الكتاب ج سابع ص ۲۸۱، نمبر ۱۳۹۸۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بنی ينكح النصرانية ولا ينكح النصارني المسلمة ( نمبر ۱۳۹۸۵) اور اسی باب میں ہے سمع جابر بن عبد الله ... .... ونساء هم لنا لنا حل ونساء نا عليهم حرام (ج) (سنن للبیہقی ، باب ما جاء فی تحریم حرائر اہل الشرک And it is permissible to marry a Kitabi woman. Kitabi refers to Jewish and Christian women. Marrying them is permissible provided they are truly from the People of the Book, not atheists. But still, it is not commendable. The proof of permissibility is the verse: 'And chaste women from among the believers and chaste women from among those who were given the Scripture before you, when you have given them their due compensation.' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:5) This verse makes marriage with a Kitabi woman lawful. But it is not commendable because if a Jewish or Christian woman enters the home, the whole household will become Jewish or Christian, as indicated by Umar when he wrote to Hudhayfa about divorcing his Jewish wife... From this athar it is understood that one should not marry Kitabi women. And some Companions did not even consider Arab Christians as People of the Book, so how can European Christians be considered? ... Ata said: The Arab Christians are not from the People of the Book; the People of the Book are the Children of Israel who received the Torah and Gospel. As for those who entered among them, they are not from them. ... From this athar it is understood that Jews or Christians outside the family of Children of Israel are not considered as People of the Book for marriage. However, if a Muslim woman marries a Christian or Jewish man, it is not permissible. The verse says 'women from those who were given the Scripture before you', meaning marriage with a Kitabi woman is permitted, so a Muslim woman marrying a Kitabi man is not permissible. Umar ibn al-Khattab wrote: 'A Muslim man may marry a Christian woman, but a Christian man may not marry a Muslim woman.' ... From this athar it is understood that a Muslim woman cannot marry a Kitabi man.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage discusses two separate but related rulings: first, the permissibility of Muslim men marrying Kitabi women, and second, the prohibition of Muslim women marrying Kitabi men. The author presents the Quranic verse as primary evidence for permissibility for men, but then introduces several athar (reports) from the Companions that discourage the practice, citing concerns about religious influence. A significant point is the discussion about Arab Christians: some authorities, including Ata and the early scholars, did not consider Arab Christians as true People of the Book, thus their women are not permissible to marry. The passage also clarifies that the permissibility is specific to Muslim men; Muslim women are absolutely prohibited from marrying non-Muslim men, regardless of their scriptural status.

Key Terms
كتابية (kitabiyyah): A woman from the People of the Book (Jewish or Christian) who follows a revealed scripture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is the basis for discouraging Muslim men from marrying Kitabi women?
A) The Quranic verse abrogated the permission
B) The risk that the household may adopt non-Muslim practices
C) It is prohibited in the Hadith
D) Kitabi women are not chaste

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits Muslim men to marry Kitabi women but discourages it, and absolutely prohibits Muslim women from marrying non-Muslim men.

Prohibition of Marrying Magian and Idolatrous Women
Ruling on prohibiting marriage with Magians and idolaters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying Magian and idolatrous women and explain the legal reasoning based on their status as non-Ahl al-Kitab.

Core Idea
Marriage to Magian and idolatrous women is absolutely prohibited in the Hanafi school.

This passage addresses a specific question in the law of marriage (nikah): which non-Muslim women are permissible to marry? The Hanafi school is clear that only Kitabi women (Jews and Christians) are allowed, and even then it is discouraged. Magians (Zoroastrians) and idolaters (e.g., Hindus, Buddhists) are not considered People of the Book, so marriage to them is invalid and forbidden.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The passage rules on the act of marrying (nikah) two categories of women: Magians (fire-worshippers) and idolaters (statue-worshippers). The ruling is clear: it is not permissible (jā'iz). In Hanafi terms, this is haram.
The verb 'jā'iz' in negative form indicates prohibition.
2
Understand the reasoning for Magians
The passage explains that Magians worship fire, which makes them idolaters (mushrikūn) and disbelievers. Since they are not from the People of the Book (Ahl al-Kitāb), the general prohibition against marrying idolaters (Qur'an 2:221) applies.
The Hanafi school does not accept the Zoroastrian scripture as divinely revealed in its current form.
3
Recognize the exception for Kitabis
By implication, the prohibition does not extend to Jewish and Christian women, who are permitted (though makruh tanzihan) according to the Hanafi school. This passage contrasts with that exception.
The Qur'an explicitly permits marrying chaste women from the People of the Book (5:5).
4
Consider the legal consequence
If a marriage contract is conducted with a Magian or idolatress, it is invalid (bāṭil). The couple must separate immediately, and any children are considered illegitimate.
This differs from a fasid contract, which may be rectified; batil is void from the start.
5
Address a common misconception
Some may argue that Magians have a scripture (the Avesta) and should be treated like Ahl al-Kitab. The Hanafi response: their scripture has been altered and they are not recognized as monotheists in the Islamic sense.
The Prophet ﷺ treated Magians as non-Kitabis, taking jizya from them but not permitting intermarriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور نہیں جائز ہے نکاح آتش پرست عورتوں سے اور بت پرست عورتوں سے۔ مجوسی لوگ آگ کی پوجا کرتے ہیں اس لئے یہ بت پرست اور کافر ہوئے۔ اس لئے ان کی عورتوں سے نکاح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
And it is not permissible to marry fire-worshipping women and idol-worshipping women. Magians worship fire, so they are idolaters and disbelievers. Therefore, marrying their women is not permissible.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage states the prohibition of marrying women who are Magians (Zoroastrians) or idolaters. The reasoning is that they are polytheists and disbelievers, not from the People of the Book. The Hanafi school is clear that only marriage with Kitabi women (Jews and Christians) is permissible, and even then discouraged. Magians and idolaters are not considered Ahl al-Kitab, so their marriage is invalid.

Key Terms
مجوس (majus): Magians, Zoroastrians, fire-worshippers.
وثنيات (wathaniyyat): Idolatresses, women who worship idols.

Key Takeaway
Marriage to Magian and idolatrous women is invalid (bāṭil) in the Hanafi school because they are not from the People of the Book.

Marriage to Majus and Idolaters is Prohibited
States ruling and provides proofs from hadith and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying Majus and idolatrous women and cite the proofs from the text, including the athar of Umar and the statement of Ata.

Core Idea
Marriage to Magians and idolaters is haram; only original Kitabiyyat are permissible under strict conditions.

This passage establishes a clear prohibition: marrying a woman from the Magian (fire-worshipping) or idolatrous religion is not allowed. The author supports this ruling with several reports from the Companions and early scholars, showing that even marriage to Jewish and Christian women is subject to restrictions. As you study this lesson, you will learn the exact ruling, the proofs from hadith and athar, and the nuanced condition that not all Christians are considered People of the Book.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the legal classification is. The act is marrying a Magian or idolatrous woman; the ruling is explicitly 'la yajuz' (not permissible) – intellectually a prohibition.
Note that the text combines both groups (Majus and idolaters) under the same prohibition.
2
Locate the primary proofs (dalil)
Find the evidence cited by the author. It includes: (1) the story of Hudhayfah marrying a Jewish woman and Umar's order to separate, (2) Ata's statement that Arab Christians are not true People of the Book, (3) a report from Umar permitting Muslim men to marry Christian women but not vice versa, and (4) a quote from Jabir and the Quranic verse about Kitabiyyat.
The proofs are a mix of Quranic citation and athar (reports from Companions).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how each proof supports the ruling)
Explain how each piece of evidence leads to the prohibition. Umar's letter shows disapproval even for a Jewish woman – a type of Kitabiyya. Ata's restriction narrows the Quranic permission, meaning that only original descendents of Israel qualify. Thus, Majus and idolaters, who have no scripture, are clearly excluded.
The Quranic verse 'wa al-muhsanat min alladhina utu al-kitab' is restricted by the athar.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (difference of opinion) on the scope of Ahl al-Kitab
Observe the disagreement: some consider all Christians (including Arab Christians) as People of the Book and thus permissible to marry. The text sides with the view that Arab Christians are not true Ahl al-Kitab, citing Ata and reports from Umar and Ali.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the early Muslim community; the Hanafi school follows the stricter view here.
5
Understand the Hanafi tarjih (preferred view)
The Hanafi position, as presented, is that only original Kitabiyyat (Jewish/Christian women from the Children of Israel) are permitted, while Majus, idolaters, and even Arab Christians are prohibited. The mufta bihi ruling today is that marriage to a Magian or idolatrous woman is absolutely haram.
This ruling is considered zahir al-riwayah and is agreed upon by the Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز تزويج المجوسيات ولا الوثنيات.
سمعت أبا وائل يقول تزوج حذيفة يهودية فكتب اليه عمر ان يفارقها فقال انى اخشى ان تدعوا المسلمات وتنكحوا المومسات.
قال عطاء ليس نصارى العرب باهل الكتاب انما اهل الكتاب بنو اسرائيل والذين جائتهم التوراة والانجيل فاما من دخل فيهم من الناس فليسوا منهم قال الشيخ وقدروينا عن عمر وعلي في نصارى العرب بمعنى هذا وانه لا توكل ذبائحهم.
قال كتب اليه عمر بن الخطاب ان المسلم ينكح النصرانية ولا ينكح النصراني المسلمة.
سمع جابر بن عبد الله ... ونساءهم لنا حل ونساؤنا عليهم حرام.
والمحصنات من الذين اوتو الكتاب من قبلكم.
It is not permissible to marry Magian women nor idolatrous women. I heard Abu Wa'il say: Hudhayfah married a Jewish woman, so Umar wrote to him to separate from her, saying: I fear that you will abandon Muslim women and marry prostitutes. Ata said: The Christians of the Arabs are not People of the Book; the People of the Book are only the Children of Israel and those to whom the Torah and Gospel came. As for those who entered among them from other people, they are not of them. The shaykh said: It has been narrated from Umar and Ali regarding the Christians of the Arabs similarly, and that their slaughtered animals are not to be eaten. Umar ibn al-Khattab wrote: A Muslim man may marry a Christian woman, but a Christian man may not marry a Muslim woman. Jabir ibn Abdullah heard ... their women are lawful for us, and our women are forbidden to them. And [He said] 'chaste women from those who were given the Book before you.'
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage begins with a clear ruling: it is not permissible (la yajuz) to marry Magian women (al-majusiyat) or idolatrous women (al-wathaniyat). The author then provides several proofs. First, an athar from Umar to Hudhayfah who married a Jewish woman, illustrating that even with People of the Book, there is caution. Second, a statement from Ata that Arab Christians are not true People of the Book—only the Children of Israel are, implying that those considered Christians today may not qualify. Third, a report from Umar ibn al-Khattab confirming that Muslim men may marry Christian women but not vice versa. Fourth, Jabir ibn Abdullah affirms that Muslim women are forbidden to non-Muslim men. Finally, a reference to the Quranic verse permitting marriage to chaste women from the People of the Book is interpreted as restricted to those who are genuinely from the original People of the Book. The Hanafi position is that Magians are treated like polytheists due to their fire worship, hence marriage to them is absolutely prohibited. The ruling is based on the principle that marriage to non-Muslims is only allowed for kitabiyyat (Jewish/Christian women) under specific conditions, and even then it is discouraged by many Hanafi scholars as per this text.

Key Terms
مجوسيات (majusiyat): Women who follow the Magian religion, i.e., fire-worshippers.
وثنيات (wathaniyyat): Women who worship idols.
أهل الكتاب (ahl al-kitab): People who possess a revealed scripture, specifically Jews and Christians of the original lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on marrying a Magian woman?
A) It is permissible if she converts.
B) It is disliked but valid.
C) It is not permissible at all.
D) It depends on her status as a kitabiyya.

Key Takeaway
Marriage to Magian and idolatrous women is absolutely haram; only genuine Kitabiyyat (original People of the Book) are permissible, and even then under strict conditions.

Marriage to Sabian Women: Conditional Permissibility
States ruling with condition, proving from hadith and Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marriage to Sabian women and identify the condition that distinguishes permissible from impermissible.

Core Idea
Marriage to Sabian women is permissible only if they have a prophet and scripture; otherwise they are polytheists.

Sabians are an ambiguous religious group. This passage clarifies that not all Sabians are alike—their status depends on whether they follow a revealed religion. Understanding this nuance is crucial for correctly applying the rules of marriage to non-Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Marriage to Sabian women. What is the hukm? It is mubah (permissible) conditionally.
The condition is explicitly stated: believing in a prophet and having a book.
2
Locate the dalil
What proofs does the author cite? A hadith about the Magians of Hajar, Quran 2:221, and an athar from Hasan ibn Zayd.
Each proof is used to support a different aspect of the ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each dalil prove the ruling? The hadith prohibits marrying Magian women, who have no scripture, analogically applying to scripture-less Sabians. The Quran absolutely prohibits polytheists. The athar shows that superficial monotheistic practices are insufficient.
The athar demonstrates that even if Sabians appear monotheistic (praying toward qibla, giving khums), they are not Ahl al-Kitab if their actual belief is angel-worship.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i, Maliki) generally do not consider Sabians as Ahl al-Kitab at all.
The dispute revolves around the definition of Ahl al-Kitab – whether it extends beyond Jews and Christians.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the school. The evidence of differentiation between Sabian groups is considered strong.
The Hanafi school relies on the principle that any group with a divine prophet and book can be treated as Ahl al-Kitab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز تزويج الصابيات ان كانوا يؤمنون بنبي ويقرون بكتاب وان كانوا يعبدون الكواكب ولا كتاب لهم لم تجز مناكحتهم.
عن الحسن بن محمد بن علي قال كتب رسول الله الى مجوس هجر يدعوهم الى الاسلام فمن اسلم قبل منه الحق ومن ابى كتب عليه الجزية ولا توكل لهم ذبيحة ولا تنكح منهم امرأة.
ولا تنكحوا المشركات حتى يؤمن ولامة مؤمنة خير من مشركة ولو اعجبتكم ولا تنكحوا المشركين حتى يؤمنوا ولعبد مؤمن خير من مشرك ولو اعجبكم اولئك يدعون الى النار والله يدعوا الى الجنة والمغفرة باذنه.
انبأنا الحسن بن زيد ان الصابئين يصلون الى القبلة ويعطون الخمس قال فاراد ان يضع عنهم الجزية قال فاخبر بعد انهم يعبدون الملائكة.
It is permissible to marry Sabian women if they believe in a prophet and acknowledge a book. But if they worship the stars and have no book, their marriage is not permissible. From al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Ali: The Messenger of God wrote to the Magians of Hajar, calling them to Islam: whoever accepts Islam, accept his right; whoever refuses, impose jizya upon him, and do not eat their slaughtered animals, and do not marry a woman from them. 'And do not marry polytheist women until they believe; a believing slave woman is better than a polytheist woman even if she pleases you. And do not marry polytheist men until they believe; a believing slave man is better than a polytheist man even if he pleases you. Those invite to the Fire, while God invites to Paradise and forgiveness by His permission.' al-Hasan ibn Zayd informed us that the Sabians pray toward the qibla and give khums; he intended to remove jizya from them, but then he was informed that they worship angels.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of marrying Sabian women. The ruling is conditional: if they believe in a prophet and possess a book, marriage is permissible; if they worship stars and have no book, it is not. The author then brings proofs. First, a hadith about Majus of Hajar, which also includes prohibition of marrying their women, but here it is used to contrast with Sabians. Second, the Quranic verse (2:221) prohibiting marriage to polytheists unless they believe. This verse is applied to Sabians who are star-worshippers—they are polytheists, so marriage is forbidden. Third, an athar about Sabians who initially appeared to follow a religion (praying toward qibla, giving khums), but when found to worship angels, they are not treated as Ahl al-Kitab. The Hanafi position is that Sabians are not automatically Ahl al-Kitab; their status depends on whether they have an authentic prophet and scripture. The key distinction is that if they have a recognized prophet and book, they are like Ahl al-Kitab; otherwise, they are mushrikun. This ruling is rooted in the principle that marriage to non-Muslims is only allowed for Kitabiyyat, and that Kitabiyyat must be from those who follow an original revelation.

Key Terms
صابيات (sabiyat): Women belonging to the Sabian religion, which is ambiguous; some groups believe in a prophet and book, others worship stars.
مشركات (mushrikat): Polytheist women, those who associate partners with God.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following Sabian women is permissible to marry?
A) One who worships the stars.
B) One who believes in a prophet and a book.
C) One who gives khums.
D) One who prays toward the qibla.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of marrying a Sabian woman hinges on whether she belongs to a group that has a recognized prophet and scripture; otherwise she is treated as a polytheist.

Marriage with Sabian Women: Condition of Belief in a Prophet and Scripture
Ruling with proofs on conditional marriage to Sabian women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying Sabian women and identify the condition that determines permissibility.

Core Idea
Marrying a Sabian woman is only permissible if she believes in a prophet and has a scripture — otherwise she is a polytheist.

This passage addresses a nuanced fiqh issue: the permissibility of marrying women from the Sabian community. The Hanafi school distinguishes between Sabians who follow a prophet and have a divine scripture, treating them akin to People of the Book, and those who worship stars without scripture, who are treated as polytheists. The passage provides proof from hadith and Quran to support the conditional ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Marriage to Sabian women. Determine the hukm: it is conditional permissibility (mubah) or prohibition (haram) based on their beliefs.
The ruling is not absolute; it depends on a condition.
2
Locate the dalil
What proofs are cited? A hadith mursal about Magians (forbidding marriage) and Quranic verse 2:221 (forbidding marriage to polytheists).
The Magian hadith is used to exclude those without scripture.
3
Analyze the condition
What distinguishes a permissible Sabian from an impermissible one? The text states: 'if they believe in a prophet and acknowledge a scripture.'
This condition is essential; without it, they fall under the general prohibition for polytheists.
4
Understand the principle
The Hanafi principle: ahl al-kitab are those with a revealed book and belief in a prophet; others are mushrikun. Sabians with these attributes are treated as ahl al-kitab.
This principle resolves the conflicting reports about Sabians.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز تزويج الصابيات ان كانوا يؤمنون بنبي ويقرون بكتاب وان كانوا يعبدون الكواكب ولا كتاب لهم لم تجز مناكحتهم.
حدیث مرسل میں مجوسی سے نکاح کرنے سے منع فرمایا ہے ۔ عن الحسن بن مـحـمـد بـن عـلـى قال كتب رسول الله الى جوس هجريدعوهم الى الاسلام فمن اسلم قبل منه الحق ومن ابى كتب عليه الجزية ولا توكل لهم ذبيحة ولا تنكح منهم امرأة (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، اخذ الجزية من المجوس ج سادس ص۰ ۷ نمبر ۱۰۰۲۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مجوسیہ عورت سے نکاح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے (۲) اور بت پرست اور کافر کے لئے تو آیت موجود ہے۔ ولا تنكحوا المشركات حتى يؤمن ولامة مؤمنة خير من مشركة ولو اعجبتكم ولا تنكحوا المشركين حتى يؤمنوا ولعبد مؤمن خير من مشرك ولو اعجبكم اولئك يدعون الى النار والله يدعوا الى الجنة والمغفرة باذنه (ب) ( آیت ۲۲۱ سورۃ البقر (۲) اس آیت میں مشرک مرد اور مشرک عورتوں سے نکاح کرنا حرام قرار دیا ہے۔ اور یہ بھی حکمت بیان کی ہے وہ جہنم کی طرف بلانے والے ہیں۔ اس لئے مشرکہ عورت اور بہت برست عورت یا مرد سے نکاح کرنا حرام ہوگا۔
و اس میں یہ بھی دیکھا جائے گا کہ نصرانیہ اور یہودیہ عورت جہنم کی طرف بلانے والی ہو تو ان سے بھی نکاح کرنا اچھا نہیں ہو گا۔ [۱۷۵۱) (۲۶) اور جائز ہے صابیہ عورتوں سے نکاح کرنا اگر وہ ایمان رکھتی ہوں کسی نبی پر اور پڑھتی ہوں کتاب، اور اگر عبادت کرتی ہوں ستاروں کی اور ان کے پاس کتاب نہ ہو تو ان سے نکاح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ اہل کتاب کی طرح کسی قوم کے پاس کوئی بھی آسمانی کتاب ہو اور کسی نبی پر ایمان رکھتی ہو تب تو وہ اہل کتاب کے درجے میں ہیں۔ اور ان کی عورتوں سے نکاح کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ اور اگر ان کے پاس کتاب نہ ہو اور نہ کسی نبی پر ایمان رکھتی ہوں تو وہ بت پرست ہیں ان سے نکاح کرنا جائز نہیں ہوگا، چنانچہ صابیات کے بارے میں متضاد خبریں اثر میں ہیں۔ اس لئے ان کے بارے میں یہ قاعدہ بیان کر دیا۔ انبـأنـا الحسن بني زيد ان الصابئين يصلون الى القبلة ويعطون الخمس قال فاراد ان يضع عنهم الجزية قال فاخبر بعد انهم يعبدون الملائكة (ج) (سنن للبیہقی ، باب من دان دینہ الیهو دوالنصارى من الصائمين والسامرة ج سابع میں ۲۸۱ نمبر ۱۳۹۹۰) اس اثر میں پہلے خبر دی گئی کہ صابی قبلہ کی طرف نماز پڑھتے ہیں اور شمس دیتے ہیں تو فرمایا کہ وہ اہل کتاب کی طرح ہیں۔ اس لئے ان سے جزیہ ہٹا دیا جائے۔ بعد میں پتہ چلا کہ وہ فرشتوں کی پوجا کرتے ہیں تو ان سے جزیہ نہیں ہٹایا۔ کیونکہ وہ اہل کتاب کی حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے ہجر کے مجوس کو لکھا ، ان کو اسلام کی دعوت دی ۔ ہیں جو اسلام لائے اس سے حق قبول کر لیا گیا۔ اور جس نے انکار کیا اس پر جزیہ لازم کیا۔ اور یہ کہ ان کا ذبیحہ نہ کھایا جائے اور نہ ان کی عورتوں سے نکاح کیا جائے (ب) مشرکہ عورتوں سے نکاح نہ کرو جب تک کہ ایمان نہ لائے۔ اور مؤمن باندی زیادہ بہتر ہے مشرکہ سے چاہے تم کو اچھی کیوں نہ لگے۔ اور مشرک مرد سے نکاح نہ کرو جب تک کہ ایمان نہ لائیں۔ اور مؤمن غلام زیادہ بہتر ہے مشرک سے چاہے تم کو اچھے کیوں نہ لگے۔ یہ آگ کی طرف بلاتا ہے اور اللہ جنت اور مغفرت کی طرف بلاتے ہیں اپنے حکم سے (ج) حسن بن زیاد نے خبر دی کہ صائین قبلہ کی طرف نماز پڑھتے ہیں اور شمس دیتے ہیں۔ فرمایا کہ اس سے جزیہ ختم کرنے کا ارادہ کر لیا۔ پھر خبر دی کہ وہ فرشتوں کی عبادت کرتے ہیں۔
It is permissible to marry Sabian women if they believe in a prophet and acknowledge a scripture. But if they worship the stars and have no scripture, then marrying them is not permissible. A hadith mursal forbids marrying a Magian woman. From al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Ali: The Messenger of Allah wrote to the Magians of Hajar, inviting them to Islam. Whoever accepted Islam, his right was accepted. Whoever refused, jizya was imposed on him, and their slaughtered meat is not to be eaten, and no woman from them is to be married. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on taking jizya from Magians, vol. 6, p. 7, no. 10028) From this hadith, it is understood that marrying a Magian woman is not permissible. And for idol worshipers and disbelievers, there is the verse: 'And do not marry polytheistic women until they believe. And a believing slave woman is better than a polytheistic woman, even if she pleases you. And do not marry polytheistic men until they believe. And a believing slave is better than a polytheistic man, even if he pleases you. Those invite to the Fire, but Allah invites to Paradise and forgiveness by His permission.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:221) This verse declares marriage with polytheistic men and women forbidden. It also explains the wisdom: they invite to Hellfire. Therefore, marrying a polytheistic woman or man is forbidden. And in this, it will also be considered that if a Christian or Jewish woman is one who invites to Hellfire, then marrying them is also not good. [1751] (26) And it is permissible to marry Sabian women if they believe in a prophet and recite a scripture. And if they worship the stars and have no scripture, then marrying them is not permissible. This ruling is based on the principle that if a people, like the People of the Book, possess any heavenly scripture and believe in a prophet, then they are in the rank of the People of the Book, and marrying their women is permissible. And if they have no scripture and do not believe in a prophet, then they are idol worshippers, and marrying them is not permissible. Thus, there are contradictory reports about the Sabians in the traditions. Therefore, this rule has been stated. Al-Hasan ibn Zaid informed us that the Sabians pray towards the qibla and give khums. He said, 'He wanted to remove jizya from them.' Then he was informed later that they worship angels. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on those who follow the religion of Jews and Christians among the Sabians and Samaritans, vol. 7, p. 281, no. 13990) In this report, first it was reported that the Sabians pray towards the qibla and give khums, so he said that they are like the People of the Book. Therefore, jizya should be removed from them. Later, it was discovered that they worship angels, so jizya was not removed from them. Footnote (a): He wrote to the Magians of Hajar, inviting them to Islam. Those who accepted Islam had their rights accepted. Those who refused had jizya imposed. And their slaughtered meat is not to be eaten, nor are their women to be married. (b) 'Do not marry polytheistic women until they believe...' (c) Al-Hasan ibn Zaid reported that the Sabians pray towards the qibla and give khums. He said, 'He intended to remove jizya from them.' Then he was informed that they worship angels.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs on marrying Sabian women. The author states the general rule: if Sabians believe in a prophet and have a scripture, they are considered akin to the People of the Book, and marrying them is permissible. If they worship stars and have no scripture, they are polytheists and marriage is forbidden. The proof includes a hadith about Magians, who are treated as a distinct category—they are allowed to give jizya but their women are not to be married. Then the Quranic verse (2:221) is cited, which prohibits marriage with polytheists (mushrikun). The author then applies this to Sabians: there are conflicting reports about them. One report indicates they pray to the qibla and give khums, suggesting they are like People of the Book, but another says they worship angels, making them polytheists. Hence, the ruling is conditional: only those Sabians who follow a prophet and have a scripture are permissible to marry. The footnote clarifies the hadith about Magians and the Quranic verse.

Key Terms
صابيات (sābiyāt): Sabian women; a religious group whose status is debated—some follow a prophet and scripture, others worship stars.
مجوس (majūs): Magians or Zoroastrians; they are given jizya but their women cannot be married and their meat cannot be eaten.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition is it permissible for a Muslim man to marry a Sabian woman according to the Hanafi school?
A) If she worships the stars
B) If she believes in a prophet and has a scripture
C) If she is from the Magians
D) If she is a polytheist

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of marrying a Sabian woman hinges on her belief in a prophet and possession of a divine scripture.
